  \item Explain decoherence as environment-induced suppression of off-diagonal density matrix elements.
  \item Construct two-electron spin states (singlet and triplet) and explain their exchange origin.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Dual-track content:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item \textit{Physical/applied track:} Fermi's golden rule in atomic spectroscopy,
    nuclear decay, and solid-state (electron--phonon scattering); Lindblad equation in
    quantum optics (spontaneous emission) and quantum computing (gate errors);
    decoherence as the bridge between quantum and classical.
  \item \textit{Mathematical/structural track:} Derivation of Fermi's golden rule rigorously;
    Lindblad equation from complete positivity and the GKSL theorem;
    pointer states as preferred bases selected by the environment.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``open systems'' as a leaky box --- energy and information escaping to the environment;
radioactive decay as Fermi's golden rule in action.
Beg.\ UG: compute $\Gamma_{i\to f}$ for a constant perturbation;
simple Lindblad evolution (amplitude damping) for a qubit.
Adv.\ UG: derive Fermi's golden rule from TDPT; verify Lindblad equation
preserves $\operatorname{Tr}\hat{\rho}=1$ and positivity; singlet/triplet construction.
MSc: GKSL theorem and complete positivity; Kraus representation;
decoherence in the spin-boson model; Born--Markov approximation.
PhD: Nakajima--Zwanzig projection technique; non-Markovian dynamics;
Floquet--Lindblad equation; entanglement in many-body systems.

\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- compute $\Gamma_{i\to f}$ for an atom in an oscillating field;
simple Lindblad evolution; singlet/triplet state construction and symmetry.
Set~B --- derive Fermi's golden rule; prove Lindblad equation trace-preserving;
exchange interaction from antisymmetry of two-electron wavefunction.
Projects: (simple) decoherence visualiser: off-diagonal decay under Lindblad dephasing;
(complex) Born--Markov derivation of Lindblad equation for a qubit coupled to a harmonic bath.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip
%------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Assessment Strategy}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Module I.3 Assessment Strategy}

\begin{tcolorbox}[highlightbox]
\textbf{Per-Lecture Assessment Bundle} (every lecture):
concept check (10--15~min, 5--8 short conceptual questions);
Problem Set~A (simple, 6--10 computational exercises);
Problem Set~B (complex, 3--6 multi-step derivations and proofs);
mini-project simple (1--3 hours);
mini-project complex (5--10 hours, open-ended);
research questions well-defined (2--4 scoped prompts);
research questions fully open (1--2 frontier-style prompts).
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Course-level grading template:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.5em]
  \item Weekly homework (best 8/10): 40\%
  \item Mid-course synthesis (after L06): 20\%
  \item Project (simple or complex track): 25\%
  \item Final oral/whiteboard exam or take-home: 15\%
\end{itemize}
Mixed cohorts: HS/UG $\to$ simple track; MSc/PhD $\to$ complex track.

%------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Reading Strategy}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Module I.3 Reading Strategy}

\noindent\textbf{Track A --- Core textbooks:}
Sakurai \& Napolitano, \textit{Modern Quantum Mechanics} Ch.~2--5 (dynamics, symmetry, perturbation theory);
Shankar, \textit{Principles of Quantum Mechanics} (perturbation theory and example systems).

\noindent\textbf{Track B --- Support:}
Messiah, \textit{Quantum Mechanics} (density matrix, open systems);
Cohen-Tannoudji, Diu \& Lalo\"e (time-dependent PT, Fermi's golden rule).

\noindent\textbf{Track C --- Specialised:}
Lindblad (1976) original paper on master equations (MSc/PhD);
Born \& Oppenheimer (1927) original paper.

\newpage

%=============================================================
\subsection{Module I.4 --- Paradigm Physical Systems}
\label{sec:mod-I4}
%=============================================================

\begin{tcolorbox}[seriesbox]
  \textbf{Series I / Module~I.4} \quad
  \textit{Paradigm Physical Systems}\\[4pt]
  \textbf{Duration:} 12 lectures $\times$ 90 minutes (Lectures~L01--L12).
  Each lecture develops one canonical quantum system in full depth, applying
  the formalism of Modules~I.1--I.3. Lectures are self-contained and may be
  taught in any order after Module~I.3~L10.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\subsubsection*{Module Overview}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Module I.4 Overview}
{\footnotesize
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lp{4.2cm}p{6.8cm}@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Lec.} & \textbf{Title} & \textbf{Key Concepts}\\
\midrule
L01 & Free Particle \& Particle in a Box & Plane waves; wave packets; quantisation; DOS in 1/2/3D\\
L02 & Simple Bloch Electron & Bloch's theorem; BZ; nearly-free electron gap; tight-binding\\
L03 & Harmonic Oscillator & Ladder operators; coherent states; anharmonic PT\\
L04 & Rabi Model \& Two-Level Systems & Jaynes--Cummings; Rabi oscillations; RWA; $\pi$-pulses\\
L05 & Minimal Coupling \& Landau Levels & $(\hat{\mathbf{p}}-e\mathbf{A})^2/2m$; gauge invariance; Landau levels\\
L06 & Zeeman Effect & Normal and anomalous; Paschen--Back; Breit--Rabi\\
\midrule
L07 & Stark Effect & Linear and quadratic; parabolic coordinates; polarisability\\
L08 & Spin--Orbit \& Fine Structure & Thomas precession; $\hat{\mathbf{L}}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{S}}$; $E_{nj}^{\rm FS}$\\
L09 & Hydrogen Atom & Coulomb potential; radial equation; $\psi_{nlm}$; $SO(4)$ symmetry\\
L10 & Scattering from a Potential Barrier & Step potential; transmission; tunnelling; $T$ and $R$ coefficients\\
L11 & Scattering from a Potential Well & Finite square well; bound states; resonance transmission\\
L12 & Delta-Function Potential \& WKB & $\delta(x)$ bound state; WKB quantisation; tunnelling rate\\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
}

\subsubsection*{Lecture-by-Lecture Syllabi}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Module I.4 Lecture Syllabi}

% ------ L01 -----------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~I.4 / L01: Free Particle and Particle in a Box}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Free particle: $\hat{H}=\hat{p}^2/2m$;
plane-wave solutions $\psi_k(x)=e^{ikx}/\sqrt{L}$ (periodic BC) or $e^{ikx}/\sqrt{2\pi}$ (continuum);
energy $E_k=\hbar^2k^2/2m$; continuum of states; momentum eigenstates;
(20--45~min) Wave packets: $\psi(x,t)=\int \tilde\phi(k)e^{ikx-i\omega_k t}dk/\sqrt{2\pi}$;
group velocity $v_g=d\omega/dk|_{k_0}=\hbar k_0/m$; phase velocity $v_p=\omega/k=\hbar k/2m$;
dispersion broadening; Gaussian wave packet: exact solution; $\Delta x\,\Delta p=\hbar/2$ at $t=0$,
grows as $t\to\infty$;
(45--70~min) Infinite square well: $V=0$ for $0<x<L$, $\infty$ otherwise;
solutions $\psi_n=\sqrt{2/L}\sin(n\pi x/L)$; energies $E_n=n^2\pi^2\hbar^2/2mL^2$;
zero-point energy $E_1>0$; parity; orthonormality; completeness; expectation values;
(70--90~min) 3D box; degeneracy; density of states in 1D, 2D, 3D
$g(E)=(L/\pi\hbar)\sqrt{m/2E}$ in 1D, $g(E)=mL^2/\pi\hbar^2$ in 2D (constant!),
$g(E)=V(2m)^{3/2}E^{1/2}/2\pi^2\hbar^3$ in 3D; van Hove singularities.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Solve the free-particle and infinite-square-well Schr\"odinger equations.
  \item Construct and propagate a Gaussian wave packet; compute group and phase velocities.
  \item Derive the density of states in 1D, 2D, and 3D.
  \item Interpret zero-point energy physically and compute $\langle x\rangle,\langle p\rangle,\langle E\rangle$.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Dual-track content:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item \textit{Physical track:} Particle in a box as the prototype for all confined quantum systems;
    zero-point energy as the origin of atomic stability; wave packet spreading as a measurable quantum effect.
  \item \textit{Mathematical track:} Fourier analysis as change of basis; density of states from counting
    states in $k$-space; van Hove singularities from $\nabla_k E=0$.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``the particle cannot be at rest inside the box'' --- zero-point energy and quantum confinement.
Beg.\ UG: $\psi_n$, $E_n$, $\langle x\rangle$, $\langle p\rangle$; Gaussian wave packet; group velocity.
Adv.\ UG: 3D box; density of states; van Hove singularities; wave-packet dispersion derivation.
MSc: Airy functions for a linear potential; finite square well; transfer matrix method.
PhD: self-adjoint extensions of $\hat{p}$ on $[0,L]$; particle in a box in curved space;
resonances and quasi-bound states (complex scaling).

\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- $E_n$, $\psi_n$, $\langle x\rangle$, $\Delta x\,\Delta p$ for 1D box; group velocity of Gaussian packet.
Set~B --- density of states in 2D and 3D; wave-packet spreading: $\Delta x(t)$ for Gaussian.
Projects: (simple) Gaussian wave packet animation: $|\psi(x,t)|^2$ spreading and oscillation;
(complex) van Hove singularities in 1D and 3D DOS: logarithmic vs.\ power-law divergence.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

% ------ L02 -----------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~I.4 / L02: The Simple Bloch Electron}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Periodic potential $V(x+a)=V(x)$; translation operator
$\hat{T}_a\ket{x}=\ket{x+a}$; $[\hat{H},\hat{T}_a]=0$ when $V$ is periodic;
simultaneous eigenstates;
(20--45~min) Bloch's theorem: $\psi_{nk}(x)=e^{ikx}u_{nk}(x)$ with $u_{nk}(x+a)=u_{nk}(x)$;
crystal momentum $\hbar k$; first Brillouin zone $k\in(-\pi/a,\pi/a]$;
band index $n$; reduced, extended, and repeated zone schemes;
(45--65~min) Nearly-free electron model: treat $V$ as a small perturbation;
energy near zone boundary $k=\pm\pi/a$ splits into two bands;
band gap $2|V_G|$ at the zone boundary ($V_G$ = Fourier component of $V$);
effective mass $m^*=(d^2E/dk^2)^{-1}\hbar^2$; heavy and light bands;
(65--90~min) Tight-binding model (1D, one orbital per site):
$E(k)=\varepsilon_0-2t\cos(ka)$; bandwidth $4t$; effective mass at $k=0$;
connection to hopping integrals; Wannier functions;
metals, insulators, and semiconductors from band filling.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item State and derive Bloch's theorem from translation symmetry.
  \item Identify crystal momentum, the Brillouin zone, and band gaps.
  \item Compute band gaps from the nearly-free electron model.
  \item Solve the 1D tight-binding model and extract the effective mass.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Dual-track content:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item \textit{Physical/materials track:} Connection to real materials: Si, GaAs, graphene;
    band filling and electrical conductivity; effective mass in semiconductor devices;
    Wannier functions as chemically intuitive localised orbitals.
  \item \textit{Mathematical track:} Bloch's theorem from the representation theory of $\mathbb{Z}$;
    Floquet--Bloch analogy (time vs.\ space periodicity); Wannier--Kohn theorem;
    Berry phase of Bloch bands (preview of topology).
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``a periodic lattice turns continuous energy into discrete bands'' --- the origin of conductors and insulators.
Beg.\ UG: Bloch's theorem; BZ; nearly-free electron gap; tight-binding $E(k)$.
Adv.\ UG: derivation of Bloch from $[\hat{H},\hat{T}_a]=0$; effective mass derivation; Wannier functions.
MSc: Peierls instability; Su--Schrieffer--Heeger model; Berry phase of a band; Zak phase.
PhD: Wannier functions and maximally localised orbitals; topological invariants (Chern number); non-Abelian Berry connection.

\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- Bloch wave for a cosine potential; BZ boundaries; tight-binding $E(k)$ and bandwidth.
Set~B --- derive Bloch's theorem; nearly-free electron gap $2|V_G|$; effective mass at $k=0$.
Projects: (simple) tight-binding band structure for 1D, 2D square, and graphene lattices;
(complex) Berry phase (Zak phase) for a 1D SSH model: topological vs.\ trivial phase.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

% ------ L03 -----------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~I.4 / L03: The Harmonic Oscillator}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Hamiltonian $\hat{H}=\hat{p}^2/2m+m\omega^2\hat{x}^2/2$;
algebraic approach: ladder operators $\hat{a}=\sqrt{m\omega/2\hbar}(\hat{x}+i\hat{p}/m\omega)$,
$\hat{a}^\dagger=\sqrt{m\omega/2\hbar}(\hat{x}-i\hat{p}/m\omega)$;
$[\hat{a},\hat{a}^\dagger]=1$; $\hat{H}=\hbar\omega(\hat{a}^\dagger\hat{a}+\tfrac{1}{2})$;
(20--45~min) Spectrum: $E_n=(n+\tfrac{1}{2})\hbar\omega$; number states $\ket{n}$;
$\hat{a}\ket{n}=\sqrt{n}\ket{n-1}$, $\hat{a}^\dagger\ket{n}=\sqrt{n+1}\ket{n+1}$;
matrix elements $\bra{m}\hat{x}\ket{n}=\sqrt{\hbar/2m\omega}(\sqrt{n}\delta_{m,n-1}+\sqrt{n+1}\delta_{m,n+1})$;
position wavefunctions via $\hat{a}\ket{0}=0$: Hermite polynomials;
(45--65~min) Coherent states: $\hat{a}\ket{\alpha}=\alpha\ket{\alpha}$;
$\ket{\alpha}=e^{-|\alpha|^2/2}\sum_n\alpha^n\ket{n}/\sqrt{n!}$; over-completeness;
Poisson photon number distribution; minimum uncertainty; classical-like oscillation $\langle\hat{x}\rangle=x_{\rm cl}(t)$;
(65--90~min) Anharmonic oscillator: $\hat{V}'=\lambda\hat{x}^3+\mu\hat{x}^4$;
first- and second-order energy corrections via ladder operators; selection rules $\Delta n=\pm1,\pm2,\pm3$;
Morse potential as a realistic anharmonic oscillator; vibrational spectroscopy.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Derive the HO spectrum algebraically using ladder operators.
  \item Compute matrix elements of $\hat{x}$ and $\hat{p}$ in the number basis.
  \item Construct and interpret coherent states as minimum-uncertainty classical-like states.
  \item Apply first-order PT to compute anharmonic energy corrections.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Dual-track content:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item \textit{Physical track:} HO as the universal model near a potential minimum;
    zero-point energy in He (stays liquid at atmospheric pressure);
    photons as HO quanta; phonons in solids; vibrational spectra of diatomic molecules.
  \item \textit{Mathematical track:} Ladder operator algebra as $\mathfrak{su}(1,1)$ or Heisenberg--Weyl;
    coherent states as displaced vacuum; Glauber--Sudarshan $P$-representation;
    generating function for Hermite polynomials.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: HO as the ``building block of physics'' --- springs, pendula, photons, phonons.
Beg.\ UG: spectrum; ladder operators; zero-point energy; Hermite polynomials.
Adv.\ UG: matrix elements; coherent states; Poisson distribution; anharmonic PT.
MSc: squeezed states; Wigner function; $P$-function; Husimi $Q$-function.
PhD: quantisation of EM field from HO; non-linear optics from anharmonicity;
exactly solvable anharmonic potentials (Morse, P\"oschl--Teller).

\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- $E_n$, $\bra{m}\hat{x}^2\ket{n}$, $\langle\hat{x}\rangle(t)$ for coherent state;
first-order anharmonic correction to $E_n$ for $\lambda\hat{x}^4$.
Set~B --- derive $\ket{n}=(\hat{a}^\dagger)^n\ket{0}/\sqrt{n!}$; prove coherent state over-completeness;
second-order anharmonic for $\lambda\hat{x}^3$.
Projects: (simple) Wigner function of $\ket{n}$, $\ket{\alpha}$, and superposition states;
(complex) Morse potential: exact vs.\ perturbative vibrational levels for HCl.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

% ------ L04 -----------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~I.4 / L04: Rabi Model and Two-Level Systems}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Two-level system (TLS) Hamiltonian:
$\hat{H}_0=\tfrac{\hbar\omega_0}{2}\hat\sigma_z$; energy splitting $\hbar\omega_0$;
Bloch sphere representation; general state $\ket{\psi}=\cos(\theta/2)\ket{\uparrow}+e^{i\phi}\sin(\theta/2)\ket{\downarrow}$;
(20--45~min) Driven TLS: oscillating field $\hat{H}'=-d E_0\cos(\omega t)\hat\sigma_x$;
transformation to rotating frame; rotating wave approximation (RWA):
drop counter-rotating term; resonance condition $\omega=\omega_0$;
Rabi Hamiltonian in rotating frame: $\hat{H}_{\rm rot}=\tfrac{\hbar\Delta}{2}\hat\sigma_z+\tfrac{\hbar\Omega_R}{2}\hat\sigma_x$
with detuning $\Delta=\omega-\omega_0$ and Rabi frequency $\Omega_R=dE_0/\hbar$;
(45--65~min) Exact Rabi solution: generalised Rabi frequency $\tilde\Omega=\sqrt{\Delta^2+\Omega_R^2}$;
population inversion $P_{\uparrow}(t)=(\Omega_R/\tilde\Omega)^2\sin^2(\tilde\Omega t/2)$;
$\pi$-pulse ($\Omega_R t=\pi$) and $\pi/2$-pulse for complete inversion/superposition;
(65--90~min) Jaynes--Cummings model: full quantum treatment of TLS + single EM mode;
$\hat{H}_{\rm JC}=\hbar\omega_c\hat{a}^\dagger\hat{a}+\tfrac{\hbar\omega_0}{2}\hat\sigma_z+\hbar g(\hat{a}\hat\sigma_++\hat{a}^\dagger\hat\sigma_-)$;
dressed states; collapse and revival of Rabi oscillations; photon number states.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Derive the rotating frame Hamiltonian and apply the RWA.
  \item Solve the Rabi problem exactly for arbitrary detuning.
  \item Compute the population inversion and identify $\pi$- and $\pi/2$-pulses.
  \item Write the Jaynes--Cummings Hamiltonian and identify dressed states.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Dual-track content:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item \textit{Physical/applications track:} NMR and MRI as Rabi oscillations of nuclear spins;
    qubit gates in quantum computing as $\pi$/$\pi/2$ pulses; atom trapping and cooling;
    dressed-state picture for AC Stark shift.
  \item \textit{Mathematical track:} $SU(2)$ structure of TLS; Bloch equation of motion;
    Jaynes--Cummings exact diagonalisation in $\{|n,\uparrow\rangle,|n+1,\downarrow\rangle\}$ subspace.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``a laser pulse can flip a quantum spin --- that's the basis of NMR and quantum computers.''
Beg.\ UG: driven TLS; resonance; Rabi oscillations; $\pi$-pulse.
Adv.\ UG: RWA derivation; off-resonance Rabi; Bloch--Siegert shift.
MSc: Jaynes--Cummings dressed states; collapse and revival; vacuum Rabi splitting.
PhD: beyond RWA (Rabi model vs.\ JC); ultra-strong coupling; quantum phase transition in Rabi model.

\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- Rabi frequency for given field strength; $\pi$-pulse time; on-resonance inversion.
Set~B --- derive rotating frame Hamiltonian; off-resonance Rabi: $P_{\uparrow}(t)$ for $\Delta=\Omega_R$.
Projects: (simple) Bloch sphere trajectory under $\pi/2$--wait--$\pi/2$ (Ramsey spectroscopy);
(complex) Jaynes--Cummings: collapse and revival of Rabi oscillations for Fock and coherent states.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

% ------ L05 -----------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~I.4 / L05: Minimal Coupling Hamiltonian and Landau Levels}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Classical mechanics in EM fields: Lorentz force;
canonical momentum $\mathbf{p}_{\rm can}=m\mathbf{v}+e\mathbf{A}$;
Hamiltonian $H=(\mathbf{p}_{\rm can}-e\mathbf{A})^2/2m+e\phi$;
quantisation: $\hat{H}=(\hat{\mathbf{p}}-e\mathbf{A})^2/2m+e\phi$;
gauge invariance: $\mathbf{A}\to\mathbf{A}+\nabla\chi$, $\psi\to e^{ie\chi/\hbar}\psi$;
(20--45~min) Uniform magnetic field $\mathbf{B}=B\hat{z}$;
symmetric gauge $\mathbf{A}=\tfrac{B}{2}(-y,x,0)$ or Landau gauge $\mathbf{A}=(0,Bx,0)$;
Landau gauge: $\hat{H}=\tfrac{1}{2m}[\hat{p}_x^2+(\hat{p}_y-eBx)^2]$;
reduce to HO: $\hat{H}=\hat{p}_x^2/2m+\tfrac{m\omega_c^2}{2}(x-x_0)^2$
with cyclotron frequency $\omega_c=eB/m$ and guiding centre $x_0=\hbar k_y/m\omega_c$;
(45--65~min) Landau levels: $E_n=(n+\tfrac{1}{2})\hbar\omega_c$; massive degeneracy;
density of states: one state per area $2\pi l_B^2$ where $l_B=\sqrt{\hbar/eB}$ (magnetic length);
filling factor $\nu=N_e/(eBA/h)$; quantum Hall effect preview;
(65--90~min) Aharonov--Bohm effect: $\oint\mathbf{A}\cdot d\mathbf{l}=\Phi$ (enclosed flux);
phase $e\Phi/\hbar$; physical despite $\mathbf{B}=0$ in accessible region;
experimental observation via electron interferometry; connection to Berry phase.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Write the minimal coupling Hamiltonian and explain gauge invariance.
  \item Solve for Landau levels and derive their degeneracy.
  \item Define the magnetic length and filling factor.
  \item Explain the Aharonov--Bohm effect and its topological character.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Dual-track content:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item \textit{Physical track:} Landau levels as the quantum basis for the quantum Hall effect;
    cyclotron resonance in semiconductors; Shubnikov--de Haas oscillations;
    Aharonov--Bohm interference in mesoscopic rings.
  \item \textit{Mathematical track:} Gauge theory as $U(1)$ fibre bundle; minimal coupling as
    covariant derivative; Aharonov--Bohm as holonomy; magnetic translation group.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``a magnetic field forces electrons to move in circles --- quantised, those circles become Landau levels.''
Beg.\ UG: minimal coupling Hamiltonian; gauge transformation; Landau level spectrum.
Adv.\ UG: gauge derivation; degeneracy; filling factor; Aharonov--Bohm phase.
MSc: magnetic length; QHE overview; Laughlin's gauge argument; de Haas--van Alphen.
PhD: magnetic translation group; Hofstadter butterfly; fractional QHE; composite fermions.

\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- gauge transform $\mathbf{A}\to\mathbf{A}+\nabla\chi$; Landau level $E_n$; cyclotron frequency for electron.
Set~B --- Landau level degeneracy derivation; Aharonov--Bohm phase for a given flux.
Projects: (simple) Landau level DOS vs.\ magnetic field: SdH oscillation preview;
(complex) Aharonov--Bohm interference in a ring: conductance oscillations vs.\ flux.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

% ------ L06 -----------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~I.4 / L06: Zeeman Effect}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Magnetic moment from orbital motion:
$\hat{\boldsymbol\mu}_L=-\tfrac{e}{2m}\hat{\mathbf{L}}=-\mu_B\hat{\mathbf{L}}/\hbar$;
Bohr magneton $\mu_B=e\hbar/2m$;
interaction Hamiltonian $\hat{H}_Z=-\hat{\boldsymbol\mu}\cdot\mathbf{B}$;
(20--45~min) Normal Zeeman effect (spin ignored): $\hat{H}'=\mu_B B\hat{L}_z/\hbar$;
first-order PT: $E^{(1)}_{nlm}=\mu_B m B$; triplet splitting $\Delta E=\mu_B B$;
Lorentz classical model gives the same result; experimental observation in Cd, Mg;
(45--65~min) Anomalous Zeeman effect (spin included):
total magnetic moment $\hat{\boldsymbol\mu}=-\mu_B(\hat{\mathbf{L}}+g_s\hat{\mathbf{S}})/\hbar$ with $g_s\approx2$;
Land\'e $g$-factor from projection: $g_J=1+\tfrac{j(j+1)+s(s+1)-l(l+1)}{2j(j+1)}$;
energy $E^{(1)}_{njm_j}=g_J\mu_B m_j B$; pattern of anomalous Zeeman in Na D-lines;
(65--90~min) Paschen--Back effect: strong field limit where $\mu_B B\gg$ spin--orbit splitting;
good quantum numbers switch from $j,m_j$ to $m_l,m_s$; linear splitting in $m_l+2m_s$;
Breit--Rabi diagram: interpolation between weak and strong field;
applications: laser cooling and trapping (magneto-optical trap); EPR/ESR spectroscopy.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Derive the normal Zeeman splitting from first-order PT.
  \item Compute the Land\'e $g$-factor and explain anomalous Zeeman splitting.
  \item Identify the good quantum numbers in weak and strong field limits.
  \item Describe the Breit--Rabi interpolation and its applications.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Dual-track content:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item \textit{Spectroscopy track:} Normal and anomalous Zeeman patterns; Na D-line splitting;
    astrophysical Zeeman effect (magnetic fields in sunspots and neutron stars);
    magneto-optical trap level structure.
  \item \textit{Theoretical track:} Land\'e $g$-factor from Wigner--Eckart theorem; Breit--Rabi exact solution
    for two-level mixing; $g$-factor anomaly $g_s-2$ from QED (preview).
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``a magnetic field splits spectral lines --- Zeeman used it to discover spin (indirectly).''
Beg.\ UG: normal Zeeman; Land\'e $g_J$; triplet pattern; anomalous Zeeman for Na.
Adv.\ UG: Land\'e $g$-factor derivation from projection; Paschen--Back limit.
MSc: Breit--Rabi exact solution; astrophysical applications; magneto-optical trap.
PhD: $g_s-2$ from QED one-loop; nuclear Zeeman; molecular Zeeman in diamagnetic molecules.

\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- normal Zeeman triplet for Cd; Land\'e $g_J$ for $^2P_{3/2}$; anomalous Zeeman pattern for Na~D.
Set~B --- Land\'e $g_J$ derivation from Wigner--Eckart; Paschen--Back level energies for H $n=2$.
Projects: (simple) Zeeman energy level diagram for H $n=2$ vs.\ field strength (weak$\to$Paschen--Back);
(complex) Breit--Rabi diagram for $^{87}$Rb $F=1,2$ hyperfine states: magneto-optical trap.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

% ------ L07 -----------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~I.4 / L07: Stark Effect}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Electric field perturbation:
$\hat{H}'=-e\mathbf{E}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{r}}=-eE\hat{z}$ (field along $z$);
why first-order vanishes for non-degenerate eigenstates of definite parity:
$\langle nlm|z|nlm\rangle=0$ by parity;
exception: degenerate $n=2$ states of hydrogen;
(20--45~min) Linear Stark effect in hydrogen $n=2$:
four degenerate states $\{2s,2p_{-1},2p_0,2p_1\}$;
only $\langle 2s|\hat{H}'|2p_0\rangle=-3eEa_0$ is non-zero (by selection rules and parity);
diagonalise $4\times4$ matrix; four eigenstates with energies $\{-3eEa_0,0,0,+3eEa_0\}$;
physical picture: mixed $s$-$p$ states with permanent electric dipole moment;
(45--65~min) Quadratic Stark effect for ground state of H:
$E^{(2)}_0=\sum_{n\neq 0}|\langle n|\hat{H}'|0\rangle|^2/(E_0-E_n)$;
evaluate using sum rules: $E^{(2)}_0=-\tfrac{9}{4}a_0^3E^2$ (exact);
polarisability $\alpha=-\partial^2 E/\partial E^2=\tfrac{9}{2}a_0^3$ (in Gaussian units);
(65--90~min) Parabolic coordinates for the Stark effect in hydrogen:
exact separation in $(\xi,\eta,\phi)$; quantum numbers $n_1,n_2,m$;
$E_{n_1 n_2 m}^{(1)}=-3neEa_0(n_1-n_2)/2$; connection to classical ionisation (barrier suppression);
strong-field ionisation and above-threshold ionisation preview.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Explain why the first-order Stark shift vanishes for non-degenerate parity eigenstates.
  \item Compute the linear Stark effect for hydrogen $n=2$ by degenerate PT.
  \item Derive the quadratic Stark shift and polarisability for the hydrogen ground state.
  \item Describe parabolic coordinates and the exact separation of the Stark Hamiltonian.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Dual-track content:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item \textit{Physical track:} Stark effect in molecular spectroscopy (polarity measurement);
    DC Stark shift for qubit control; electric-field ionisation; Rydberg atoms in electric fields;
    barrier-suppression ionisation in intense laser fields.
  \item \textit{Mathematical track:} Sum-rule approach to quadratic Stark; parabolic coordinates as
    a natural frame for the Coulomb + linear potential problem; connection to classical action variables.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``an electric field shifts energy levels --- the Stark effect measures molecular polarity.''
Beg.\ UG: parity argument for vanishing first order; $n=2$ linear Stark; polarisability.
Adv.\ UG: quadratic Stark derivation; sum rules; parabolic quantum numbers.
MSc: exact parabolic solution; tunnelling ionisation (Keldysh parameter); above-threshold ionisation.
PhD: strong-field ionisation rates (ADK formula); high-harmonic generation; attosecond physics.

\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- parity argument; $n=2$ Stark matrix elements; polarisability of H ground state.
Set~B --- derive quadratic Stark via sum rules; parabolic quantum numbers for $n=3$ H.
Projects: (simple) Stark energy levels for H $n=2,3$: linear splitting vs.\ field;
(complex) polarisability of alkali atoms from sum rules: compare Li, Na, K.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

% ------ L08 -----------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~I.4 / L08: Spin--Orbit Coupling and Fine Structure of Hydrogen}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Physical origin of spin--orbit coupling:
in the rest frame of the electron, the nucleus orbits and creates a magnetic field
$\mathbf{B}_{\rm eff}=\mathbf{v}\times\mathbf{E}/c^2$;
magnetic moment of the electron $\hat{\boldsymbol\mu}_s=-g_s\mu_B\hat{\mathbf{S}}/\hbar$;
naive SO Hamiltonian $\hat{H}_{\rm SO}^{\rm naive}=\mu_B\mathbf{B}_{\rm eff}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{S}}/\hbar$;
Thomas precession: relativistic correction reduces by factor 2;
correct result $\hat{H}_{\rm SO}=\tfrac{1}{2m^2c^2}\tfrac{1}{r}\tfrac{dV}{dr}\hat{\mathbf{L}}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{S}}=\xi(r)\hat{\mathbf{L}}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{S}}$;
(20--45~min) Evaluation in hydrogen: $\hat{\mathbf{L}}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{S}}=\tfrac{1}{2}(\hat{J}^2-\hat{L}^2-\hat{S}^2)$;
eigenvalue in $|ljm_j\rangle$ basis: $\tfrac{\hbar^2}{2}[j(j+1)-l(l+1)-s(s+1)]$;
$\langle r^{-3}\rangle_{nl}=\tfrac{2}{n^3 a_0^3 l(l+\tfrac{1}{2})(l+1)}$;
first-order SO energy for $l>0$: $E_{\rm SO}^{(1)}=\tfrac{\alpha^2 E_n}{2n}\tfrac{j(j+1)-l(l+1)-3/4}{l(l+\tfrac{1}{2})(l+1)}$;
(45--65~min) Other fine-structure corrections: relativistic kinetic energy $\hat{H}_{\rm KE}'=-\hat{p}^4/8m^3c^2$;
Darwin term $\hat{H}_D=\tfrac{\pi\hbar^2}{2m^2c^2}|e|\delta^3(\mathbf{r})$ (only for $l=0$);
total fine structure: $E_{nj}^{\rm FS}=-\tfrac{\alpha^2 E_n}{2n^2}\bigl[\tfrac{4n}{j+1/2}-3\bigr]$;
(65--90~min) Fine structure of hydrogen: energy level diagram including all three corrections;
$2s_{1/2}$ and $2p_{1/2}$ are degenerate in Dirac theory; Lamb shift lifts this (QED);
comparison with Dirac equation prediction; $LS$ vs.\ $jj$ coupling in heavy atoms;
hyperfine structure from nuclear spin (preview); precision measurements and the fine structure constant.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Derive the spin--orbit Hamiltonian including the Thomas precession factor.
  \item Evaluate SO energy corrections using $\hat{\mathbf{L}}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{S}}$ in the $|ljm_j\rangle$ basis.
  \item Identify all three fine-structure corrections and compute the total $E_{nj}^{\rm FS}$.
  \item Explain the Lamb shift qualitatively and its significance for QED.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Dual-track content:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item \textit{Physical track:} Fine structure as the gateway to relativistic QM;
    Thomas precession as a measurable relativistic effect; $LS$ vs.\ $jj$ coupling in the periodic table;
    Lamb shift as the first clear sign of vacuum fluctuations (QED); precision spectroscopy tests.
  \item \textit{Mathematical track:} Derivation from Dirac equation in the non-relativistic limit;
    $1/r\,dV/dr$ expectation value via Kramers--Pasternack relation;
    Foldy--Wouthuysen transformation.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``relativity and quantum mechanics together split hydrogen's spectral lines into fine structure.''
Beg.\ UG: SO Hamiltonian; $\hat{\mathbf{L}}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{S}}$ in $j$-basis; energy diagram.
Adv.\ UG: Thomas precession; Darwin term; all three corrections; $E_{nj}^{\rm FS}$.
MSc: Lamb shift (qualitative QED); $jj$ coupling in heavy atoms; Kramers--Pasternack.
PhD: Foldy--Wouthuysen; Dirac equation non-relativistic limit; QED radiative corrections;
Breit equation for two-electron systems.

\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- SO energy for H $2p$ with $j=3/2$ and $j=1/2$; fine-structure splitting;
Darwin correction for $ns$ states.
Set~B --- derive $\hat{H}_{\rm SO}$ including Thomas factor; Kramers--Pasternack for $\langle r^{-3}\rangle$;
fine-structure formula $E_{nj}^{\rm FS}$.
Projects: (simple) hydrogen fine-structure energy level diagram: $n=1,2,3$ including all three corrections;
(complex) Foldy--Wouthuysen transformation: derive non-relativistic limit of Dirac Hamiltonian.
\end{tcolorbox}


\medskip

% ------ L09 -----------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~I.4 / L09: The Hydrogen Atom}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Hydrogen Hamiltonian in atomic units:
$\hat{H}=-\tfrac{1}{2}\nabla^2-\tfrac{1}{r}$;
separation in spherical coordinates: $\psi_{nlm}(r,\theta,\phi)=R_{nl}(r)Y_l^m(\theta,\phi)$;
reduction of radial equation via $u_{nl}(r)=rR_{nl}(r)$;
effective potential $V_{\rm eff}(r)=-1/r+l(l+1)/2r^2$;
(20--45~min) Power-series solution: associated Laguerre polynomials;
termination condition gives quantisation $E_n=-1/(2n^2)$ a.u.\ $= -13.6/n^2$~eV;
principal quantum number $n=1,2,3,\ldots$; orbital $l=0,\ldots,n-1$; magnetic $m=-l,\ldots,l$;
radial wavefunctions $R_{nl}(r)$ for $n=1,2,3$; radial nodes $n-l-1$; angular nodes $l$;
(45--65~min) Degeneracy: $n^2$-fold degeneracy (ignoring spin); explanation via hidden $SO(4)$ symmetry;
Runge--Lenz vector $\hat{\mathbf{A}}$; $[\hat{H},\hat{\mathbf{A}}]=0$; $\mathfrak{so}(4)$ algebra;
algebraic derivation of $1/n^2$ spectrum without solving the radial equation;
(65--90~min) Expectation values and radial properties: $\langle r\rangle_{nl}=a_0[3n^2-l(l+1)]/2Z$;
$\langle r^{-1}\rangle=Z/n^2a_0$; $\langle r^{-3}\rangle$ (Kramers--Pasternack);
most probable radius; radial probability density $4\pi r^2|R_{nl}|^2$;
connection to fine structure (L08) and to multi-electron atoms.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Separate the hydrogen Schr\"odinger equation and solve the radial part.
  \item State the energy spectrum, quantum numbers, and degeneracy.
  \item Compute radial expectation values and interpret radial probability densities.
  \item Explain the hidden $SO(4)$ symmetry and its algebraic consequences.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Dual-track content:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item \textit{Physical track:} Hydrogen as the prototype for all atomic structure;
    comparison with experimental spectroscopy (Lyman, Balmer, Paschen series);
    connection to fine structure (L08), Zeeman (L06), and Stark (L07) effects.
  \item \textit{Mathematical track:} Runge--Lenz vector and $\mathfrak{so}(4)$ algebra;
    algebraic derivation of the spectrum; parabolic coordinates as an alternative separation;
    $N$-dimensional hydrogen and supersymmetric QM.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: hydrogen orbitals as the shapes of atomic physics; spectral series and the Bohr model vs.\ exact QM.
Beg.\ UG: radial wavefunctions; probability densities; $E_n=-13.6/n^2$~eV; quantum numbers.
Adv.\ UG: series solution and termination; $\langle r^k\rangle_{nl}$; $SO(4)$ symmetry sketch.
MSc: Runge--Lenz vector algebra; parabolic coordinates; algebraic derivation of spectrum.
PhD: $N$-dimensional hydrogen; supersymmetric QM for hydrogen; muonic hydrogen and reduced mass.

\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- $R_{10},R_{21}$; probability density; most probable radius; $\langle r\rangle_{2p}$; $E_n$.
Set~B --- termination condition derivation; prove $[\hat{H},\hat{\mathbf{A}}]=0$; algebraic spectrum from $\mathfrak{so}(4)$.
Projects: (simple) radial probability density plotter for all orbitals with $n\leq3$;
(complex) Runge--Lenz algebra: derive energy spectrum of hydrogen without the Schr\"odinger equation.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

% ------ L10 -----------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~I.4 / L10: Scattering from a Potential Barrier}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Setup: particle with energy $E$ incident from the left on a
rectangular potential barrier $V_0>0$ of width $a$;
three regions with different wavevectors:
$k_1=\sqrt{2mE}/\hbar$ (regions I, III), $k_2=\sqrt{2m|E-V_0|}/\hbar$ (region II);
two sub-cases: $E>V_0$ (above barrier) and $E<V_0$ (tunnelling);
(20--50~min) Matching boundary conditions: continuity of $\psi$ and $\psi'$ at $x=0$ and $x=a$;
matrix transfer method; transmission amplitude $t$ and reflection amplitude $r$;
transmission coefficient $T=|t|^2$ and reflection coefficient $R=|r|^2$; verify $T+R=1$;
above-barrier case $E>V_0$: oscillatory $T(E)$ with resonances at $k_2 a=n\pi$;
(50--70~min) Tunnelling case $E<V_0$: $k_2\to i\kappa_2=i\sqrt{2m(V_0-E)}/\hbar$;
$T=\bigl[1+\tfrac{(k_1^2+\kappa_2^2)^2}{4k_1^2\kappa_2^2}\sinh^2(\kappa_2 a)\bigr]^{-1}$;
thin-barrier limit: $T\approx e^{-2\kappa_2 a}$; Gamow factor;
applications: alpha decay, STM, nuclear fusion;
(70--90~min) Step potential (limiting case $a\to0$, $V_0\to\infty$):
$T=4k_1k_2/(k_1+k_2)^2$, $R=(k_1-k_2)^2/(k_1+k_2)^2$;
above-barrier reflection (quantum effect with no classical analogue);
energy dependence of $T$; time delay; phase of reflection coefficient; Hartman effect.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Apply boundary conditions to derive $T$ and $R$ for a rectangular barrier.
  \item Derive the tunnelling transmission coefficient and the Gamow factor.
  \item Explain above-barrier reflection as a quantum effect with no classical analogue.
  \item Identify resonance transmission conditions and their physical origin.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Dual-track content:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item \textit{Physical/applications track:} STM tunnelling current; alpha-decay Gamow factor;
    nuclear quantum tunnelling in fusion; Josephson junction; resonant tunnelling diode.
  \item \textit{Mathematical track:} Transfer matrix method; S-matrix; unitarity $T+R=1$ from
    probability current conservation; analytic structure of $T(E)$ and its poles (resonances).
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``a quantum particle can pass through a wall --- that's tunnelling.''
Beg.\ UG: rectangular barrier $T$ and $R$; tunnelling formula; step potential.
Adv.\ UG: transfer matrix; resonance condition; Gamow factor; Hartman effect.
MSc: S-matrix; analytic continuation; poles and resonances; time delay.
PhD: Breit--Wigner resonances; complex scaling; multi-channel scattering; Feshbach resonances.

\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- $T$ and $R$ for rectangular barrier at given $E$ and $V_0$; verify $T+R=1$; step potential.
Set~B --- transfer matrix derivation; thin-barrier $T\approx e^{-2\kappa a}$; resonance condition.
Projects: (simple) $T(E)$ plotter for rectangular barrier: resonances and tunnelling regime;
(complex) STM tunnelling current vs.\ tip--sample distance: exponential decay and work function.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

% ------ L11 -----------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~I.4 / L11: Scattering from a Potential Well}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Finite square well: $V(x)=-V_0<0$ for $|x|<a$, $V=0$ outside;
bound states ($E<0$) vs.\ scattering states ($E>0$); even and odd solutions from parity;
(20--50~min) Bound states: inside $k=\sqrt{2m(E+V_0)}/\hbar$;
outside $\kappa=\sqrt{-2mE}/\hbar$;
transcendental equations: $k\tan(ka)=\kappa$ (even), $-k\cot(ka)=\kappa$ (odd);
graphical solution; minimum well depth for first bound state $V_0^{\rm min}=\pi^2\hbar^2/8ma^2$;
number of bound states $\approx\sqrt{2mV_0}\cdot 2a/\pi\hbar$;
(50--70~min) Scattering states ($E>0$): transmission resonances at $k_{\rm in}a=n\pi/2$
(Ramsauer--Townsend effect); $T=1$ at resonance (perfect transmission);
physical interpretation: standing wave inside well; comparison with classical case;
(70--90~min) Ramsauer--Townsend effect in rare-gas electron scattering: historical significance;
comparison of 1D well with 3D spherically symmetric well;
zero-energy scattering: scattering length $a_s$; $T\to1$ for $a_s\to0$;
connection to Feshbach resonances in cold atom physics; unitarity limit.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Solve the finite square well for both bound and scattering states.
  \item Derive the transcendental equations graphically and interpret their solutions.
  \item Explain transmission resonances and the Ramsauer--Townsend effect.
  \item Define scattering length and relate it to the Feshbach resonance.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Dual-track content:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item \textit{Physical track:} Ramsauer--Townsend effect as the first evidence for wave nature of electrons;
    nuclear well models; cold-atom Feshbach resonances; unitarity limit in scattering.
  \item \textit{Mathematical track:} Transcendental equations and graphical analysis;
    analytic structure of $T(E)$; scattering length from the zero-energy limit of the S-matrix;
    Levinson's theorem: $\delta(0)-\delta(\infty)=N_b\pi$.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: finite well as a better model than infinite well; why bound states have limited energy.
Beg.\ UG: even/odd bound states; graphical solution; transmission resonances.
Adv.\ UG: minimum well depth; Ramsauer--Townsend; scattering length.
MSc: Levinson's theorem; Feshbach resonances; connection to cold-atom physics.
PhD: multi-channel scattering; effective range expansion; universality at unitarity.

\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- bound state count for given $V_0,a$; graphical transcendental solution; resonance $E$.
Set~B --- derive transcendental equations from BCs; Levinson's theorem statement and example.
Projects: (simple) bound state energies vs.\ $V_0$ for finite well: emergence of new states;
(complex) Ramsauer--Townsend: $T(E)$ for Xe modelled as a finite spherical well.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

% ------ L12 -----------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~I.4 / L12: Delta-Function Potential and WKB Tunnelling}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) The delta-function potential $V(x)=-\alpha\delta(x)$;
integration of Schr\"odinger equation across $x=0$: discontinuity in $\psi'$,
continuity of $\psi$; condition $\psi'(0^+)-\psi'(0^-)=-2m\alpha\psi(0)/\hbar^2$;
(20--45~min) Bound state ($E<0$): $\psi=Ae^{-\kappa|x|}$ with $\kappa=m\alpha/\hbar^2$;
$E_b=-m\alpha^2/2\hbar^2$ (unique bound state for any $\alpha>0$);
scattering states: $T=1/(1+m\alpha^2/2\hbar^2 E)$; $R=1-T$;
double delta-function: two wells at $\pm a$; bonding and antibonding states;
connection to molecular bonding;
(45--65~min) WKB approximation reviewed: $\psi\approx C/\sqrt{p(x)}\exp(\pm\tfrac{i}{\hbar}\int p(x)dx)$
in classically allowed regions; $p(x)=\sqrt{2m(E-V(x))}$;
connection formulae across turning points;
Bohr--Sommerfeld quantisation $\oint p\,dx=2\pi\hbar(n+\tfrac{1}{2})$;
(65--90~min) WKB tunnelling: barrier penetration factor
$T\approx\exp\bigl(-\tfrac{2}{\hbar}\int_{x_1}^{x_2}\sqrt{2m(V-E)}\,dx\bigr)$;
Gamow factor for Coulomb barrier: $G=\pi Z_1Z_2e^2/\hbar v$;
alpha decay rate $\Gamma=\nu_0 T$ with attempt frequency $\nu_0$; Geiger--Nuttall law;
WKB for bound states in a Morse potential; limitations at turning points.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Solve the delta-function potential for bound and scattering states.
  \item Derive the WKB wavefunction and Bohr--Sommerfeld quantisation.
  \item Compute the WKB tunnelling factor for a general barrier.
  \item Apply the Gamow factor to alpha decay and derive the Geiger--Nuttall law.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Dual-track content:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item \textit{Physical track:} Delta potential as a model for molecular bonding (H$_2^+$);
    WKB tunnelling in alpha decay, proton--proton fusion in the Sun;
    Geiger--Nuttall law as a triumph of WKB; enzyme catalysis via proton tunnelling.
  \item \textit{Mathematical track:} Distributional derivative and delta-function BCs;
    WKB as the leading-order term in an $\hbar$ expansion;
    connection formulae from Airy functions; uniform approximation near turning points.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: the delta potential as the thinnest possible wall; WKB as ``tunnelling with an exponential rule.''
Beg.\ UG: delta-function bound state and $T$; WKB quantisation for HO; Gamow factor formula.
Adv.\ UG: double delta-function bonding/antibonding; WKB connection formulae; Geiger--Nuttall.
MSc: Airy function connection formulae; Morse potential WKB levels; uniform approximation.
PhD: Instanton as imaginary-time WKB; exact WKB; resurgence; Gamow vectors and complex scaling.

\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- delta-function $E_b$ and $T$; WKB levels for harmonic oscillator; Gamow factor for $^{238}$U.
Set~B --- double delta-function bonding/antibonding states; WKB connection formula derivation.
Projects: (simple) WKB energy levels for Morse potential vs.\ exact: anharmonicity;
(complex) Geiger--Nuttall law: alpha decay rate vs.\ $Z$ and $E_\alpha$ for actinide series.
\end{tcolorbox}

%------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Assessment Strategy}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Module I.4 Assessment Strategy}

\begin{tcolorbox}[highlightbox]
\textbf{Per-Lecture Assessment Bundle} (every lecture):
concept check (10--15~min, 5--8 short conceptual questions);
Problem Set~A (simple, 6--10 computational exercises);
Problem Set~B (complex, 3--6 multi-step derivations and proofs);
mini-project simple (1--3 hours);
mini-project complex (5--10 hours, open-ended).
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Course-level grading template:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.5em]
  \item Weekly homework (best 9/12): 40\%
  \item System synthesis project (one chosen system, deep study): 35\%
  \item Final oral/whiteboard exam: 25\%
\end{itemize}
Mixed cohorts: HS/UG $\to$ Set~A + simple projects; MSc/PhD $\to$ Set~B + complex projects.

%------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Reading Strategy}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Module I.4 Reading Strategy}

\noindent\textbf{Track A --- Core textbooks:}
Sakurai \& Napolitano, \textit{Modern Quantum Mechanics} Ch.~2 (HO, hydrogen), 4 (Zeeman/Stark), 5 (PT);
Griffiths, \textit{Introduction to Quantum Mechanics} Ch.~2--6 (all systems).

\noindent\textbf{Track B --- Support:}
Cohen-Tannoudji, Diu \& Lalo\"e, \textit{Quantum Mechanics} Vol.~II (spin--orbit, Stark, scattering);
Atkins \& Friedman, \textit{Molecular Quantum Mechanics} (Zeeman, hydrogen, spectroscopy).

\noindent\textbf{Track C --- Specialised:}
Allen \& Eberly, \textit{Optical Resonance and Two-Level Atoms} (Rabi model);
Landau \& Lifshitz, \textit{Quantum Mechanics} \S{}23 (delta potential), \S{}50 (WKB), \S{}113 (Stark);
Holstein, Am.\ J.\ Phys.\ \textbf{57}, 714 (1989) --- Thomas precession;
Gamow, Z.\ Phys.\ \textbf{51}, 204 (1928) --- original tunnelling calculation.

%=============================================================
\subsection{Module I.5 --- Introductory Physical Systems (Lecture Menu)}
\label{sec:mod-I5}
%=============================================================

\begin{tcolorbox}[seriesbox]
  \textbf{Series I / Module~I.5} \quad
  \textit{Introductory Physical Systems --- Lecture Menu}\\[4pt]
  \textbf{Format:} 12 stand-alone lecture topics at the level of a first
  quantum mechanics course. Each topic is self-contained and applies the
  formalism of Modules~I.1--I.3 to a canonical physical system.
  Instructors may select any subset as worked-example lectures or problem
  classes. Full expansion to the standard 90-minute format (dual-track
  content, five-tier pedagogy, Problem Sets A \& B, mini-projects) is
  available on request.\\[4pt]
  \textbf{Recommended audience:} Undergraduate students during or
  immediately after Module~I.3. Prerequisites: Modules~I.1--I.3.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\subsubsection*{Module Overview}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Module I.5 Overview}

{\footnotesize
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lp{4.2cm}p{6.8cm}@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Lec.} & \textbf{Title} & \textbf{Key Concepts / Theme}\\
\midrule
L01 & The Finite Square Well & Bound state counting; graphical transcendental; parity\\
L02 & The Quantum Harmonic Oscillator in 1D (Wave Mechanics) & Hermite polynomials; recursion; zero-point; wave functions\\
L03 & The Rigid Rotor & Spherical harmonics; moment of inertia; rotational spectra\\
L04 & The Hydrogen-Like Ion & $Z_{\rm eff}$; scaling of $E_n$; radial densities; periodic table\\
L05 & The Particle on a Ring & $e^{im\phi}$; angular momentum quantisation; Aharonov--Bohm\\
L06 & The Double-Well Potential & Tunnelling splitting; symmetric/antisymmetric; inversion in NH$_3$\\
\midrule
L07 & The Kronig--Penney Model & Periodic $\delta$-function array; band structure; Bloch waves\\
L08 & The Helium Atom & Two-electron problem; variational $Z_{\rm eff}$; exchange\\
L09 & The H$_2$ Molecule (Simple LCAO) & Bonding/antibonding; overlap integral; dissociation curve\\
L10 & The Square Barrier and Tunnel Diode & Resonant tunnelling; $T(E)$ oscillations; device physics\\
L11 & The Linear Stark Effect in Hydrogen & Degenerate PT; $n=2$ level splitting; parabolic eigenstates\\
L12 & The 1D Dirac Comb and Band Gaps & Bloch's theorem applied; dispersion relation; effective mass\\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
}

\subsubsection*{Lecture Titles and Scope}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Module I.5 Lecture Titles}

\begin{description}[leftmargin=1.4em, style=nextline, itemsep=6pt]
\emergencystretch=3em

\item[\textbf{L01 --- The Finite Square Well}]
  The finite square well $V(x)=-V_0$ for $|x|<a$ as the prototype for
  quantum confinement with finite barriers. Even and odd bound-state
  solutions; transcendental equations and their graphical solution;
  minimum well depth for the first bound state; dependence of bound-state
  count on $V_0$ and $a$; penetration of the wavefunction into classically
  forbidden regions; comparison with the infinite square well; application
  to quantum dots, nuclear potential wells, and optical waveguides.

\item[\textbf{L02 --- The Quantum Harmonic Oscillator in 1D (Wave-Mechanics Approach)}]
  Schr\"odinger equation in dimensionless units; asymptotic behaviour at
  large $|x|$; power-series (Frobenius) solution; Hermite polynomials
  $H_n(\xi)$; termination condition and energy quantisation
  $E_n=(n+\tfrac{1}{2})\hbar\omega$; normalised wavefunctions
  $\psi_n(x)=N_n H_n(\alpha x)e^{-\alpha^2x^2/2}$; parity; node theorem;
  zero-point energy; comparison with classical probability density;
  connection to the ladder-operator treatment of Module~I.4-L03.

\item[\textbf{L03 --- The Rigid Rotor}]
  Quantum rigid rotor as a particle constrained to a sphere of radius $R$;
  Hamiltonian $\hat{H}=\hat{\mathbf{L}}^2/2I$ with moment of inertia $I=\mu R^2$;
  eigenfunctions $Y_l^m(\theta,\phi)$ and eigenvalues $E_l=\hbar^2l(l+1)/2I$;
  degeneracy $2l+1$; rotational constant $B=\hbar^2/2I$;
  electric dipole selection rule $\Delta l=\pm1$;
  microwave rotational spectrum: equally spaced lines at $\bar\nu=2B(l+1)$;
  determination of bond lengths; centrifugal distortion correction;
  connection to diatomic molecular spectroscopy.

\item[\textbf{L04 --- Hydrogen-Like Ions}]
  Generalisation of hydrogen to nuclear charge $Z$: $\hat{H}=-\nabla^2/2-Z/r$;
  scaling $E_{nl}\to Z^2E_n^{\rm H}$ and $\langle r\rangle\to\langle r\rangle^{\rm H}/Z$;
  radial wavefunctions for He$^+$, Li$^{2+}$, and general $Z$;
  connection to Slater screening and $Z_{\rm eff}$ in many-electron atoms;
  ionisation energies across the periodic table;
  X-ray emission energies (Moseley's law);
  positronium ($\mu\to m_e/2$) and muonic hydrogen ($\mu\to m_\mu$);
  reduced mass correction and its significance.

\item[\textbf{L05 --- The Particle on a Ring}]
  Particle confined to a 1D ring of radius $R$; Hamiltonian
  $\hat{H}=-(\hbar^2/2mR^2)\partial^2/\partial\phi^2$; periodic boundary
  conditions; eigenfunctions $e^{im\phi}/\sqrt{2\pi}$; quantised angular
  momentum $\hbar m$, $m\in\mathbb{Z}$; doubly degenerate levels $E_m=\hbar^2m^2/2I$
  ($m\neq0$); application to $\pi$-electrons in benzene (H\"uckel analogy);
  Aharonov--Bohm effect on a ring: flux-dependent energy levels
  $E_m\propto(m-\Phi/\Phi_0)^2$; persistent current in mesoscopic rings.

\item[\textbf{L06 --- The Double-Well Potential and Molecular Inversion}]
  Symmetric double well $V(x)=\tfrac{\lambda}{4}(x^2-a^2)^2$;
  qualitative picture: two nearly degenerate levels split by tunnelling;
  symmetric ($+$) and antisymmetric ($-$) combinations of localised states;
  tunnelling splitting $\Delta E\propto e^{-\gamma}$;
  inversion of NH$_3$: experimental microwave spectrum at 23.79~GHz;
  application to maser principle; asymmetric double well and localisation;
  connection to instanton picture (Module~II.2~L08); two-level system
  Hamiltonian $\hat{H}=-\tfrac{\Delta}{2}\hat\sigma_z-\tfrac{\epsilon}{2}\hat\sigma_x$.

\item[\textbf{L07 --- The Kronig--Penney Model}]
  1D periodic array of $\delta$-function barriers $V(x)=\sum_n V_0\,\delta(x-na)$;
  Bloch's theorem applied; transfer matrix for one period; transcendental
  dispersion relation $\cos(ka)=\cos(K a)+\tfrac{mV_0}{\hbar^2 K}\sin(Ka)$;
  graphical solution: allowed bands where $|\cos ka|\leq1$;
  band gaps at $ka=n\pi$; effective mass near band edges; weak- and
  strong-coupling limits; connection to the nearly-free electron and
  tight-binding models; relevance to semiconductor superlattices.

\item[\textbf{L08 --- The Helium Atom}]
  Two-electron Hamiltonian $\hat{H}=-\tfrac{1}{2}\nabla_1^2-\tfrac{1}{2}\nabla_2^2
  -2/r_1-2/r_2+1/r_{12}$; zeroth-order product wavefunction;
  first-order perturbation theory: $\langle1/r_{12}\rangle=5Z/8$;
  variational treatment with $Z_{\rm eff}$; shielding constant;
  exchange integral; para- and ortho-helium (singlet and triplet);
  comparison of perturbative, variational, and experimental energies;
  connection to Slater--Condon rules and the many-body problem.

\item[\textbf{L09 --- The H$_2$ Molecule: Simple LCAO-MO}]
  H$_2$ as the simplest two-electron molecule; Born--Oppenheimer PES;
  LCAO-MO ansatz with $1s$ hydrogen orbitals; bonding $\sigma_g$ and
  antibonding $\sigma_u^*$ MOs; overlap $S$, Coulomb $\alpha$, and resonance
  $\beta$ integrals; variational MO energies; bond order; optimise bond
  length and compare to experiment; Heitler--London VB wavefunction;
  comparison of MO and VB predictions for dissociation; correlation energy.

\item[\textbf{L10 --- The Square Barrier and Resonant Tunnel Diode}]
  Double-barrier heterostructure $V(x)$: two rectangular barriers of height
  $V_0$ and width $b$ separated by a well of width $a$; transmission $T(E)$
  via the transfer matrix; resonant transmission $T=1$ when quasi-bound
  state energy $E_n$ lies below $V_0$; resonance width $\Gamma$;
  current--voltage ($I$--$V$) characteristic of a resonant tunnel diode;
  peak-to-valley ratio; negative differential resistance; GaAs/AlAs
  heterostructure parameters; applications in high-frequency oscillators.

\item[\textbf{L11 --- The Linear Stark Effect in Hydrogen}]
  Electric field perturbation $\hat{H}'=-eEz$ applied to the degenerate
  $n=2$ level of hydrogen ($2s$, $2p_{-1}$, $2p_0$, $2p_1$);
  selection rules from parity and $\Delta m=0$;
  only $\langle 2s|z|2p_0\rangle=-3ea_0$ is non-zero;
  degenerate perturbation theory: diagonalise the $4\times4$ perturbation matrix;
  four eigenstates with energies $\pm3eEa_0$ and two unshifted states;
  physical picture: linear combinations with permanent electric dipole moment;
  parabolic eigenstates $|n_1,n_2,m\rangle$; comparison with the quadratic
  (second-order) Stark effect of the $n=1$ ground state.

\item[\textbf{L12 --- The 1D Dirac Comb and Band Structure}]
  Dirac comb: infinite periodic array of $\delta$-function wells
  $V(x)=-\alpha\sum_n\delta(x-na)$; exact solution using Bloch's theorem and
  transfer-matrix matching; dispersion relation
  $\cos(ka)=\cos(Ka)-\tfrac{m\alpha}{\hbar^2 K}\sin(Ka)$;
  energy bands and gaps in the reduced zone scheme;
  effective mass $m^*$ at band edges; density of states in 1D;
  dependence of band gaps on $\alpha$: strong-coupling (tight-binding)
  and weak-coupling (nearly-free electron) limits;
  connection to the Kronig--Penney model (L07) and Bloch electron (Module~I.4-L02).

\end{description}

\begin{tcolorbox}[highlightbox]
\textbf{Module I.5 Note:} These lecture topics are pitched at the level of a
standard first-year quantum mechanics course (advanced undergraduate).
Each can be taught as a standalone 90-minute worked-example class or
problem session. Full expansion to the standard syllabus format
(90-min pacing, dual-track content, five-tier pedagogy,
Problem Sets A \& B, simple and complex mini-projects) is available on request.
\end{tcolorbox}

mechanics to modern research areas.\\[4pt]
