\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
}

\subsubsection*{Lecture-by-Lecture Syllabi}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Module II.3 Lecture Syllabi}

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.3 / L01: The $\mathfrak{su}(2)$ Algebra}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Rotation symmetry generators $\hat{J}_x,\hat{J}_y,\hat{J}_z$; algebra $[\hat{J}_i,\hat{J}_j]=i\hbar\epsilon_{ijk}\hat{J}_k$; Casimir $\hat{\mathbf{J}}^2$ commutes with all $\hat{J}_i$; (20--45~min) Irreducible representations: $j\in\{0,\tfrac{1}{2},1,\ldots\}$; simultaneous eigenstates $\ket{j,m}$; $(2j+1)$-dimensional; (45--70~min) $SU(2)$ vs.\ $SO(3)$: $2\pi$ rotation gives $-1$ for half-integer $j$; Schur's lemma; (70--90~min) Physical realisations: orbital AM ($j$ integer), spin ($j$ half-integer); fundamental vs.\ adjoint representation.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item State $\mathfrak{su}(2)$ commutation relations and identify the Casimir.
  \item Label irreps by $j,m$ and state their ranges.
  \item Distinguish $SU(2)$ from $SO(3)$ and explain double-valued representations.
  \item Apply Schur's lemma.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``angular momentum comes in units of $\hbar$.''
Beg.\ UG: Casimir; $2\times2$ and $3\times3$ representations.
Adv.\ UG: all irreps from Schur; $SU(2)$ vs.\ $SO(3)$.
MSc: universal enveloping algebra; Casimir from Killing form.
PhD: highest-weight theory; Verma modules; quantum groups $SU_q(2)$.
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- verify Casimir commutes with $\hat{J}_i$; eigenvalues for $j=1,\tfrac{3}{2}$.
Set~B --- prove irreps labelled by $j\geq 0$; $SU(2)$ double cover.
Projects: (simple) angular momentum algebra visualiser; (complex) character table for $j=0,\tfrac{1}{2},1,\tfrac{3}{2}$.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.3 / L02: Ladder Operators and Spectrum}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Ladder operators $\hat{J}_\pm=\hat{J}_x\pm i\hat{J}_y$; $[\hat{J}_z,\hat{J}_\pm]=\pm\hbar\hat{J}_\pm$; (20--50~min) Matrix elements $\hat{J}_+\ket{j,m}=\hbar\sqrt{j(j+1)-m(m+1)}\ket{j,m+1}$; termination at $m=\pm j$; quantisation of $j$; (50--70~min) Explicit matrices $j=\tfrac{1}{2}$ (Pauli) and $j=1$; (70--90~min) Schwinger boson representation: $\hat{J}_+=\hat{a}^\dagger\hat{b}$, $\hat{J}_-=\hat{b}^\dagger\hat{a}$; spin coherent states.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Derive spectrum and matrix elements via ladder operators.
  \item Explain quantisation of $j$ from ladder termination.
  \item Write explicit matrices for $j=\tfrac{1}{2},1$.
  \item Construct the Schwinger boson representation.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- matrix elements $\bra{j,m'}\hat{J}_x\ket{j,m}$ for $j=1$; $\hat{\mathbf{J}}^2$ check.
Set~B --- quantisation from termination; Schwinger boson algebra.
Projects: (simple) Bloch sphere visualiser; (complex) Schwinger bosons: generate all $j$ from two HO modes.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.3 / L03: Orbital Angular Momentum and Spherical Harmonics}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) $\hat{\mathbf{L}}=-i\hbar(\mathbf{r}\times\nabla)$; $\hat{L}_z=-i\hbar\partial_\phi$; $\hat{\mathbf{L}}^2$ in spherical coordinates; (20--50~min) Spherical harmonics $Y_l^m(\theta,\phi)$; associated Legendre polynomials; orthonormality; parity $(-1)^l$; (50--70~min) Addition theorem; solid harmonics; multipole expansion; (70--90~min) Rigid rotor $\hat{H}=\hat{\mathbf{L}}^2/2I$; spectrum $E_l=\hbar^2l(l+1)/2I$; selection rule $\Delta l=\pm1$.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Express $\hat{L}_z$ and $\hat{\mathbf{L}}^2$ in spherical coordinates.
  \item State properties of spherical harmonics and use the addition theorem.
  \item Solve the rigid rotor and identify selection rules.
  \item Apply multipole expansion.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- $Y_l^m$ for $l=0,1$; addition theorem; rigid rotor spectrum.
Set~B --- derive $\hat{\mathbf{L}}^2$ in spherical coordinates; prove addition theorem.
Projects: (simple) 3D orbital visualiser; (complex) multipole expansion of arbitrary charge distribution.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.3 / L04: Spin Angular Momentum}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Spin: $\hat{\mathbf{S}}=\tfrac{\hbar}{2}\hat{\boldsymbol{\sigma}}$; Pauli matrices; spinors; (20--45~min) $SU(2)$ double cover; $2\pi$ rotation $\to-1$; neutron interferometry; (45--65~min) Spin in magnetic field: Larmor precession; Rabi formula; (65--90~min) Spin coherent states; Bloch sphere; over-completeness; spin-coherent-state PI.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Compute Pauli matrix algebra and spin precession.
  \item Explain the $SU(2)$ double cover physically.
  \item Solve spin in a magnetic field exactly.
  \item Describe spin coherent states and the Bloch sphere.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- Pauli algebra; Larmor frequency; $\langle\hat{S}_z\rangle(t)$.
Set~B --- $SU(2)$ double cover; spin coherent state over-completeness.
Projects: (simple) Bloch sphere trajectory for Rabi problem; (complex) spin-coherent-state PI: Berry phase.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.3 / L05: Addition of Angular Momenta}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) $\hat{\mathbf{J}}=\hat{\mathbf{J}}_1+\hat{\mathbf{J}}_2$; uncoupled and coupled bases; triangle rule; (20--50~min) Clebsch--Gordan coefficients; symmetry properties; ladder-operator derivation; tables for $\tfrac{1}{2}\otimes\tfrac{1}{2}$, $\tfrac{1}{2}\otimes1$; (50--70~min) Singlet and triplet states; entanglement; (70--90~min) Spin--orbit states for hydrogen; $6j$-symbols as recoupling coefficients.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Apply the triangle rule and compute CG coefficients.
  \item Construct singlet and triplet states.
  \item Apply CG to spin--orbit coupling in hydrogen.
  \item Define $6j$-symbols and explain recoupling.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- CG for $\tfrac{1}{2}\otimes1$; triplet/singlet states; spin--orbit $m_j$.
Set~B --- derive CG by ladders; verify orthogonality of coupled basis.
Projects: (simple) CG coefficient calculator; (complex) spin--orbit spectrum via CG recoupling.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.3 / L06: Wigner $3j$-Symbols and Racah Algebra}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Wigner $3j$-symbols; symmetry properties; relation to CG; (20--45~min) Racah formula; selection rules $m_1+m_2+m_3=0$ and triangle rule; (45--70~min) $6j$-symbols as recoupling; $9j$-symbols; orthogonality; (70--90~min) Applications: atomic $E1$ selection rules; Laporte rule; astrophysical line strengths.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Define $3j$-symbol and state symmetry properties.
  \item Derive selection rules from $3j$-symbols.
  \item Define $6j$-symbols and explain recoupling.
  \item Apply to atomic electric dipole selection rules.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- $3j$-symbols for given $j,m$; identify forbidden transitions.
Set~B --- $3j$ symmetry derivation; $6j$ orthogonality.
Projects: (simple) atomic line-strength calculator; (complex) Racah algebra for hyperfine matrix elements.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.3 / L07: The Wigner--Eckart Theorem}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Spherical tensor operators $\hat{T}^{(k)}_q$; transformation under $\hat{J}$; rank-0 (scalar), rank-1 (vector), rank-2 (quadrupole); (20--45~min) Wigner--Eckart theorem: $\bra{j',m'}\hat{T}^{(k)}_q\ket{j,m}=\braket{j,m;k,q|j',m'}\tfrac{\bra{j'}\|\hat{T}^{(k)}\|\ket{j}}{\sqrt{2j'+1}}$; reduced matrix element; (45--65~min) Applications: $E1$ selection rules; dipole matrix elements; Land\'e $g$-factor; (65--90~min) Composite systems; $6j$-symbols; effective operators.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Define spherical tensor operators and verify transformation properties.
  \item State W-E theorem and identify reduced matrix element.
  \item Apply W-E to selection rules and Land\'e $g$-factor.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- identify ranks; $E1,M1,E2$ selection rules; Land\'e $g$ for $^3P_1$.
Set~B --- W-E proof from Schur; reduced matrix element for HO ladder.
Projects: (simple) line-strength calculator; (complex) quadrupole moments for nuclear models.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.3 / L08: Hydrogen Atom and $SO(4)$ Symmetry}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Hydrogen Hamiltonian; separation; radial equation; (20--45~min) Radial wavefunctions; Laguerre polynomials; $E_n=-13.6/n^2$~eV; degeneracy $n^2$; (45--65~min) $SO(4)$: Runge--Lenz vector $\hat{\mathbf{A}}$; $[\hat{H},\hat{\mathbf{A}}]=0$; $\mathfrak{so}(4)$ from $\hat{\mathbf{L}}$ and rescaled $\hat{\mathbf{A}}$; algebraic derivation of $1/n^2$ spectrum; (65--90~min) Parabolic coordinates; $n_1,n_2,m$; Stark effect.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Solve the hydrogen radial equation and identify quantum numbers.
  \item Define Runge--Lenz and show $[\hat{H},\hat{\mathbf{A}}]=0$.
  \item Derive the spectrum algebraically from $\mathfrak{so}(4)$.
  \item Describe parabolic coordinates and Stark effect.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- $R_{nl}$ for $2s,2p$; $n=2$ degeneracy count.
Set~B --- verify Runge--Lenz commutator; $n^2$ degeneracy from $\mathfrak{so}(4)$.
Projects: (simple) hydrogen orbital density visualiser; (complex) algebraic spectrum without radial equation.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.3 / L09: Fine and Hyperfine Structure}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Three fine-structure corrections: relativistic KE, spin--orbit, Darwin; (20--45~min) First-order PT: $\hat{\mathbf{L}}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{S}}=\tfrac{1}{2}(\hat{\mathbf{J}}^2-\hat{\mathbf{L}}^2-\hat{\mathbf{S}}^2)$; $\langle r^{-3}\rangle_{nl}$; energy $E_{nj}^{(1)}$; (45--65~min) Hyperfine: Fermi contact + orbital + dipole--dipole; $\hat{\mathbf{F}}=\hat{\mathbf{J}}+\hat{\mathbf{I}}$; 21~cm line; (65--90~min) Zeeman: weak (anomalous) and strong (Paschen--Back); Breit--Rabi diagram.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Evaluate the three fine-structure corrections.
  \item Derive spin--orbit splitting via PT in the $j$-basis.
  \item Describe hyperfine Hamiltonian and 21~cm line.
  \item Analyse Zeeman effect in weak and strong limits.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- fine-structure splitting of $2p$; 21~cm energy.
Set~B --- $\langle r^{-3}\rangle_{nl}$; Darwin term; Breit--Rabi diagram.
Projects: (simple) hydrogen energy-level diagram with fine and hyperfine; (complex) Zeeman splitting of hyperfine levels: Breit--Rabi formula.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.3 / L10: Wigner $D$-matrices}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Euler angles; rotation operator $\hat{R}(\alpha,\beta,\gamma)=e^{-i\alpha\hat{J}_z/\hbar}e^{-i\beta\hat{J}_y/\hbar}e^{-i\gamma\hat{J}_z/\hbar}$; (20--45~min) $D^{(j)}_{m'm}(\alpha,\beta,\gamma)$; $d^{(j)}(\beta)$ real matrices; explicit forms for $j=\tfrac{1}{2},1$; (45--65~min) Properties: unitarity; orthogonality $\int D^{(j)*}D^{(j')}d\Omega\propto\delta_{jj'}$; connection $D^{(l)*}_{m0}\propto Y_l^m$; (65--90~min) Applications: rotation of $Y_l^m$; symmetric top; NMR pulse sequences; single-qubit gates.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Parametrise $SO(3)$ and compute $D$-matrices for $j=\tfrac{1}{2},1$.
  \item Apply orthogonality and connection to spherical harmonics.
  \item Rotate $Y_l^m$ and analyse symmetric top.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- $D^{(1/2)}(\alpha,\beta,\gamma)$; rotate $Y_1^0$; orthogonality.
Set~B --- group multiplication law; symmetric top selection rules.
Projects: (simple) $D$-matrix rotation visualiser; (complex) symmetric top levels and NMR pulses.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.3 / L11: Angular Momentum in Many-Body Systems}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Multi-electron atoms: $LS$ vs.\ $jj$ coupling; term symbols $^{2S+1}L_J$; Hund's rules; (20--45~min) $LS$ coupling: spin--orbit via W-E; Lande interval rule $E(J)-E(J-1)=\tfrac{A}{2}J$; (45--65~min) Nuclear shell model: magic numbers; spin--orbit splitting; $nlj$ states; (65--90~min) $jj$ coupling for heavy nuclei; intermediate coupling; Racah for many-body.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Construct term symbols and apply Hund's rules.
  \item Derive the Lande interval rule.
  \item Explain magic numbers from the shell model.
  \item Distinguish $LS$ and $jj$ coupling.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- term symbols for $p^2,d^3$; Hund's ground state; interval rule for $^3P$.
Set~B --- Lande interval rule; $LS$ vs.\ $jj$ for Pb vs.\ C.
Projects: (simple) atomic term symbol calculator; (complex) shell model: magic numbers from spin--orbit.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.3 / L12: Rotational Spectroscopy}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Rigid rotor: $E_J=\hbar^2J(J+1)/2I$; $B=\hbar/4\pi cI$; (20--45~min) Selection rules $\Delta J=\pm1$; microwave spectrum; bond lengths; centrifugal distortion; (45--65~min) Symmetric top: prolate/oblate; $E_{J,K}=\hbar^2[BJ(J+1)+(A-B)K^2]$; (65--90~min) Raman: $\Delta J=0,\pm2$; nuclear spin statistics; ortho/para-H$_2$; alternating intensity.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Derive rigid rotor spectrum and selection rules.
  \item Extract $B$ and bond length from rotational spectrum.
  \item Solve symmetric top and identify quantum numbers.
  \item Explain nuclear spin statistics and intensity alternation.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- rotational spectrum of HCl; $B$ and bond length; centrifugal distortion.
Set~B --- symmetric top energy levels; ortho/para-H$_2$ statistics.
Projects: (simple) simulated rotational spectrum of a diatomic; (complex) ortho/para-H$_2$ ratio vs.\ temperature.
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[highlightbox]
\textbf{Module II.3 Reading:} Sakurai \& Napolitano, Ch.~3; Edmonds, \textit{Angular Momentum in QM}; Varshalovich, Moskalev \& Khersonskii, \textit{Quantum Theory of Angular Momentum}; Bunker \& Jensen, \textit{Molecular Symmetry and Spectroscopy}.
\end{tcolorbox}

%=============================================================
\subsection{Module II.4 --- Second Quantisation and Introductory Many-Body Theory}
\label{sec:mod-II4}
%=============================================================

\subsubsection*{Module Overview}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Module II.4 Overview}

{\footnotesize
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lp{4.2cm}p{6.8cm}@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Lec.} & \textbf{Title} & \textbf{Key Concepts}\\
\midrule
L01 & Fock Space & Occupation number; creation/annihilation; Jordan--Wigner; field operators\\
L02 & Operators in 2nd Quantisation & One- and two-body operators; normal ordering; Wick\'s theorem\\
L03 & Homogeneous Electron Gas & Jellium; Fermi sea; HF exchange; Lindhard; Friedel; plasmon\\
L04 & HF in 2nd Quantisation & Mean-field decoupling; Brillouin; Koopman; HFB; Nambu\\
L05 & Beyond Mean Field & CI; MP2; Goldstone diagrams; linked cluster; GW; RPA\\
L06 & Green's Functions I & Retarded GF; Lehmann representation; spectral function; Galitskii--Migdal\\
\midrule
L07 & Green's Functions II & Dyson equation; HF and GW self-energies; quasiparticle weight\\
L08 & Interacting Bosons: BEC & Bogoliubov transformation; Goldstone; Landau criterion; vortices\\
L09 & Interacting Fermions: BCS & Cooper instability; gap equation; Bogoliubov--Valatin; BCS--BEC\\
L10 & The Hubbard Model & Tight-binding; Mott insulator; superexchange; DMFT\\
L11 & Quantum Magnetism & Heisenberg model; Holstein--Primakoff; magnons; frustrated magnets\\
L12 & Towards Non-Equilibrium & Keldysh motivation; Floquet theory; driven-dissipative balance\\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
}

\subsubsection*{Lecture-by-Lecture Syllabi}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Module II.4 Lecture Syllabi}

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.4 / L01: Fock Space and Second Quantisation}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Fock space $\mathcal{F}=\bigoplus_{N=0}^\infty\mathcal{H}^{(N)}$; vacuum; (20--50~min) Bosons $[\hat{a}_i,\hat{a}_j^\dagger]=\delta_{ij}$; fermions $\{\hat{c}_i,\hat{c}_j^\dagger\}=\delta_{ij}$; Pauli exclusion from $\hat{c}^2=0$; occupation basis; (50--70~min) Many-body states from creation operators; inner products; comparison with Slater determinants; Jordan--Wigner string; (70--90~min) Field operators $\hat\psi(\mathbf{r})=\sum_k\phi_k\hat{c}_k$; density operator $\hat{n}(\mathbf{r})=\hat\psi^\dagger\hat\psi$.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Construct Fock space and define creation/annihilation operators.
  \item Show Pauli exclusion from fermionic anti-commutation.
  \item Write many-body states as products of creation operators.
  \item Define field operators and their (anti-)commutation relations.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- $\hat{a}\hat{a}^\dagger\ket{n}$; verify Pauli from $\hat{c}^2=0$; write $\ket{1,0,1,0}$.
Set~B --- Jordan--Wigner derivation; field operator commutation.
Projects: (simple) boson vs.\ fermion occupation statistics; (complex) Jordan--Wigner for 1D spin chain: map to free fermions.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.4 / L02: Operators in Second Quantisation}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) One-body: $\hat{T}=\sum_{ij}t_{ij}\hat{c}_i^\dagger\hat{c}_j$; kinetic energy; external potential; (20--45~min) Two-body: $\hat{V}=\tfrac{1}{2}\sum_{ijkl}V_{ijkl}\hat{c}_i^\dagger\hat{c}_j^\dagger\hat{c}_l\hat{c}_k$; Coulomb interaction; normal ordering; Wick's theorem; (45--65~min) Contractions; compute $\langle\hat{T}\rangle,\langle\hat{V}\rangle$ in Slater determinant; (65--90~min) Generalised Wick; Isserlis theorem; Feynman diagrams as Wick contractions.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Write one- and two-body operators in second quantisation.
  \item Apply Wick's theorem to evaluate expectation values.
  \item Draw Feynman diagrams as Wick contractions.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- one-body Hamiltonian; $\langle\hat{V}\rangle$ in HF by Wick.
Set~B --- prove Wick for 4-operator product; generalised Wick for BCS state.
Projects: (simple) Wick contraction calculator; (complex) Wick-based HF energy: all diagrams.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.4 / L03: The Homogeneous Electron Gas}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Jellium model; Hamiltonian components; (20--45~min) Fermi sea; $k_F=(3\pi^2n)^{1/3}$; kinetic energy; (45--65~min) HF exchange energy $E_{\rm ex}=-\tfrac{3e^2k_F}{4\pi}$; correlation energy; $r_s$ parameter; Gell-Mann--Brueckner high-density limit; (65--90~min) Lindhard dielectric function; Thomas--Fermi screening; plasmon; Friedel oscillations.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Set up jellium model and compute HF exchange energy.
  \item Define correlation energy and describe its $r_s$ dependence.
  \item Derive Thomas--Fermi screening and identify the plasmon.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- $k_F,E_F$; HF exchange energy; Gell-Mann--Brueckner high-density limit.
Set~B --- Lindhard function at $q\to0$; plasmon dispersion.
Projects: (simple) HEG energy vs.\ $r_s$; (complex) Lindhard dielectric function and Friedel oscillations.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.4 / L04: Hartree--Fock in Second Quantisation}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) HF ansatz; variational principle; orbital rotations; (20--45~min) Mean-field decoupling; Fock matrix; Brillouin's theorem; Koopman's theorem; (45--65~min) SCF density matrix idempotency; symmetry breaking; (65--90~min) HFB generalisation; pairing; BCS as HFB; Bogoliubov transformation in Nambu space.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Derive HF mean-field decoupling and prove Brillouin's theorem.
  \item Describe the HFB generalisation and BCS connection.
  \item Perform a Bogoliubov transformation in Nambu space.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- mean-field decoupling; Brillouin theorem check.
Set~B --- Thouless stability; Bogoliubov transformation: diagonalise HFB matrix.
Projects: (simple) HF for Hubbard dimer; (complex) HFB pairing: gap equation.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.4 / L05: Beyond Mean Field --- MP2, Diagrams, and Resummations}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Correlation energy; CI; size inconsistency; (20--45~min) MBPT: MP2 $E^{(2)}=\sum_{ia,jb}\tfrac{|\langle\Phi_{ij}^{ab}|\hat{V}|\Phi_0\rangle|^2}{E_0-E_{ij}^{ab}}$; Goldstone diagrams; (45--65~min) Linked-cluster theorem; MP2 as two Goldstone diagrams; MP3; Dyson equation; (65--90~min) GW: screened interaction $W=v/(1-vP)$; self-consistent GW; RPA as ring-diagram sum; connection to TDDFT.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Compute MP2 energy and draw its Goldstone diagrams.
  \item State the linked-cluster theorem.
  \item Describe GW and RPA as diagrammatic resummations.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- MP2 for H$_2$; two Goldstone diagrams; size-consistency check.
Set~B --- linked-cluster derivation; Dyson equation from self-energy.
Projects: (simple) MP2 correlation energy vs.\ basis size; (complex) RPA correlation energy for HEG.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.4 / L06: Green's Functions I}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Retarded GF $G^R(t)=-i\theta(t)\langle\{\hat{c}(t),\hat{c}^\dagger(0)\}\rangle$; (20--50~min) Lehmann representation; spectral function $A(k,\omega)=-2\text{Im}G^R$; poles at ionisation/affinity energies; (50--70~min) Non-interacting GF; quasiparticle peak; incoherent background; $Z_k$; lifetime; (70--90~min) Observables: Galitskii--Migdal; DOS; momentum distribution.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Define retarded GF and derive the Lehmann representation.
  \item Interpret poles as ionisation/affinity energies.
  \item Compute spectral function and DOS for a non-interacting system.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- non-interacting GF; spectral function; DOS for HEG.
Set~B --- Lehmann representation; Galitskii--Migdal energy.
Projects: (simple) spectral function: non-interacting to quasiparticle; (complex) Lehmann from CI eigenvalues of a cluster.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.4 / L07: Green's Functions II --- Dyson Equation}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Self-energy $\Sigma$ via Dyson $G=G_0+G_0\Sigma G$; (20--45~min) HF self-energy diagrams; GW: $\Sigma^{GW}=iGW$; $W=v/(1-vP)$; (45--65~min) Quasiparticle equation; $Z_k=[1-\partial_\omega\text{Re}\Sigma]^{-1}$; lifetime $\tau^{-1}=-2Z_k\text{Im}\Sigma$; (65--90~min) $G_0W_0$ band gaps; ARPES; self-consistent GW.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Derive Dyson equation and compute HF and GW self-energies.
  \item Solve quasiparticle equation; compute $Z_k$ and lifetime.
  \item Describe $G_0W_0$ accuracy for band gaps.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- HF and GW diagrams; $Z_k$ for model self-energy; DOS from $G$.
Set~B --- Dyson derivation; prove $Z_k\leq1$; lifetime from Im$\Sigma$.
Projects: (simple) model spectral function: QP peak + satellite; (complex) $G_0W_0$ band gap for Si.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.4 / L08: Interacting Bosons and BEC}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Weakly interacting Bose gas; BEC: $\hat{a}_0\approx\sqrt{N_0}$; (20--50~min) Bogoliubov transformation; dispersion $E_k=\sqrt{\varepsilon_k(\varepsilon_k+2gn_0)}$; phonon mode; Goldstone; (50--70~min) Depletion; Lee--Huang--Yang; Landau criterion; two-fluid model; (70--90~min) Quantised vortices; BKT in 2D; GP equation; experimental realisations.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Perform Bogoliubov transformation and derive dispersion.
  \item Identify Goldstone mode and explain Landau criterion.
  \item Describe vortices and GP equation.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- Bogoliubov spectrum; depletion; Landau critical velocity.
Set~B --- Bogoliubov derivation; Goldstone: $E_k\propto k$.
Projects: (simple) Bogoliubov dispersion vs.\ free particle; (complex) GP vortex solution and energy.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.4 / L09: Interacting Fermions and BCS Theory}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Cooper instability; exponential binding energy $E_B\sim-2\hbar\omega_D e^{-1/\lambda}$; (20--50~min) BCS wavefunction; gap equation $\Delta_k=-\sum_{k'}V_{kk'}\tfrac{\Delta_{k'}}{2E_{k'}}$; quasiparticle energy $E_k=\sqrt{\xi_k^2+|\Delta_k|^2}$; (50--70~min) Bogoliubov--Valatin transformation; condensation energy; Meissner effect; (70--90~min) BCS--BEC crossover; Feshbach resonance; unitary Fermi gas; cold atoms.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Derive Cooper pairing and the gap equation.
  \item Perform the Bogoliubov--Valatin transformation.
  \item Describe BCS--BEC crossover.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- Cooper binding energy; gap equation at $T=0$; quasiparticle spectrum.
Set~B --- derive gap equation; Bogoliubov--Valatin derivation.
Projects: (simple) BCS gap vs.\ coupling $\lambda$; (complex) BCS--BEC crossover: quasiparticle spectrum vs.\ $1/k_Fa_s$.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.4 / L10: The Hubbard Model}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Tight-binding + Hubbard $U$; Hamiltonian; (20--45~min) Half-filling: non-interacting metal; Mott insulator at large $U$; spectral weight transfer; (45--65~min) Limits: $U\to0$ (perturbation theory); $U\to\infty$ (Heisenberg/$t$--$J$); magnetic phase diagram; Stoner criterion; (65--90~min) Exact 1D solution (Bethe ansatz); spinon--holon separation; DMFT; high-$T_c$ cuprates.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Write the Hubbard Hamiltonian and describe its two limiting cases.
  \item Explain the Mott insulator and derive the Heisenberg model.
  \item Describe DMFT and connections to high-$T_c$.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- tight-binding band; Mott gap; Stoner criterion.
Set~B --- superexchange derivation ($t$--$J$ model); Mott transition.
Projects: (simple) Hubbard dimer: exact vs.\ HF; (complex) DMFT self-consistency for Bethe lattice.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.4 / L11: Quantum Magnetism}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Heisenberg model $J\sum\hat{\mathbf{S}}_i\cdot\hat{\mathbf{S}}_j$; mean-field; (20--45~min) Holstein--Primakoff: $\hat{S}^+\approx\sqrt{2S}\hat{a}$; magnon dispersion $\omega_k=4JS(1-\gamma_k)$; Goldstone at $k=0$; (45--65~min) AFM: two-sublattice; Bogoliubov transformation; zero-point fluctuations; Mermin--Wagner in 1D; (65--90~min) Frustrated magnets; quantum spin liquids; Kitaev honeycomb: exact solution via Majorana fermions.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Apply Holstein--Primakoff and derive magnon dispersion.
  \item Explain zero-point fluctuations in AFM and Mermin--Wagner.
  \item Describe frustrated magnets and quantum spin liquids.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- magnon dispersion for FM; mean-field $T_c$; AFM zero-point fluctuation.
Set~B --- AFM Bogoliubov transformation; Mermin--Wagner sketch.
Projects: (simple) magnon dispersion for 1D/2D FM; (complex) AFM spin-wave theory: zero-point reduction vs.\ dimension.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.4 / L12: Towards Non-Equilibrium}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Limitations of equilibrium: laser-driven systems, biased junctions, periodic drives; (20--45~min) Keldysh contour motivation; closed-time-path; contour-ordered GF; (45--65~min) Floquet theory: $\ket{\psi(t)}=e^{-i\varepsilon t/\hbar}\ket{u(t)}$; quasi-energies; effective Floquet Hamiltonian from Magnus; (65--90~min) Driven-dissipative steady states; Lindblad from Keldysh limit; Floquet topological insulators; time-crystalline order.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Explain the Keldysh contour and its relation to real-time GFs.
  \item State Floquet's theorem and derive the effective Hamiltonian.
  \item Describe driven-dissipative steady states.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- Keldysh contour GF relations; Floquet quasi-energies for two-level system.
Set~B --- Magnus expansion for Floquet Hamiltonian; Lindblad steady-state derivation.
Projects: (simple) Floquet quasi-energy spectrum for driven TLS; (complex) Floquet engineering of Haldane model from driven graphene.
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[highlightbox]
\textbf{Module II.4 Reading:} Fetter \& Walecka, \textit{Quantum Theory of Many-Particle Systems}; Bruus \& Flensberg, \textit{Introduction to Many-Body QT in Condensed Matter}; Altland \& Simons, \textit{Condensed Matter Field Theory}; Auerbach, \textit{Interacting Electrons and Quantum Magnetism}.
\end{tcolorbox}

%=============================================================
\subsection{Module II.5 --- Non-Equilibrium Quantum Many-Body Green's Functions}
\label{sec:mod-II5}
%=============================================================

\subsubsection*{Module Overview}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Module II.5 Overview}

{\footnotesize
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lp{4.2cm}p{6.8cm}@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Lec.} & \textbf{Title} & \textbf{Key Concepts}\\
\midrule
L01 & Motivation and Scope & Transport; ultrafast; driven systems; failure of equilibrium MBPT\\
L02 & The Keldysh Contour & CTP; forward/backward branches; contour ordering; generating functional\\
L03 & Contour Green's Functions & $G^c,G^<,G^>,G^R,G^A,G^K$; LO matrix; FDT; Matsubara limit\\
L04 & Langreth Rules & Analytic continuation; convolution identities; GW and 2B self-energies\\
L05 & Kadanoff--Baym Equations & EOM; two-time structure; $\Phi$-derivable; conserving approximations\\
L06 & Self-Energies & HF; GW; second Born; T-matrix; KB conservation theorem\\
\midrule
L07 & Quantum Boltzmann Equation & Wigner transform; gradient expansion; collision integral; Drude\\
L08 & Steady-State Transport & Meir--Wingreen; Landauer; Kondo; IETS; shot noise\\
L09 & Electron--Phonon Coupling & Fr\"ohlich; Fan--Migdal; polaron; Eliashberg; $T_c$\\
L10 & Pump--Probe Dynamics & Time-resolved spectral function; Peierls; tr-ARPES; thermalisation\\
L11 & Driven-Dissipative Systems & Lindblad from NEGF; Floquet--Keldysh; NESS; polaritons\\
L12 & Numerical NEGF & Time-stepping KB; GKBA; NESSi; ML surrogate self-energies\\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
}

\subsubsection*{Lecture-by-Lecture Syllabi}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Module II.5 Lecture Syllabi}

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.5 / L01: Motivation and Scope of NEGF}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Paradigmatic non-equilibrium situations: molecular junctions under bias; laser-driven solids; open quantum systems; (20--45~min) Why equilibrium MBPT fails: adiabatic switching; no transient dynamics; (45--65~min) Survey of formalisms: Redfield/Lindblad (Markovian); TDCI (exponential); NEGF (systematically improvable); (65--90~min) Key observables: $I(t)$; non-equilibrium spectral function; tr-ARPES; entanglement entropy from NEGF.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Identify physical situations requiring non-equilibrium treatment.
  \item Explain why Matsubara MBPT fails for driven systems.
  \item Compare Lindblad, TDCI, and NEGF in accuracy and cost.
  \item List observables accessible from the NEGF.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- identify equilibrium vs.\ non-equilibrium scenarios; match formalism to problem.
Set~B --- limitations of Matsubara: why adiabatic switching fails.
Projects: (simple) scenario classification exercise; (complex) NEGF vs.\ TDDFT comparison for driven quantum dot.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.5 / L02: The Keldysh Contour}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) CTP $\mathcal{C}=\mathcal{C}^+\cup\mathcal{C}^-$; motivation from $\langle\hat{O}(t)\rangle=\operatorname{Tr}[\hat{U}(t_0,t)\hat{O}\hat{U}(t,t_0)\hat\rho_0]$; (20--45~min) Contour-ordering $T_\mathcal{C}$; contour-ordered GF $G^c=-i\langle T_\mathcal{C}\hat{c}(t)\hat{c}^\dagger(t')\rangle$; (45--65~min) Perturbation theory on contour; Wick's theorem; (65--90~min) Keldysh generating functional; Schwinger--Dyson equations.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Construct the CTP contour and justify its necessity.
  \item Define contour ordering and the contour GF.
  \item Apply Wick's theorem on the Keldysh contour.
  \item Derive GFs as functional derivatives of the generating functional.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- contour ordering examples; $G^c$ for non-interacting system.
Set~B --- Wick on contour; Keldysh action for free fermions.
Projects: (simple) diagrammatic free-fermion GF on Keldysh contour; (complex) Keldysh generating functional: $G^<$ and $G^>$ as derivatives.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.5 / L03: Contour-Ordered Green's Functions}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Six real-time GFs from contour decomposition: $G^c,G^{\bar c},G^<,G^>,G^R,G^A$; (20--45~min) Keldysh GF $G^K=G^<+G^>$; Larkin--Ovchinnikov (LO) matrix $\hat{G}=\begin{pmatrix}G^R&G^K\\0&G^A\end{pmatrix}$; causality; (45--65~min) FDT at equilibrium: $G^K=(1-2f)(G^R-G^A)$; Lehmann for $G^R$ and $G^<$; (65--90~min) Analytic continuation Keldysh$\to$Matsubara; connection at equilibrium.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Define all six real-time GFs and state their relations.
  \item Construct the LO matrix representation.
  \item Derive the FDT from Keldysh formalism.
  \item Connect Keldysh GFs to Matsubara GF at equilibrium.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- $G^R,G^<,G^>$ for non-interacting fermion; verify FDT.
Set~B --- LO matrix algebra; analytic continuation to Matsubara.
Projects: (simple) GF component visualiser at various temperatures; (complex) LO Dyson equation for model self-energy.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.5 / L04: Langreth Rules}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Need for Langreth rules: contour convolutions in real time; (20--50~min) Basic rules: $C^R=A^R B^R$; $C^<=A^R B^<+A^< B^A$; $C^K=A^R B^K+A^K B^A$; $n$-fold generalisations; (50--70~min) Mixed products for vertex corrections; (70--90~min) GW self-energy $\Sigma^R=iG^RW^<+iG^<W^R$; second-Born $\Sigma^<=i^2G^<G^<G^>$; T-matrix.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item State and derive Langreth rules for contour convolutions.
  \item Apply rules to convert contour diagrams to real-time expressions.
  \item Derive real-time GW and second-Born self-energies.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- apply Langreth rules to product of two GFs; HF self-energy in real time.
Set~B --- GW $\Sigma^{R,<}$ from Langreth; verify equilibrium FDT.
Projects: (simple) Langreth rule calculator; (complex) second-Born $\Sigma^{R,<}$: verify FDT at equilibrium.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.5 / L05: Kadanoff--Baym Equations}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) EOM for $G^c(t,t')$: apply $i\partial_t$; (20--50~min) KB equations for $G^<$ and $G^R$; two-time integro-differential structure; initial conditions; (50--65~min) Matsubara track for correlated initial states; (65--90~min) $\Phi$-derivable conserving approximations: $\Sigma=\delta\Phi/\delta G$; KB conservation theorem.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Write the KB equations for $G^R$ and $G^<$.
  \item Explain two-time structure and initial conditions.
  \item Define conserving approximations via the $\Phi$-functional.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- EOM for $G^<$; particle conservation for HF self-energy.
Set~B --- derive KB from $\Phi$-functional; conserving approximation check.
Projects: (simple) KB for two-level system: exact vs.\ HF; (complex) energy conservation in KB with second-Born for quantum dot.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.5 / L06: Self-Energies and Conserving Approximations}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Self-energy hierarchy from $\Phi$-functional; HF $\Phi_{\rm HF}$; (20--45~min) GW: $\Phi_{\rm GW}=-\tfrac{i}{2}\operatorname{Tr}[\ln(1-vP)]$; $W=v+vPW$; $\Sigma^{\rm GW}=iGW$; $\mathcal{O}(N^3)$/step; (45--65~min) Second Born: $\Sigma^{\rm 2B}=i^2VGGV+\text{exchange}$; T-matrix: ladder resummation; (65--90~min) Comparison: accuracy vs.\ cost; benchmark vs.\ TDCI; KB conservation theorem.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Derive GW, second-Born, and T-matrix from $\Phi$-functionals.
  \item State the KB conservation theorem.
  \item Compare self-energy approximations in accuracy and scaling.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- HF and GW diagrams; identify conserving vs.\ non-conserving.
Set~B --- $\Phi$ derivation of GW; KB conservation theorem proof.
Projects: (simple) GW vs.\ HF spectral function for Hubbard dimer; (complex) benchmark GW vs.\ 2B vs.\ exact.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.5 / L07: Quantum Boltzmann Equation}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Wigner transform: $T=(t+t')/2$, $\omega\leftrightarrow t-t'$; $G(T,\omega)$; (20--45~min) Gradient expansion of KB; QBE: $\partial_T f+\mathbf{v}_k\cdot\nabla f+\mathbf{F}\cdot\partial_k f=I_{\rm coll}[f]$; Wigner distribution $f(T,\mathbf{k})=G^</(2\pi)$; (45--65~min) Collision integral from self-energy; Born approximation; H-theorem; (65--90~min) Drude conductivity; electron--phonon scattering; relaxation-time approximation; beyond Born.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Perform Wigner transform and gradient expansion of KB equations.
  \item Derive the QBE and identify the collision integral.
  \item Compute Drude conductivity from the QBE.
  \item State the H-theorem and entropy production.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- Wigner transform of $G^<$; Drude from RTA.
Set~B --- gradient expansion of KB; collision integral from Born self-energy.
Projects: (simple) Boltzmann relaxation to equilibrium; (complex) electron--phonon QBE: $T$-dependent resistivity.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.5 / L08: Steady-State Transport}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Nanojunction: central region + leads L,R at $\mu_L,\mu_R$; (20--50~min) Meir--Wingreen formula; embedding self-energy $\Sigma^R_{L/R}$; broadening $\Gamma_{L/R}$; Landauer non-interacting limit: $T(\omega)=\operatorname{Tr}[\Gamma_L G^R\Gamma_R G^A]$; (50--70~min) Kondo effect; IETS; shot noise; Fano factor; (70--90~min) Experimental comparison: STM break junction; mechanically controlled break junction.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Derive the Meir--Wingreen formula.
  \item Obtain the Landauer formula in the non-interacting limit.
  \item Compute transmission for a molecular junction.
  \item Describe Kondo effect and IETS.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- Landauer for single-channel wire; transmission for resonant level.
Set~B --- Meir--Wingreen derivation; Kondo temperature estimate.
Projects: (simple) Landauer transmission: conductance vs.\ gate voltage; (complex) Meir--Wingreen for Anderson model: interacting vs.\ non-interacting.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.5 / L09: Electron--Phonon Coupling}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Fr\"ohlich Hamiltonian $\hat{H}_{\rm el-ph}=\sum_{kq}g_{kq}\hat{c}^\dagger_{k+q}\hat{c}_k(\hat{b}_q+\hat{b}^\dagger_{-q})$; (20--45~min) Fan--Migdal electron self-energy; phonon self-energy from electrons; (45--65~min) Polaron: Fr\"ohlich effective mass; Holstein small polaron; Lang--Firsov; (65--90~min) Eliashberg theory: $\alpha^2F(\omega)$; $\lambda=2\int d\omega\alpha^2F/\omega$; McMillan $T_c$; comparison to BCS.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Write the Fr\"ohlich Hamiltonian and derive Fan--Migdal self-energy.
  \item Describe the polaron and compute its effective mass.
  \item Explain Eliashberg theory and the phonon contribution to $T_c$.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- Fr\"ohlich coupling; electron lifetime; Drude resistivity.
Set~B --- Fan--Migdal self-energy derivation; large polaron effective mass.
Projects: (simple) electron spectral function renormalisation from phonons; (complex) Eliashberg $T_c$ from ab initio $\alpha^2F$.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.5 / L10: Pump--Probe Dynamics}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Femtosecond pump--probe; time-resolved ARPES; transient absorption; (20--45~min) Non-equilibrium spectral function $A(T,\omega)$; Wigner-transformed $G^<$; time-energy uncertainty; (45--65~min) KB equations for pump-driven system; Peierls substitution; photo-excited $f(T,\mathbf{k})$; (65--90~min) Relaxation: electron--electron thermalisation; electron--phonon cooling; Auger recombination; comparison to experiment.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Define time-resolved spectral function and relate to tr-ARPES.
  \item Set up KB equations for a laser-driven solid.
  \item Describe the hierarchy of relaxation processes after photo-excitation.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- non-equilibrium $f(\mathbf{k},T)$ after Gaussian pulse; energy conservation check.
Set~B --- Peierls substitution derivation; KB for driven two-band model.
Projects: (simple) two-band model: population dynamics after laser pulse; (complex) tr-ARPES simulation for driven graphene.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.5 / L11: Driven-Dissipative Systems}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Open quantum systems: Markovian bath; Lindblad from NEGF by tracing out bath; (20--45~min) Bath self-energy gives imaginary contribution; jump operators from bath spectral function; (45--65~min) Floquet--Keldysh: periodic drive + bath; NESS from Dyson equation; (65--90~min) Polariton condensation; quantum synchronisation; Floquet topological states; time-crystalline order.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Derive Lindblad by integrating out a Markovian bath in NEGF.
  \item Set up Floquet--Keldysh GF for a periodically driven open system.
  \item Compute NESS from the Dyson equation.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- Lindblad from bath self-energy; NESS for two-level system.
Set~B --- Floquet--Keldysh GF structure; NESS for driven resonant level.
Projects: (simple) NESS occupation for driven-dissipative resonant level; (complex) Floquet--Keldysh NESS for driven Haldane model.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.5 / L12: Numerical Methods for NEGF}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Computational challenge: 2D time grid $\mathcal{O}(N_T^2N_k^2)$ memory; $\mathcal{O}(N_T^3N_k^3)$ cost; (20--45~min) Predictor--corrector (Adams--Bashforth--Moulton); stability; parallelisation; (45--65~min) GKBA: $G^<(t,t')\approx G^R(t,t')\rho(t')-\rho(t)G^A(t,t')$; $\mathcal{O}(N_TN_k^3)$; accuracy vs.\ full KB; (65--90~min) NESSi library; GPU acceleration; ML surrogate self-energies; benchmark vs.\ TDCI.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Explain the computational cost of KB equations on a 2D time grid.
  \item Describe the predictor--corrector algorithm for KB.
  \item Derive the GKBA and state its accuracy and cost advantage.
  \item Outline NESSi software and ML-based acceleration.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- scaling analysis; GKBA for driven two-level system.
Set~B --- predictor--corrector derivation; stability analysis.
Projects: (simple) full KB vs.\ GKBA for driven HO: accuracy and cost; (complex) GPU-accelerated KB for Hubbard dimer: scaling benchmarks.
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[highlightbox]
\textbf{Module II.5 Reading:} Stefanucci \& van Leeuwen, \textit{Nonequilibrium Many-Body Theory of Quantum Systems} (Cambridge, 2013); Kadanoff \& Baym, \textit{Quantum Statistical Mechanics}; Haug \& Jauho, \textit{Quantum Kinetics in Transport and Optics of Semiconductors}.
\end{tcolorbox}

%=============================================================
\subsection{Module II.6 --- Light--Matter Interaction, Linear Response, and Spectroscopy}
\label{sec:mod-II6}
%=============================================================

\subsubsection*{Module Overview}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Module II.6 Overview}

{\footnotesize
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lp{4.2cm}p{6.8cm}@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Lec.} & \textbf{Title} & \textbf{Key Concepts}\\
\midrule
L01 & Classical and Quantum EM Fields & Coulomb gauge; mode expansion; photon; vacuum fluctuations\\
L02 & Light--Matter Coupling & Minimal coupling; dipole approximation; PZW; RWA; strong field\\
L03 & Linear Response \& Kubo Formula & Retarded susceptibility; causality; Kramers--Kronig\\
L04 & Fluctuation--Dissipation Theorem & FDT; Johnson--Nyquist; quantum noise; effective temperature\\

\midrule

\bottomrule
\end{tabular}

\subsubsection*{Lecture-by-Lecture Syllabi}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Module II.6 Lecture Syllabi}

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.6 / L01: Classical and Quantum Electromagnetic Fields}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Maxwell; Coulomb gauge $\nabla\cdot\mathbf{A}=0$; transverse/longitudinal; (20--45~min) Mode expansion; quantisation $[\hat{a}_{\mathbf{k}\lambda},\hat{a}^\dagger_{\mathbf{k}'\lambda'}]=\delta_{\mathbf{k}\mathbf{k}'}\delta_{\lambda\lambda'}$; photon; (45--65~min) Vacuum fluctuations $\langle0|\hat{\mathbf{E}}^2|0\rangle\neq0$; Casimir effect; (65--90~min) Coherent states; Fock vs.\ coherent vs.\ thermal; Glauber--Sudarshan $P$-function; $g^{(1)},g^{(2)}$.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Quantise the EM field in Coulomb gauge.
  \item Define photon operators and number states.
  \item Explain vacuum fluctuations and the Casimir effect.
  \item Distinguish coherent, Fock, and thermal states.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- EM energy in photon numbers; vacuum $\langle E^2\rangle$; Casimir force.
Set~B --- commutation relations from canonical quantisation; $g^{(2)}$ for coherent vs.\ Fock.
Projects: (simple) Casimir force vs.\ plate separation; (complex) Wigner function of single-photon Fock state.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.6 / L02: Light--Matter Coupling}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Minimal coupling $\hat{H}=\tfrac{1}{2m}(\hat{\mathbf{p}}-e\mathbf{A})^2+V$; expand to linear in $\mathbf{A}$; (20--45~min) Dipole approximation; length and velocity gauges; gauge equivalence via unitary transformation; (45--65~min) Power--Zienau--Woolley transformation; multipolar Hamiltonian; $E1,M1,E2$; (65--90~min) Strong field: beyond dipole; Floquet; RWA; driven two-level system.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Derive light--matter interaction from minimal coupling.
  \item Apply dipole approximation and verify gauge equivalence.
  \item Describe PZW transformation and multipolar Hamiltonian.
  \item Apply RWA to a driven two-level system.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- expand minimal coupling; dipole approximation; RWA for TLS.
Set~B --- gauge equivalence proof; PZW transformation.
Projects: (simple) Rabi oscillations: exact vs.\ RWA; (complex) Bloch--Siegert shift beyond RWA.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.6 / L03: Linear Response Theory and the Kubo Formula}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Linear response: $\langle\delta\hat{B}(t)\rangle=\int\chi_{BA}(t-t')F(t')dt'$; (20--50~min) Kubo formula: $\chi_{BA}(t)=-i\theta(t)\langle[\hat{B}(t),\hat{A}(0)]\rangle_0$; causality $\Rightarrow$ upper-half analyticity; Kramers--Kronig relations; (50--70~min) Physical examples: dielectric, magnetic, optical conductivity; density--density response; (70--90~min) Wiener--Khinchin: Im$\,\chi^R$ from equilibrium fluctuations.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Derive the Kubo formula for retarded susceptibility.
  \item Apply causality to derive Kramers--Kronig.
  \item Compute optical conductivity from current--current Kubo.
  \item Connect Im$\,\chi^R$ to fluctuations via Wiener--Khinchin.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- $\chi^R(\omega)$ for damped HO; Kramers--Kronig check.
Set~B --- Kubo derivation from TDPT; $f$-sum rule from commutator.
Projects: (simple) KK verification for Lorentzian; (complex) optical conductivity for tight-binding chain from Kubo.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.6 / L04: The Fluctuation--Dissipation Theorem}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) FDT: $S_{BA}(\omega)=2\hbar n_B(\omega)\text{Im}\,\chi^R_{BA}(\omega)$; (20--45~min) Derivation from Lehmann: detailed balance; classical limit $\hbar\omega\ll k_BT$; (45--65~min) Johnson--Nyquist noise $S_V=4k_BTR$; dissipation from noise; (65--90~min) Quantum noise; standard quantum limit; back-action; quantum optomechanics; FDT in non-equilibrium: effective temperature.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item State the FDT and derive it from the Lehmann representation.
  \item Apply FDT to derive Johnson--Nyquist noise.
  \item Discuss FDT in non-equilibrium: effective temperature.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- FDT for RC circuit; Johnson--Nyquist noise; classical limit.
Set~B --- Lehmann derivation; FDT for non-interacting fermion.
Projects: (simple) FDT verification: numerical dynamics vs.\ Im$\,\chi^R$; (complex) effective temperature from FDT in non-equilibrium electron gas.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.6 / L05: Optical Conductivity and the $f$-Sum Rule}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) $\sigma(\omega)$ from current--current Kubo; Re$\,\sigma(\omega)$=power absorbed; (20--45~min) Drude from Kubo; $\sigma_{\rm Drude}=\tfrac{ne^2}{m}\tfrac{1}{\gamma-i\omega}$; Drude--Lorentz; (45--65~min) $f$-sum rule: $\int_0^\infty\text{Re}\,\sigma\,d\omega=\tfrac{\pi ne^2}{2m}$; derivation from $[\hat{H},\hat{j}]$; (65--90~min) Ellipsometry; KK analysis; Drude weight; superfluid density; Mott insulator gap.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Derive optical conductivity from current--current Kubo.
  \item Obtain Drude and Drude--Lorentz models.
  \item Prove and apply the $f$-sum rule.
  \item Interpret reflectance spectra via KK analysis.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- Drude parameters from spectrum; $f$-sum rule numerical check.
Set~B --- $f$-sum derivation from Kubo; KK analysis of reflectance.
Projects: (simple) Drude--Lorentz fit to metal optical conductivity; (complex) superfluid density from spectral weight: BCS vs.\ cuprate.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.6 / L06: Absorption, Emission, and Einstein Coefficients}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Fermi's golden rule: $\Gamma_{i\to f}=\tfrac{2\pi}{\hbar}|\bra{f}\hat{H}'\ket{i}|^2\rho(E_f)$; (20--45~min) Einstein: $A_{21},B_{12},B_{21}$; relations $A_{21}=\tfrac{\hbar\omega^3}{\pi^2c^3}B_{21}$; Planck from detailed balance; (45--65~min) Spontaneous emission from QED: $\Gamma_{\rm sp}=\tfrac{e^2\omega^3}{3\pi\epsilon_0\hbar c^3}|d_{fi}|^2$; natural linewidth; (65--90~min) Line shapes: Lorentzian (lifetime); Gaussian (Doppler); Voigt; power broadening.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Apply Fermi's golden rule to compute absorption cross sections.
  \item Define Einstein coefficients and derive their relation.
  \item Compute spontaneous emission rate from first principles.
  \item Describe physical origins of line shapes.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- Einstein $A$ for H Lyman-$\alpha$; $B_{12}$ from $A_{21}$; natural linewidth.
Set~B --- spontaneous emission from minimal coupling; Wigner--Weisskopf sketch.
Projects: (simple) absorption spectrum vs.\ line shape parameters; (complex) Purcell factor: cavity modification of $A_{21}$.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.6 / L07: Selection Rules}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Selection rules from AM conservation; $\Delta m=0,\pm1$; (20--45~min) $E1$ from W-E: $\Delta l=\pm1$; parity change; Laporte rule; $\Delta j=0,\pm1$ (not $0\to0$); (45--65~min) $M1$: $\Delta l=0$, parity unchanged; $E2$: $\Delta l=0,\pm2$; competition; (65--90~min) Molecular selection rules: symmetry group; $\langle\psi_f|\hat\mu|\psi_i\rangle\neq0$ iff $\Gamma_f\otimes\Gamma_\mu\otimes\Gamma_i\supset A_1$; IR vs.\ Raman; mutual exclusion.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item State and apply $E1$ selection rules from W-E.
  \item Identify Laporte-forbidden transitions and higher-order mechanisms.
  \item Apply molecular symmetry to determine selection rules.
  \item Distinguish IR-active from Raman-active modes.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- allowed/forbidden for H $1s\to2s,2p,3d$; CO$_2$ IR modes.
Set~B --- $E2$ matrix element; group theory for $C_{2v}$ molecule.
Projects: (simple) atomic selection rule table; (complex) symmetry analysis of benzene normal modes: IR vs.\ Raman.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.6 / L08: Non-Linear Response}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) $\chi^{(2)}_{ijk}(\omega_1,\omega_2)$; $\chi^{(3)}$; (20--45~min) $\chi^{(2)}$: SHG; sum/difference frequency; optical rectification; phase matching; $\chi^{(2)}=0$ centrosymmetric; (45--65~min) $\chi^{(3)}$: TPA; FWM; self-phase modulation; solitons; (65--90~min) Ultrafast: transient absorption; 2DES; double-sided Feynman diagrams; rephasing vs.\ non-rephasing.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Define $\chi^{(2)}$ and $\chi^{(3)}$ and identify associated phenomena.
  \item Explain phase matching for SHG.
  \item Describe TPA, FWM, and transient absorption.
  \item Interpret double-sided Feynman diagrams for 2DES.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- SHG phase matching; $\chi^{(2)}=0$ for centrosymmetric; TPA cross-section.
Set~B --- $\chi^{(3)}$ from PT; Liouville pathway for TA.
Projects: (simple) SHG spectrum from phase-matching bandwidth; (complex) 2DES for coupled TLS: cross-peak identification.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.6 / L09: Time-Domain Spectroscopy}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) FID; NMR analogy; Fourier transform spectroscopy; (20--45~min) Photon echo: $\pi/2$--$\tau$--$\pi$; rephasing; inhomogeneous broadening removal; (45--65~min) Response from correlators: $\chi^R(t)\propto\theta(t)\langle[\hat\mu(t),\hat\mu(0)]\rangle$; $R^{(3)}$ as four-point correlator; (65--90~min) 2D IR; 2DES; waiting-time dynamics; quantum biology; energy transfer.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Explain FID and photon echo in terms of rephasing.
  \item Express linear and third-order response as correlators.
  \item Describe 2DES and interpret waiting-time dynamics.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- FID for TLS; photon echo timing; Fourier transform to spectrum.
Set~B --- derive $R^{(3)}$ as four-point correlator; rephasing vs.\ non-rephasing pathway.
Projects: (simple) 2DES for coupled TLS; (complex) 2D IR for Morse oscillator.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.6 / L10: Raman and Resonance Raman Spectroscopy}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Raman: Stokes/anti-Stokes; cross-section $\propto(\omega_i\pm\Omega)^4|\alpha|^2$; (20--45~min) Kramers--Heisenberg formula; resonance enhancement; (45--65~min) Vibronic coupling; Condon; Herzberg--Teller; Franck--Condon overlaps; (65--90~min) SERS; TERS; single-molecule SERS; graphene $G$ and $D$ bands; CARS microscopy.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Derive the Kramers--Heisenberg formula and identify resonance condition.
  \item Compute Raman intensities from Franck--Condon factors.
  \item Describe SERS, TERS, and CARS.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- Raman spectrum for diatomic; Stokes/anti-Stokes ratio; selection rule.
Set~B --- Kramers--Heisenberg derivation; Franck--Condon for displaced HO.
Projects: (simple) Raman spectrum of CO$_2$; (complex) resonance Raman intensity vs.\ excitation frequency.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.6 / L11: Photoelectron Spectroscopy}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) XPS/UPS: $E_B=h\nu-E_{\rm kin}-\phi$; Koopman's theorem; (20--45~min) Sudden approximation; spectral function $A(\omega)$ directly measured; shake-up/shake-off satellites; (45--65~min) Dyson orbital; pole strength = quasiparticle weight $Z$; (65--90~min) ARPES: $E_{\rm kin}(\theta,\phi)$ maps band structure; $\mathbf{k}$-resolved spectral function; matrix element effects; tr-ARPES.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Explain the sudden approximation and relate PES to spectral function.
  \item Define the Dyson orbital and quasiparticle weight.
  \item Interpret ARPES as $\mathbf{k}$-resolved spectral function.
  \item Identify shake-up satellites.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- binding energies from XPS; Koopman vs.\ $\Delta$SCF; satellite identification.
Set~B --- Dyson orbital derivation; quasiparticle weight from pole strength.
Projects: (simple) simulated ARPES for tight-binding band; (complex) Fermi liquid spectral function: QP peak and incoherent background.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.6 / L12: Cavity QED and Strong Light--Matter Coupling}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Cavity QED: three regimes ($\kappa,g,\gamma$); (20--45~min) Jaynes--Cummings: $\hat{H}_{\rm JC}=\hbar\omega_c\hat{a}^\dagger\hat{a}+\tfrac{\hbar\omega_0}{2}\hat\sigma_z+\hbar g(\hat{a}\hat\sigma_++\hat{a}^\dagger\hat\sigma_-)$; dressed states; vacuum Rabi splitting $2g$; (45--65~min) Polaritons: upper/lower branches; Hopfield coefficients; polariton condensation; (65--90~min) Ultra-strong coupling; photon blockade; circuit QED; quantum information applications.
\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Solve JC model and identify dressed states.
  \item Derive vacuum Rabi splitting and explain strong coupling.
  \item Describe polariton branches and Hopfield coefficients.
  \item Explain photon blockade and circuit QED.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- JC dressed states; Rabi splitting; photon blockade condition.
Set~B --- JC dynamics: collapse and revival; Hopfield coefficients.
Projects: (simple) JC dynamics: Fock vs.\ coherent state Rabi oscillations; (complex) polariton dispersion: upper/lower branches and Hopfield coefficients.
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[highlightbox]
\textbf{Module II.6 Reading:} Mukamel, \textit{Principles of Nonlinear Optical Spectroscopy}; Mandel \& Wolf, \textit{Optical Coherence and Quantum Optics}; Walls \& Milburn, \textit{Quantum Optics}; Atkins \& Friedman, \textit{Molecular Quantum Mechanics}.
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsection{Module II.7 --- Quantum Statistical Mechanics in Equilibrium}
\label{sec:mod-II7}
%=============================================================

%------------------------------------------------------------

{\footnotesize
