\subsubsection*{Lecture-by-Lecture Syllabi}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Module II.7 Lecture Syllabi}

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.7 / L01: Density Operators in Thermodynamics}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Statistical quantum mechanics: mixed states as ensembles; density operator $\hat\rho$; purity; thermal equilibrium state $\hat\rho=e^{-\beta\hat{H}}/Z$; (20--45~min) Partition function $Z=\operatorname{Tr}e^{-\beta\hat{H}}$; Helmholtz free energy $F=-k_BT\ln Z$; internal energy $U=-\partial_\beta\ln Z$; entropy $S=-k_B\operatorname{Tr}(\hat\rho\ln\hat\rho)$ (von Neumann); heat capacity $C_V$; (45--65~min) Maximum entropy principle: Jaynes' derivation --- maximise $S$ subject to $\operatorname{Tr}\hat\rho=1$ and $\operatorname{Tr}(\hat\rho\hat{H})=U$; Lagrange multipliers give Gibbs state; (65--90~min) Quantum information perspective: von Neumann entropy as entanglement entropy at zero temperature; relative entropy $S(\hat\rho\|\hat\sigma)=\operatorname{Tr}(\hat\rho\ln\hat\rho-\hat\rho\ln\hat\sigma)\geq 0$; trace distance; quantum thermodynamics preview.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Write the Gibbs state and compute $F,U,S,C_V$ from $Z$.
  \item Derive the Gibbs state from the maximum entropy principle.
  \item Define von Neumann entropy and compare with thermodynamic entropy.
  \item Evaluate relative entropy and trace distance for simple density matrices.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Dual-track content:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item \textit{Physical track:} Two-level system, harmonic oscillator, and spin-$\tfrac{1}{2}$ as paradigmatic examples; specific heat anomalies; Schottky anomaly.
  \item \textit{Quantum information track:} Von Neumann entropy as information content; Jaynes' maximum entropy as Bayesian inference; relative entropy as statistical distinguishability.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``thermal equilibrium is the state of maximum ignorance given the average energy.''
Beg.\ UG: $Z$ for two-level system; $F,U,S$; specific heat.
Adv.\ UG: maximum entropy derivation; von Neumann entropy; Gibbs state uniqueness.
MSc: relative entropy; trace distance; quantum thermodynamics (work extraction).
PhD: quantum fluctuation theorems (Jarzynski, Crooks); quantum heat engines; resource theory of thermodynamics.

\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- $Z$, $F$, $U$, $S$, $C_V$ for two-level system and HO; Schottky anomaly temperature.
Set~B --- Jaynes derivation of Gibbs state; von Neumann entropy of Gibbs state; relative entropy positivity proof.
Projects: (simple) $C_V(T)$ for two-level vs.\ HO: Schottky peak vs.\ Planck;
(complex) quantum Otto heat engine: efficiency from $Z$ of working fluid.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.7 / L02: Canonical and Grand-Canonical Ensembles}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Canonical ensemble: system in thermal contact with a reservoir; $Z_N=\operatorname{Tr}_Ne^{-\beta\hat{H}}$; grand canonical: additionally allows particle exchange; grand partition function $\Xi=\sum_{N=0}^\infty e^{\beta\mu N}Z_N=\operatorname{Tr}e^{-\beta(\hat{H}-\mu\hat{N})}$; (20--45~min) Grand potential $\Omega=-k_BT\ln\Xi$; mean particle number $\langle\hat{N}\rangle=-\partial\Omega/\partial\mu$; number fluctuations $\langle(\Delta N)^2\rangle=k_BT\partial\langle N\rangle/\partial\mu$; pressure $P=-\partial\Omega/\partial V$; Gibbs--Duhem relation $SdT+Vd P=Nd\mu$; (45--65~min) Deriving quantum statistics: single-mode grand canonical; Bose--Einstein $n_k=(e^{\beta(\varepsilon_k-\mu)}-1)^{-1}$; Fermi--Dirac $n_k=(e^{\beta(\varepsilon_k-\mu)}+1)^{-1}$; fugacity expansion; (65--90~min) Ensemble equivalence in the thermodynamic limit; corrections for finite systems; Yang--Lee theorem: zeros of $\Xi$ in the complex $z$-plane signal phase transitions; microcanonical saddle-point approximation.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Set up the grand canonical ensemble and derive thermodynamic relations.
  \item Derive BE and FD distributions from the single-mode grand canonical.
  \item State ensemble equivalence and identify its breakdown.
  \item Apply the Yang--Lee theorem to phase transitions.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``the chemical potential is the energy cost of adding one more particle.''
Beg.\ UG: grand canonical; BE/FD from single-mode; $\langle N\rangle$ vs.\ $\mu$.
Adv.\ UG: Gibbs--Duhem; ensemble equivalence; Yang--Lee zeros.
MSc: fugacity expansion; virial coefficients; grand canonical for interacting systems.
PhD: Yang--Lee zeros and phase transitions; Lee--Yang theorem; complex fugacity in QFT.

\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- $\langle N\rangle,\Omega,P$ for non-interacting fermion gas; BE/FD distributions.
Set~B --- Yang--Lee theorem statement; ensemble equivalence derivation via saddle point.
Projects: (simple) $\langle N\rangle$ vs.\ $\mu$ for Bose and Fermi gas at various temperatures;
(complex) virial expansion to second order: quantum corrections to classical ideal gas.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.7 / L03: Quantum Ideal Gases}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Density of states in 3D: $D(\varepsilon)=\tfrac{V}{2\pi^2}(\tfrac{2m}{\hbar^2})^{3/2}\varepsilon^{1/2}$; grand potential $\Omega=\mp k_BT\int D(\varepsilon)\ln(1\pm e^{-\beta(\varepsilon-\mu)})d\varepsilon$; (20--45~min) Ideal Fermi gas: Fermi energy $E_F=\tfrac{\hbar^2}{2m}(3\pi^2n)^{2/3}$; Sommerfeld expansion: $\langle f(\varepsilon)\rangle=\int_0^\infty f(\varepsilon)n_F d\varepsilon=\int_0^\mu f\,d\varepsilon+\tfrac{\pi^2}{6}(k_BT)^2f'(\mu)+\ldots$; specific heat $C_V=\tfrac{\pi^2}{3}k_B^2TD(E_F)$; Pauli susceptibility; (45--65~min) Ideal Bose gas: $\mu<0$ at all $T>T_c$; $\mu\to 0^-$ signals BEC; $\Omega$ for bosons; pressure and density in terms of Bose functions $g_\nu(z)$; (65--90~min) Low-$T$ thermodynamics: $T^3$ law for bosons; Fermi gas degeneracy pressure; applications: He-3 specific heat; white dwarf and neutron star equations of state; cold atoms.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Compute thermodynamic quantities for ideal Bose and Fermi gases.
  \item Derive the Sommerfeld expansion and apply it to specific heat and susceptibility.
  \item Explain degeneracy pressure and its role in stellar physics.
  \item Describe the approach to BEC as $\mu\to 0^-$ in the ideal Bose gas.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: FD and BE distributions; electronic specific heat linear in $T$; degeneracy pressure in white dwarfs.
Beg.\ UG: Fermi energy; Sommerfeld linear $C_V$; Pauli susceptibility; BEC $T_c$.
Adv.\ UG: Sommerfeld expansion derivation; Bose functions; degeneracy pressure for neutron star.
MSc: Landau diamagnetism; de Haas--van Alphen; Bose gas thermodynamics below $T_c$.
PhD: strongly interacting Fermi gas at unitarity; polaron in Fermi sea; quantum critical Fermi gas.

\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- Fermi energy for Cu; $C_V$ from Sommerfeld; Pauli susceptibility; BEC $T_c$ for $^{87}$Rb.
Set~B --- Sommerfeld expansion derivation; pressure of degenerate neutron star; Bose functions.
Projects: (simple) $C_V(T)$ for Fermi gas: crossover from linear to Dulong--Petit;
(complex) equation of state for white dwarf: degeneracy pressure vs.\ gravitational collapse.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.7 / L04: Bose--Einstein Condensation and Superfluidity}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) BEC in 3D ideal gas: $\mu\to 0^-$ at $T_c$; condensate fraction $N_0/N=1-(T/T_c)^{3/2}$; thermodynamics below $T_c$: pressure independent of $N$; (20--45~min) Off-diagonal long-range order (ODLRO): $\lim_{|\mathbf{r}-\mathbf{r}'|\to\infty}\langle\hat\psi^\dagger(\mathbf{r})\hat\psi(\mathbf{r}')\rangle=n_0\neq 0$; broken $U(1)$ symmetry; Goldstone (phonon) mode; superfluidity from ODLRO; Landau criterion $v<c_s$; (45--65~min) Superfluid $^4$He: lambda transition; two-fluid model (normal + superfluid fractions); quantised vortices $\kappa=h/m$; vortex energy and critical rotation speed; (65--90~min) 2D systems: Mermin--Wagner theorem forbids true LRO in 2D; algebraic ODLRO $\sim r^{-\eta}$ below BKT; Kosterlitz--Thouless transition: vortex--anti-vortex unbinding at $T_{\rm BKT}$; superfluid density jumps at $T_{\rm BKT}$; experimental observation in thin He films and cold atoms.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Derive BEC critical temperature and condensate fraction.
  \item Define ODLRO and connect to broken symmetry and Goldstone mode.
  \item Describe quantised vortices and the Landau criterion for superfluidity.
  \item State the BKT transition and its experimental signatures.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``below $T_c$ a macroscopic number of bosons occupy the same state.''
Beg.\ UG: $T_c$; condensate fraction; Landau criterion; two-fluid model.
Adv.\ UG: ODLRO; vortex energy; BKT transition.
MSc: algebraic order in 2D; superfluid density jump; BKT in ultracold atoms.
PhD: BKT from renormalisation group; topological defects; superfluid density from Kubo formula.

\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- $T_c$ and $N_0/N$ for $^4$He and $^{87}$Rb; Landau critical velocity from Bogoliubov spectrum.
Set~B --- ODLRO derivation; Mermin--Wagner theorem sketch; BKT vortex unbinding energy.
Projects: (simple) condensate fraction vs.\ $T/T_c$ and specific heat anomaly;
(complex) BKT transition: vortex--anti-vortex density and correlation function decay.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.7 / L05: Fermi Liquid Theory}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Landau's postulate: adiabatic continuity from non-interacting to interacting Fermi gas; quasiparticle concept; one-to-one correspondence of states; sharp Fermi surface; (20--45~min) Quasiparticle energy: $\varepsilon_k^\star=\varepsilon_k^0+\sum_{k'}f_{kk'}\delta n_{k'}$; Landau interaction function $f_{kk'}$; Landau parameters $F_l^s,F_l^a$; effective mass $m^*=m(1+F_1^s/3)^{-1}$; (45--65~min) Thermodynamics from quasiparticles: specific heat $C_V=\tfrac{\pi^2}{3}k_B^2T D^*(E_F)$ with renormalised DOS; compressibility $\kappa=\kappa_0/(1+F_0^s)$; Pauli susceptibility $\chi=\chi_0/(1+F_0^a)$; Wilson ratio $R_W=\chi/C_V$; (65--90~min) Quasiparticle lifetime: $\tau^{-1}\propto(\varepsilon-E_F)^2+(\pi k_BT)^2$ from Fermi's golden rule and phase space; Fermi liquid $\Leftrightarrow$ Im$\,\Sigma\propto\omega^2$; breakdown: Tomonaga--Luttinger in 1D; non-Fermi liquid at quantum critical points.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item State Landau's postulate and explain the quasiparticle concept.
  \item Compute renormalised thermodynamic quantities from Landau parameters.
  \item Derive quasiparticle lifetime from phase-space arguments.
  \item Identify signatures of non-Fermi liquid behaviour.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``interacting electrons still behave like free electrons but with a different mass.''
Beg.\ UG: quasiparticle concept; effective mass; Sommerfeld linear $C_V$ from FL.
Adv.\ UG: Landau parameters; compressibility; susceptibility; Wilson ratio.
MSc: quasiparticle lifetime derivation; Luttinger liquid in 1D.
PhD: Luttinger's theorem; microscopic derivation of FL from self-energy; quantum critical non-FL.

\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- effective mass for $^3$He from $C_V$; Pauli susceptibility from $F_0^a$; Wilson ratio.
Set~B --- quasiparticle lifetime derivation; Luttinger theorem statement and use.
Projects: (simple) FL thermodynamics: $C_V,\chi,\kappa$ as function of $F_0^s,F_0^a,F_1^s$;
(complex) marginal Fermi liquid self-energy: Im$\,\Sigma\propto\omega$ and its experimental signatures.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.7 / L06: Imaginary-Time Formalism and Matsubara Green's Functions}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Imaginary-time evolution $\hat{O}(\tau)=e^{\hat{H}\tau/\hbar}\hat{O}e^{-\hat{H}\tau/\hbar}$; thermal averages as Euclidean path integrals (recap); Matsubara GF $\mathcal{G}(\mathbf{k},\tau)=-\langle T_\tau\hat{c}_k(\tau)\hat{c}_k^\dagger(0)\rangle_\beta$; (anti-)periodicity in $\tau\in[0,\beta\hbar]$; (20--45~min) Fourier decomposition: fermionic $\omega_n=(2n+1)\pi/\beta\hbar$; bosonic $\omega_n=2n\pi/\beta\hbar$; non-interacting Matsubara GF $\mathcal{G}_0(\mathbf{k},i\omega_n)=(i\omega_n-\varepsilon_k)^{-1}$; Dyson equation $\mathcal{G}=\mathcal{G}_0+\mathcal{G}_0\Sigma\mathcal{G}$; (45--65~min) Matsubara frequency sums: contour integration; $\sum_n f(i\omega_n)=-\operatorname{Res}[n_F(\omega)f(\omega)]$; evaluation of one-loop self-energy; (65--90~min) Analytic continuation $i\omega_n\to\omega+i\eta$: spectral representation; Padé approximants for numerical continuation; maximum entropy method (MEM); ill-posedness and regularisation; connection between Matsubara and real-time GFs.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Define the Matsubara GF and perform Matsubara Fourier decomposition.
  \item Evaluate Matsubara frequency sums via contour integration.
  \item Apply the Dyson equation to find the interacting Matsubara GF.
  \item Perform analytic continuation and describe numerical methods (Padé, MEM).
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``imaginary-time GFs encode thermal equilibrium information.''
Beg.\ UG: Matsubara frequencies; $\mathcal{G}_0$; Dyson equation in Matsubara.
Adv.\ UG: frequency sums via contour; one-loop self-energy; analytic continuation.
MSc: Padé approximants; MEM; spectral function reconstruction.
PhD: Nevanlinna analytic continuation; stochastic MEM; sparse-modelling approach.

\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- $\mathcal{G}_0$ for fermion and boson; Dyson equation for HF self-energy.
Set~B --- Matsubara sum via contour; analytic continuation of model self-energy.
Projects: (simple) Matsubara GF for Hubbard dimer: spectral function via analytic continuation;
(complex) MEM analytic continuation: spectral function from QMC-generated $\mathcal{G}(\tau)$.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.7 / L07: Perturbation Theory at Finite Temperature}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Finite-$T$ perturbation theory: split $\hat{H}=\hat{H}_0+\hat{V}$; interaction picture in imaginary time; $\mathcal{G}=\mathcal{G}_0+\mathcal{G}_0\Sigma\mathcal{G}$; Wick's theorem in imaginary time; (20--45~min) Diagrammatic rules at finite $T$: Feynman diagrams identical to $T=0$ but with Matsubara frequencies; propagator $\mathcal{G}_0(k,i\omega_n)$; vertices $V$; frequency conservation; sums over $i\omega_n$ instead of integrals; (45--65~min) Free energy from diagrams: $F=F_0-k_BT\ln\langle T_\tau e^{-\int_0^\beta\hat{V}d\tau}\rangle_0$; linked-cluster theorem: $\ln Z=\ln Z_0+$ (linked diagrams only); first-order: $F^{(1)}=\langle\hat{V}\rangle_0$; second-order: $F^{(2)}$; (65--90~min) Self-consistent Dyson at finite $T$: HF at finite $T$ (free energy minimisation); GW at finite $T$; finite-$T$ spectral function; Matsubara self-energy and quasiparticle renormalisation; phase boundary from self-energy divergence.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Apply Wick's theorem in imaginary time to derive Matsubara diagrammatic rules.
  \item Compute the free energy perturbatively using the linked-cluster theorem.
  \item Apply Dyson's equation at finite $T$ for the HF and GW self-energies.
  \item Identify phase boundaries from divergences in the self-energy.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``quantum perturbation theory at finite temperature uses oscillating imaginary-time diagrams.''
Beg.\ UG: linked-cluster theorem; first-order free energy; HF at finite $T$.
Adv.\ UG: full diagrammatic rules; second-order $F$; Dyson at finite $T$.
MSc: GW at finite $T$; finite-$T$ spectral function; Mott transition from self-energy.
PhD: $\Phi$-derivable approximations at finite $T$; Luttinger--Ward functional; DMFT at finite $T$.

\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- first-order $F$ for Fermi gas with contact interaction; HF self-energy at finite $T$.
Set~B --- linked-cluster theorem at finite $T$; second-order free energy for electron gas.
Projects: (simple) HF free energy vs.\ $T$: paramagnetic to ferromagnetic transition (Stoner);
(complex) GW spectral function at finite $T$: quasiparticle peak broadening.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.7 / L08: Phase Transitions I --- Landau Theory}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Order parameter concept: zero above $T_c$, non-zero below; examples: magnetisation ($\hat{M}$), condensate ($\psi_0$), sublattice magnetisation; continuous (second-order) vs.\ first-order transitions; (20--45~min) Landau free energy: $F(\phi,T)=a(T)\phi^2+b\phi^4+c\phi^6+\ldots$ (symmetry $\phi\to-\phi$); $a(T)=a_0(T-T_c)$; minimisation: $\phi^*=0$ for $T>T_c$, $\phi^*=\sqrt{-a/2b}$ for $T<T_c$; second-order: $b>0$; first-order: $b<0$ with $c>0$; (45--65~min) Thermodynamic consequences: specific heat jump $\Delta C=a_0^2T_c/2b$; susceptibility $\chi=(2|a|)^{-1}$ above $T_c$; critical exponents $\alpha,\beta,\gamma,\delta$ from Landau; (65--90~min) Ginzburg criterion: Landau breaks down near $T_c$; $\xi=\xi_0(T-T_c)^{-\nu}$; fluctuations $\langle(\delta\phi)^2\rangle\sim k_BT/\xi^d$; Ginzburg--Landau theory (spatial order parameter); coherence length; domain walls; upper critical dimension $d_c^+=4$.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Construct the Landau free energy from symmetry and compute the order parameter.
  \item Distinguish first- and second-order transitions from the sign of $b$.
  \item Derive critical exponents $\alpha,\beta,\gamma,\delta$ from Landau theory.
  \item State the Ginzburg criterion and identify the upper critical dimension.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``order parameter measures how ordered the system is; it grows continuously at a second-order transition.''
Beg.\ UG: Landau free energy; minimisation; $T_c$; $\Delta C$.
Adv.\ UG: critical exponents; susceptibility; first- vs.\ second-order.
MSc: Ginzburg criterion; Ginzburg--Landau theory; coherence length; domain walls.
PhD: renormalisation group improvement of Landau; $\epsilon$-expansion; tricritical points.

\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- minimise Landau $F$; $T_c$; $\phi^*(T)$; $\Delta C$; $\chi$ above $T_c$.
Set~B --- first-order transition: discontinuous $\phi$; latent heat; Ginzburg criterion derivation.
Projects: (simple) Landau free energy landscape: second-order and first-order as function of temperature;
(complex) Ginzburg--Landau order parameter profile: domain wall solution and energy.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.7 / L09: Phase Transitions II --- Ising Model and Renormalisation Group}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Ising model: $\hat{H}=-J\sum_{\langle ij\rangle}\sigma_i\sigma_j-h\sum_i\sigma_i$; exact solution in 1D (no phase transition); exact solution in 2D (Onsager); (20--45~min) Mean-field theory: $\sigma_i\approx m+\delta\sigma_i$; self-consistency $m=\tanh(\beta zJm+\beta h)$; $T_c=zJ/k_B$; critical exponents $\beta=\tfrac{1}{2},\gamma=1,\delta=3$; mean-field fails in low $d$; (45--65~min) Kadanoff block spin and renormalisation group (RG) idea: coarse-grain by blocks of $b$ spins; effective Hamiltonian; flow of couplings; fixed points and universality; Wilson's RG in $d=4-\epsilon$; (65--90~min) Universality classes: Ising, Heisenberg, XY, $O(N)$; critical exponents from RG; scaling hypothesis; quantum phase transitions: $\hat{H}=\hat{H}_0+g\hat{V}$ at $T=0$; quantum critical point (QCP); dimensional crossover; quantum Ising model (TFIM) as paradigm.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Apply mean-field theory to the Ising model and compute critical exponents.
  \item Describe Kadanoff block-spin RG and explain universality.
  \item Identify universality classes and their experimental realisations.
  \item Distinguish classical from quantum phase transitions and describe the TFIM.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``all second-order phase transitions near their critical point behave the same way --- universality.''
Beg.\ UG: mean-field Ising; $T_c$; critical exponents; universality concept.
Adv.\ UG: Kadanoff block spin; RG flow; fixed points; universality classes.
MSc: Wilson RG in $4-\epsilon$ dimensions; $\epsilon$-expansion; quantum Ising model.
PhD: conformal field theory at the critical point; operator product expansion; exact critical exponents in 2D.

\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- mean-field $T_c$ for 3D Ising; critical exponents; Ising exact solution in 1D.
Set~B --- Kadanoff block-spin RG; fixed point analysis; $\epsilon$-expansion for $\beta$.
Projects: (simple) Monte Carlo simulation of 2D Ising model: $M(T)$ and $T_c$;
(complex) RG flow for the 1D quantum Ising model: quantum phase transition.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.7 / L10: Quantum Criticality}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Quantum phase transition at $T=0$: varying a non-thermal parameter $g$ (pressure, field, doping); quantum critical point (QCP) at $g=g_c$; diverging correlation length $\xi\propto|g-g_c|^{-\nu}$; diverging correlation time $\xi_\tau\propto\xi^z$ (dynamical exponent $z$); (20--45~min) Quantum critical region: $T>0$ near QCP; fan-shaped quantum critical region in $(g,T)$ plane; $\omega/T$ scaling: correlators $C(\omega,T)=T^{2\Delta/z}f(\omega/T)$ from conformal invariance; ``strange metal'' regime: $\rho\propto T$ linear resistivity; (45--65~min) Non-Fermi liquid signatures: self-energy Im$\,\Sigma\propto\omega$ or $T$ (vs.\ $\omega^2,T^2$ in FL); cuprate phase diagram: pseudogap, strange metal, FL; QCP under the superconducting dome; (65--90~min) Theoretical approaches: $(d+1)$-dimensional classical field theory at QCP; $1/N$ expansion; holographic duality (AdS/CFT) for strongly coupled QCPs; quantum spin liquid as frustrated QCP; experimental signatures: NMR, transport, neutron scattering.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Define a QCP and its characteristic scales $\xi$ and $\xi_\tau$.
  \item State the $\omega/T$ scaling hypothesis and its physical origin.
  \item Identify non-Fermi liquid signatures in transport and spectral functions.
  \item Describe the cuprate phase diagram and the role of the putative QCP.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``near a quantum phase transition, quantum fluctuations dominate over thermal ones.''
Beg.\ UG: QCP definition; diverging $\xi$; quantum critical fan; linear resistivity.
Adv.\ UG: $\omega/T$ scaling; dynamical exponent $z$; non-FL self-energy.
MSc: holographic duality; $1/N$ expansion; cuprate phase diagram.
PhD: conformal field theory at QCP; Hertz--Millis theory; non-Fermi liquid from FL instabilities.

\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- quantum critical scaling: $\xi(g)$, $\xi_\tau(g)$; quantum critical fan width vs.\ $T$.
Set~B --- $\omega/T$ scaling derivation from conformal invariance; non-FL self-energy and resistivity.
Projects: (simple) quantum critical fan diagram for transverse-field Ising model;
(complex) $\omega/T$ scaling: numerical correlation function for quantum Ising chain at QCP.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.7 / L11: Entanglement in Many-Body Systems}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Entanglement entropy as a probe of many-body physics: $S_A=-\operatorname{Tr}(\hat\rho_A\ln\hat\rho_A)$ where $\hat\rho_A=\operatorname{Tr}_B\hat\rho$; area law: $S_A\propto L^{d-1}$ for gapped systems; volume law for generic excited states and thermal states; (20--45~min) 1D gapped systems: area law $S_A=\mathrm{const}$; MPS as efficient representation (connection to DMRG); 1D critical systems: $S_A=\tfrac{c}{3}\ln L$ where $c$ is the central charge (conformal field theory); Calabrese--Cardy formula; (45--65~min) Higher dimensions: area law in 2D and 3D gapped phases; subleading corrections: topological entanglement entropy $S_A^{\rm top}=-\ln\mathcal{D}$ where $\mathcal{D}$ is the total quantum dimension; detection of topological order (Kitaev--Preskill, Levin--Wen); (65--90~min) Entanglement spectrum: eigenvalues $\lambda_i$ of $\hat\rho_A$; entanglement Hamiltonian $H_E=-\ln\hat\rho_A$; bulk--boundary correspondence; entanglement negativity for mixed states; multipartite entanglement measures.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Define entanglement entropy and compute it for simple bipartitions.
  \item State the area law and the Calabrese--Cardy formula for critical systems.
  \item Define topological entanglement entropy and describe how it detects topological order.
  \item Describe the entanglement spectrum and its relation to the entanglement Hamiltonian.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``entanglement tells us how quantum-correlated two parts of a system are.''
Beg.\ UG: entanglement entropy for Bell states; area law; volume law for thermal states.
Adv.\ UG: Calabrese--Cardy formula; central charge; topological entanglement entropy.
MSc: entanglement spectrum; entanglement Hamiltonian; Kitaev--Preskill construction.
PhD: modular Hamiltonian in QFT; entanglement in holography (Ryu--Takayanagi); multipartite entanglement.

\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- $S_A$ for Bell state, GHZ, and product state; area law check for 1D gapped chain.
Set~B --- Calabrese--Cardy formula for XX chain; topological entropy for toric code.
Projects: (simple) $S_A$ vs.\ subsystem size $L$ for critical vs.\ gapped 1D chain (DMRG);
(complex) topological entanglement entropy from DMRG for Kitaev honeycomb model.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[modulebox, title={Module~II.7 / L12: Open Problems and Frontiers}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Overview of open problems: high-$T_c$ superconductivity; fractional quantum Hall (FQH) effect; quantum spin liquids; non-equilibrium many-body physics; quantum simulation; (20--40~min) High-$T_c$ superconductivity: cuprate phase diagram (underdoped, optimally doped, overdoped); pseudogap; strange metal; pairing mechanism (not phonon-mediated); competing orders; $d$-wave symmetry of the gap; key experiments (ARPES, neutron, NMR); (40--55~min) Fractional quantum Hall effect: Landau levels; fractional filling $\nu=\tfrac{1}{3},\tfrac{2}{5},\ldots$; Laughlin wavefunction; fractional charge and statistics (anyons); non-Abelian FQH states ($\nu=\tfrac{5}{2}$) and topological quantum computing; (55--70~min) Quantum simulation: analog quantum simulators (cold atoms, trapped ions); digital quantum simulation (VQE, QPE); resource estimation for quantum chemistry on fault-tolerant hardware; (70--90~min) Outlook: machine learning for many-body physics (neural network quantum states, ML force fields); tensor network methods for open systems; non-equilibrium topological phases; quantum advantage in many-body simulations.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Describe the cuprate phase diagram and the open questions in high-$T_c$.
  \item Explain the FQH effect and the role of Laughlin's wavefunction.
  \item Outline quantum simulation approaches (analog and digital).
  \item Identify frontier methods: neural network states, ML, non-equilibrium topology.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``these are the unsolved problems that the next generation of physicists will crack.''
Beg.\ UG: cuprate phenomenology; FQH basics; quantum simulation concept.
Adv.\ UG: Laughlin wavefunction; fractional statistics; VQE algorithm.
MSc: non-Abelian anyons; topological quantum computing; analog simulators.
PhD: current research frontiers; neural network quantum states; quantum error correction for many-body.

\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- sketch cuprate phase diagram; Laughlin wavefunction for $\nu=\tfrac{1}{3}$; VQE ansatz design.
Set~B --- fractional charge from Laughlin; anyonic braiding statistics; QPE resource estimation for FeMoco.
Projects: (simple) cuprate phase diagram: literature survey of key experiments and their interpretation;
(complex) Laughlin wavefunction: Monte Carlo evaluation of density and pair correlation.
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[highlightbox]
\textbf{Module II.7 Reading:}
Altland \& Simons, \textit{Condensed Matter Field Theory} (Cambridge);
Sachdev, \textit{Quantum Phase Transitions}, 2nd ed.\ (Cambridge);
Goldenfeld, \textit{Lectures on Phase Transitions and the Renormalization Group};
Wen, \textit{Quantum Field Theory of Many-Body Systems} (Oxford).
\end{tcolorbox}

\newpage

\subsection{Module II.8 --- Advanced Physical Systems (Lecture Menu)}
\label{sec:mod-II8}
%=============================================================

\begin{tcolorbox}[seriesbox]
  \textbf{Series II / Module~II.8} \quad
  \textit{Advanced Physical Systems --- Lecture Menu}\\[4pt]
  \textbf{Format:} 12 stand-alone lecture topics, each self-contained.
  Instructors select any subset as optional enrichment lectures following
  Modules~I.1--I.4 and the preceding Series~II modules and Series~II. Full expansion (90-min pacing, dual-track content,
  five-tier pedagogy, assessment bundles) to be developed per instructor need.
  Prerequisites for each topic listed in parentheses.\\[4pt]
  \textbf{Recommended audience:} Advanced UG, MSc, and PhD students who have
  completed Modules~I.1--I.4 and Series~II.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\subsubsection*{Module Overview}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Module II.8 Overview}

{\footnotesize
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lp{4.2cm}p{6.8cm}@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Lec.} & \textbf{Title} & \textbf{Key Concepts / Theme}\\
\midrule
L01 & 3D Spherically Symmetric Potentials & I.4-L09; spherical harmonics; effective potential; 3D scattering\\

L03 & Identical Particles \& Quantum Statistics & I.3-L10; exchange symmetry; bosons; fermions; Gibbs paradox\\
L04 & The 3D Isotropic Harmonic Oscillator & I.4-L03; degeneracy; $\mathfrak{su}(3)$ symmetry; shell model\\
L05 & Magnetic Resonance (NMR/ESR) & I.4-L04/L06; rotating frame; Bloch equations; relaxation $T_1,T_2$\\
L06 & Coherence, Decoherence, \& the Quantum Eraser & I.3-L01; Mach--Zehnder; which-path; environment-induced decoherence\\
\midrule

L08 & Adiabatic Theorem \& Berry Phase & I.3-L04/L05; slow parameter change; geometric phase; adiabatic approximation\\
L09 & Quantum Entanglement \& Bell Inequalities & I.3-L01; EPR; CHSH; loophole-free tests; quantum cryptography\\
L10 & The WKB Method in 3D & I.4-L12; radial WKB; Langer correction; 3D Bohr--Sommerfeld; barrier\\
L11 & Supersymmetric Quantum Mechanics & I.4-L03/L09; SUSY partner potentials; factorisation; shape invariance\\
L12 & Exactly Solvable Models beyond the HO & I.4-L03; P\"oschl--Teller; Morse; P\"oschl--Teller II; reflectionless potentials\\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
}

\subsubsection*{Lecture Abstracts}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Module II.8 Lecture Abstracts}

\medskip
\begin{description}[leftmargin=1.4em, style=nextline, itemsep=6pt]
\emergencystretch=3em

\item[\textbf{L01 --- 3D Spherically Symmetric Potentials}]
Generalisation from 1D to 3D for any central potential $V(r)$; separation into radial and angular parts; effective potential including the centrifugal barrier $\hbar^2l(l+1)/2mr^2$; radial Schr\"odinger equation for $u_{nl}=rR_{nl}$; general behaviour at $r\to0$ (regularity) and $r\to\infty$ (bound vs.\ scattering); 3D infinite spherical well (spherical Bessel functions); 3D scattering: partial-wave expansion; phase shifts $\delta_l$; optical theorem; application to neutron--proton scattering and nuclear potential models.

\item[\textbf{L02 --- The Hydrogen Molecular Ion (H$_2^+$)}]
Simplest molecular system: one electron, two protons; Born--Oppenheimer PES; LCAO-MO ansatz with $1s$ atomic orbitals; bonding ($\sigma_g$) and antibonding ($\sigma_u^*$) MOs; overlap integral $S$, Coulomb integral $\alpha$, resonance integral $\beta$; variational optimisation of $Z_{\rm eff}$; exact solution in prolate spheroidal coordinates ($\xi,\eta,\phi$); comparison of LCAO vs.\ exact; equilibrium bond length and dissociation energy; connection to H\"uckel and VB theories.

\item[\textbf{L03 --- Identical Particles and Quantum Statistics}]
The identity postulate for indistinguishable particles; exchange operator $\hat{P}_{12}$; symmetric ($+1$) and antisymmetric ($-1$) subspaces; fermions (half-integer spin, antisymmetric) and bosons (integer spin, symmetric); spin--statistics theorem (statement); many-particle wavefunctions; permanents and determinants; Gibbs paradox resolved; exchange interaction as a purely quantum effect; emergence of Bose--Einstein and Fermi--Dirac statistics; brief discussion of anyons and parastatistics.

\item[\textbf{L04 --- The 3D Isotropic Harmonic Oscillator}]
Hamiltonian $\hat{H}=\hat{p}^2/2m+m\omega^2r^2/2$; three approaches: Cartesian (product of 1D HOs), spherical (radial equation + spherical harmonics), and algebraic ($\mathfrak{su}(3)$ creation operators); energy levels $E_N=(N+3/2)\hbar\omega$ with $N=2n_r+l$; degeneracy $\tfrac{1}{2}(N+1)(N+2)$; connection to nuclear shell model (magic numbers 2, 8, 20 from single-particle filling); $\mathfrak{su}(3)$ algebra and its physical interpretation.

\item[\textbf{L05 --- Magnetic Resonance (NMR and ESR)}]
Larmor precession of a spin in a static field $B_0$; resonance condition $\omega_0=\gamma B_0$; oscillating transverse field $B_1\cos(\omega t)$; rotating frame transformation; Rabi formula for spin flip; Bloch equations including phenomenological relaxation: longitudinal $T_1$ (spin--lattice) and transverse $T_2$ (spin--spin); free induction decay; Fourier transform to spectrum; pulsed NMR: $\pi/2$ pulse, FID, spin echo; chemical shift and $J$-coupling; MRI gradient encoding.

\item[\textbf{L06 --- Coherence, Decoherence, and the Quantum Eraser}]
Quantum coherence as off-diagonal elements of $\hat\rho$; Mach--Zehnder interferometer with a ``which-path'' detector; loss of interference when path information is available; quantum eraser: restoring interference by erasing which-path information; decoherence from environment entanglement: $\hat\rho_{\rm sys}=\operatorname{Tr}_E(\hat\rho_{\rm total})$; pointer states; decoherence time scale $t_D\sim\hbar/\Delta E_{\rm env}$; connection to the measurement problem; Zurek's einselection; experimental realisations.

\item[\textbf{L07 --- Path Integrals:} \textbf{First Steps}]
Feynman's sum over histories as the third formulation of QM; transition amplitude $K(x_b,t_b;x_a,t_a)=\int\mathcal{D}x(t)\,e^{iS[x]/\hbar}$; derivation from the short-time propagator; free particle: exact Gaussian integral; harmonic oscillator: classical action + fluctuation determinant; stationary phase and the classical limit; imaginary-time path integral and the partition function; brief discussion of field-theory generalisation; connection to PIMC (Module~II.2).

\item[\textbf{L08 --- Adiabatic Theorem and Berry Phase}]
Adiabatic theorem: slow variation of $\hat{H}(\mathbf{R}(t))$ keeps the system in the instantaneous eigenstate if the gap remains non-zero; quantum adiabatic condition $|\langle m|\dot{\hat{H}}|n\rangle|/(E_n-E_m)^2\ll1$; dynamical phase vs.\ geometric phase; Berry's phase $\gamma_n=i\oint\bra{n(\mathbf{R})}\nabla_\mathbf{R}\ket{n(\mathbf{R})}\cdot d\mathbf{R}$; Berry connection and curvature; examples: spin-$\tfrac{1}{2}$ in a rotating field (solid-angle formula); Aharonov--Bohm as Berry phase; non-Abelian Berry phase; connection to topology.

\item[\textbf{L09 --- Quantum Entanglement and Bell Inequalities}]
EPR paradox and local hidden variables; Bell's theorem; CHSH inequality $|S|\leq2$ (classical) vs.\ $|S|\leq2\sqrt{2}$ (quantum); derivation for singlet state; loophole-free experimental tests (2015 onwards); implications for non-locality; quantum cryptography: BB84 protocol; E91 entanglement-based QKD; quantum teleportation; entanglement as a resource; entanglement measures: concurrence, entanglement of formation; monogamy of entanglement.

\item[\textbf{L10 --- The WKB Method in 3D}]
Extension of 1D WKB to 3D spherically symmetric potentials; radial WKB wavefunction; Langer correction $l(l+1)\to(l+\tfrac{1}{2})^2$ for centrifugal barrier near origin; 3D Bohr--Sommerfeld quantisation $\int_{r_1}^{r_2}p_r\,dr=\pi\hbar(n_r+\tfrac{1}{2})$; application to hydrogen: recover $E_n=-Z^2/2n^2$ a.u.; 3D tunnelling: barrier-penetration in a central field; alpha-decay Gamow factor in 3D; connection to quasi-classical limit and semiclassical mechanics.

\item[\textbf{L11 --- Supersymmetric Quantum Mechanics}]
Factorisation of $\hat{H}=\hat{A}^\dagger\hat{A}+E_0$; supercharge operators $\hat{Q}=\hat{A}$, $\hat{Q}^\dagger=\hat{A}^\dagger$; SUSY partner potentials $V_\pm=W^2\pm W'$ (superpotential $W$); isospectrality: $V_-$ and $V_+$ have identical spectra except ground state; shape invariance: hierarchy of solvable potentials; exactly solvable potentials from SUSY: infinite square well, harmonic oscillator, hydrogen; broken vs.\ unbroken SUSY; Witten index; connection to integrability and exactly solvable models.

\item[\textbf{L12 --- Exactly Solvable Models beyond the Harmonic Oscillator}]
Criteria for exact solvability; P\"oschl--Teller potential $V(x)=-V_0/\cosh^2(x/a)$: hypergeometric equation; $N$ bound states for $V_0=\hbar^2N(N+1)/2ma^2$; reflectionless property; Morse potential $V(r)=D_e(1-e^{-a(r-r_e)})^2$: exact vibrational levels $E_n=\hbar\omega_e(n+\tfrac{1}{2})-x_e\hbar\omega_e(n+\tfrac{1}{2})^2$ (finite anharmonicity); P\"oschl--Teller II (symmetric Rosen--Morse); inverse square potential; connection to SUSY hierarchy (L11); experimental relevance: diatomic molecules, optical solitons.

\end{description}

\begin{tcolorbox}[highlightbox]
\textbf{Module II.8 Note:} These lectures are intended as optional enrichment modules. Each can be taught as a standalone 90-minute lecture. Full expansion to the standard format (90-min pacing, dual-track content, five-tier pedagogy, Problem Sets A \& B, mini-projects) can be carried out on request. Prerequisites listed in the overview table are recommended but not strictly required for strong students.
\end{tcolorbox}

%=============================================================
\subsection{Module II.9 --- Quantum Information and Quantum Logic}
\label{sec:mod-II9}
%=============================================================

\begin{tcolorbox}[seriesbox]
  \textbf{Series II / Module~II.9} \quad
  \textit{Quantum Information and Quantum Logic}\\[4pt]
  \textbf{Duration:} 12 lectures $\times$ 90 minutes.
  Prerequisites: Modules~I.1--I.3 (bra-ket, density matrices, measurement);
  Module~II.4 (Fock space and many-body formalism) recommended.
  This module develops the mathematical language and operational framework
  of quantum information processing from first principles.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\subsubsection*{Module Overview}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Module II.9 Overview}
{\footnotesize
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lp{4.2cm}p{6.8cm}@{}}

\midrule
L01 & Qubits, Qutrits, and Qudits & Two-level quantum systems; Bloch sphere; generalisation to $d$-level; Hilbert space $\mathbb{C}^d$\\
L02 & Quantum Gates and Circuits & Unitary gates; Pauli, Hadamard, CNOT, Toffoli; universality; circuit model\\
L03 & Entanglement: Measures and Classification & Bell states; Schmidt rank; concurrence; entanglement of formation; PPT criterion\\
L04 & Quantum Teleportation and Superdense Coding & Bell measurement; classical communication; channel capacity; no-cloning\\
\midrule

\bottomrule

\end{tcolorbox}

%=============================================================
\subsection{Module II.11 --- The Tenfold Way and Symmetry Classification of Topological Phases}
\label{sec:mod-II11}
%=============================================================

\begin{tcolorbox}[seriesbox]
  \textbf{Series II / Module~II.11} \quad
  \textit{The Tenfold Way and Symmetry Classification of Topological Phases}\\[4pt]
  \textbf{Duration:} 12 lectures $\times$ 90 minutes.
  Prerequisites: Modules~II.3 (angular momentum, time-reversal),
  II.4 (second quantisation), II.7 (statistical mechanics);
  Module~II.9 recommended.
  This module develops the complete classification of non-interacting
  fermionic topological phases by symmetry class and spatial dimension.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\subsubsection*{Module Overview}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Module II.11 Overview}
{\footnotesize
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lp{4.2cm}p{6.8cm}@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Lec.} & \textbf{Title} & \textbf{Key Concepts}\\
\midrule
L01 & Symmetry Classes: Time-Reversal, Particle--Hole, Chiral & Antiunitary symmetries; $\hat{T}^2=\pm1$, $\hat{C}^2=\pm1$; chiral $\hat{S}=\hat{T}\hat{C}$; Wigner's theorem revisited\\
L02 & Cartan's Classification and the Tenfold Way & Ten Altland--Zirnbauer symmetry classes; Cartan labels (A, AI, AII, $\ldots$, CI); table of classes\\
L03 & Topological Invariants in 0D and 1D & $\mathbb{Z}$ and $\mathbb{Z}_2$ invariants; SSH model; winding number; Zak phase; Majorana end modes\\
L04 & Topological Invariants in 2D & Chern number; TKNN formula; $\mathbb{Z}_2$ Kane--Mele invariant; time-reversal polarisation\\
\midrule
L05 & The Periodic Table of Topological Insulators & Classifying space; Bott periodicity; $(d,\delta)$-dimensional table; eight-fold periodicity in $d$\\
L06 & Bulk--Boundary Correspondence & Spectral flow; index theorem; edge states as topological zero modes; K-theory sketch\\
L07 & Interacting Topological Phases and SPT Orders & Beyond free fermions; group cohomology; SPT phases; symmetry-protected vs.\ intrinsic topological order\\
L08 & Topological Semimetals and Weyl Physics & Weyl nodes as monopoles; surface Fermi arcs; chiral anomaly; Nielsen--Ninomiya theorem\\
\midrule
L09 & Floquet Topological Phases & Periodically driven systems; anomalous Floquet topological insulator; $\pi$-mode edge states\\
L10 & Topological Superconductors & Class D and DIII; $p$-wave pairing; Majorana zero modes; Kitaev chain classification\\
L11 & Disorder and Topological Robustness & Anderson localisation; topological protection; symmetry-class-dependent DOS at zero energy\\
L12 & Experimental Signatures and Outlook & ARPES of topological surface states; transport anomalies; non-Abelian braiding experiments\\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
}

\begin{tcolorbox}[highlightbox]
\textbf{Module II.11 Reading:} Chiu \textit{et al.}, Rev.\ Mod.\ Phys.\ \textbf{88}, 035005 (2016) --- tenfold way review; Hasan \& Kane, Rev.\ Mod.\ Phys.\ \textbf{82}, 3045 (2010) --- topological insulators; Altland \& Zirnbauer, Phys.\ Rev.\ B \textbf{55}, 1142 (1997) --- original classification.
\end{tcolorbox}

\newpage

%=============================================================
\subsection{Module II.12 --- Signature Physical Systems of the Tenfold Way}
\label{sec:mod-II12}
%=============================================================

\begin{tcolorbox}[seriesbox]
  \textbf{Series II / Module~II.12} \quad
  \textit{Signature Physical Systems of the Tenfold Way}\\[4pt]
  \textbf{Duration:} 12 lectures $\times$ 90 minutes.
  Each lecture presents one canonical physical system that realises a
  distinct symmetry class or spatial dimension of the tenfold way
  classification. Lectures are self-contained case studies and may be
  selected individually. Prerequisite: Module~II.11.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\subsubsection*{Module Overview}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Module II.12 Overview}
{\footnotesize
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lp{4.2cm}p{6.8cm}@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Lec.} & \textbf{Title} & \textbf{System / Class / Key Physics}\\
\midrule
L01 & The SSH Model (Class BDI, 1D) & Polyacetylene; dimerised chain; winding number $\in\mathbb{Z}$; edge modes; solitons\\
L02 & The Kitaev Chain (Class D, 1D) & $p$-wave superconductor; Majorana fermions; topological $\mathbb{Z}_2$ invariant; non-Abelian statistics\\
L03 & Integer Quantum Hall Effect (Class A, 2D) & Landau levels; Chern number = Hall conductance; TKNN; edge states; plateau robustness\\
L04 & The Quantum Spin Hall Insulator (Class AII, 2D) & HgTe/CdTe quantum well; Kane--Mele model; $\mathbb{Z}_2$ invariant; helical edge states; experiment\\
\midrule
L05 & The 3D Topological Insulator (Class AII, 3D) & Bi$_2$Se$_3$; surface Dirac cone; spin-momentum locking; ARPES observation; gapping by magnetism\\
L06 & Topological Crystalline Insulators (Class A with $C_{4v}$) & SnTe; mirror Chern number; crystalline symmetry protection; surface states on high-symmetry faces\\
L07 & The Kitaev Honeycomb Model (Class D, 2D) & Exactly solvable spin liquid; Majorana bands; abelian and non-Abelian phases; $\mathbb{Z}_2$ flux\\
L08 & Helical Topological Superconductors (Class DIII, 3D) & Time-reversal invariant $p$-wave; surface Majorana cone; $\mathbb{Z}$ classification; $^3$He-B analogy\\
\midrule
L09 & Weyl Semimetals (Class A, 3D) & TaAs; Weyl nodes; Fermi arcs; chiral anomaly; negative magnetoresistance; ARPES\\
L10 & Floquet Topological Insulator (Class A, Driven 2D) & Circularly polarised light on graphene; anomalous edge states; Floquet Chern insulator\\
L11 & Higher-Order Topological Insulators (HOTI) & Corner and hinge states; quadrupole insulator; breathing kagome; $C_4$-protected\\
L12 & Interacting Topological Phases: Fractional QHE & Laughlin state; composite fermions; $\nu=5/2$ non-Abelian state; experimental signatures\\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
}

\begin{tcolorbox}[highlightbox]
\textbf{Module II.12 Reading:} Chiu \textit{et al.}, Rev.\ Mod.\ Phys.\ \textbf{88}, 035005 (2016); Ando \& Fu, Annu.\ Rev.\ Condens.\ Matter Phys.\ \textbf{6}, 361 (2015) --- topological crystalline; Armitage, Mele \& Vishwanath, Rev.\ Mod.\ Phys.\ \textbf{90}, 015001 (2018) --- Weyl semimetals.
\end{tcolorbox}
