%#############################################################
\section{Series III --- Molecular Electronic Structure \texorpdfstring{\\}{}and Quantum Chemistry}
\label{sec:seriesIII}
%#############################################################

\begin{tcolorbox}[seriesbox, title={Series~III Overview}]
\textbf{Prerequisite:} Series~I required; Series~II Modules II.1, II.4 strongly recommended.\\
\textbf{Structure:} Three modules totalling approximately 31 lectures.\\
\textbf{Core aim:} Rigorous, graduate-level understanding of molecular electronic structure
from first principles through to modern computational methods.\\[4pt]
\begin{tabular}{llr}
\toprule
\textbf{Module} & \textbf{Title} & \textbf{Lectures}\\
\midrule
III.1 & Basic Premises of Quantum Chemistry & 3\\
III.2 & Principles of Molecular and Atomic Electronic Structure & 16\\
III.3 & Density Functional Theory and Beyond & 12\\
\midrule
 & \textbf{Total} & \textbf{31}\\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{tcolorbox}

%=============================================================
\subsection{Module III.1 --- Basic Premises of Quantum Chemistry}
\label{sec:mod-III1}
%=============================================================

\subsubsection*{Module Overview}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Module III.1 Overview}
{\footnotesize
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lp{4.2cm}p{6.8cm}@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Lec.} & \textbf{Title} & \textbf{Key Concepts}\\
\midrule
L01 & The Molecular Hamiltonian & $\hat{T}_n+\hat{T}_e+\hat{V}_{ne}+\hat{V}_{ee}+\hat{V}_{nn}$; atomic units; degrees of freedom; symmetries\\
L02 & Born--Oppenheimer Approximation & Adiabatic PES; non-adiabatic couplings; derivative couplings; conical intersections\\
L03 & Feynman--Hellmann Theorem & $\partial_\lambda E=\langle\partial_\lambda\hat{H}\rangle$; forces; geometry optimisation; analytic gradients\\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
}

\subsubsection*{Lecture-by-Lecture Syllabi}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Module III.1 Lecture Syllabi}

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.1 / L01: The Molecular Hamiltonian}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) The complete molecular Hamiltonian in SI and atomic units: $\hat{H}=\hat{T}_n+\hat{T}_e+\hat{V}_{ne}+\hat{V}_{ee}+\hat{V}_{nn}$; nuclear KE $\hat{T}_n=-\sum_A\tfrac{\hbar^2}{2M_A}\nabla_A^2$; electronic KE $\hat{T}_e=-\sum_i\tfrac{\hbar^2}{2m_e}\nabla_i^2$; electron--nuclear attraction $\hat{V}_{ne}=-\sum_{iA}\tfrac{Z_Ae^2}{r_{iA}}$; electron--electron repulsion $\hat{V}_{ee}=\sum_{i<j}\tfrac{e^2}{r_{ij}}$; nuclear--nuclear repulsion $\hat{V}_{nn}=\sum_{A<B}\tfrac{Z_AZ_Be^2}{R_{AB}}$; (20--45~min) Atomic units: Hartree $E_h=27.211$~eV; Bohr $a_0=0.529$~\AA; time $\hbar/E_h=24.2$~as; mass ratio $m_e/M_p\approx1/1836$; physical intuition for each scale; (45--70~min) Degrees of freedom: $3N_e$ electronic + $3N_n$ nuclear; total $3(N_e+N_n)$ minus COM; translational/rotational invariance; remaining internal coordinates; electronic Schr\"odinger equation at fixed $\{\mathbf{R}_A\}$; (70--90~min) Symmetries of the molecular Hamiltonian: permutation symmetry of electrons (Pauli); permutation of identical nuclei; point-group symmetry; time-reversal; connection between molecular symmetry and observable selection rules.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Write the full molecular Hamiltonian and identify each physical contribution.
  \item Convert between SI and atomic units fluently.
  \item Count the independent degrees of freedom for a given molecule.
  \item Identify the symmetries of $\hat{H}$ and their consequences.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Dual-track content:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item \textit{Physical/chemical track:} Physical meaning of each term; energy scales ($\hat{V}_{ee}$ vs.\ $\hat{T}_e$ vs.\ $\hat{V}_{ne}$ for H$_2$); why $\hat{V}_{ee}$ is the source of difficulty.
  \item \textit{Mathematical track:} Schr\"odinger equation as a PDE; separation of COM motion; permutation group $S_{N_e}$; point groups as symmetry of the Hamiltonian operator.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: the molecular Hamiltonian as ``the rule book for quantum chemistry.''
Beg.\ UG: write $\hat{H}$ in atomic units for H$_2$; count degrees of freedom.
Adv.\ UG: symmetry operators that commute with $\hat{H}$; block-diagonal structure.
MSc: permutation symmetry of $\hat{H}$; parity; time-reversal; vibrational normal modes.
PhD: Born--Huang expansion; relativistic corrections (Breit--Pauli); quantum electrodynamic corrections.

\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- write $\hat{H}$ for H$_2$, H$_2$O, CH$_4$ in atomic units; count internal DOF.
Set~B --- symmetry analysis: which symmetry operators commute with $\hat{H}$ for a given point group?
Projects: (simple) plot potential energy terms vs.\ $r$ for H$_2^+$; (complex) relativistic corrections: mass--velocity, Darwin, spin--orbit for He using perturbation theory.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.1 / L02: Born--Oppenheimer Approximation and Adiabaticity}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Physical motivation: nuclei are $10^3$--$10^5$ times heavier than electrons; electronic motion is ``infinitely fast'' on nuclear timescale; decoupling ansatz $\Psi(\mathbf{r},\mathbf{R})=\psi_e(\mathbf{r};\mathbf{R})\chi(\mathbf{R})$; (20--45~min) Formal BO derivation: expand full wavefunction in adiabatic electronic states; project onto single state; leading BO approximation neglects non-adiabatic coupling $\mathbf{d}_{IJ}=\langle\psi_I|\nabla_\mathbf{R}|\psi_J\rangle/({E_J-E_I})$; adiabatic potential energy surface (PES) $V_I(\mathbf{R})=E_I(\mathbf{R})+V_{nn}(\mathbf{R})$; (45--65~min) Validity of BO: small $m_e/M_n$; large energy gap $E_J-E_I$; breakdown near conical intersections and avoided crossings; derivative couplings and non-adiabatic dynamics; (65--90~min) Beyond BO: Born--Huang expansion; diabatic states; non-adiabatic matrix elements; \emph{ab initio} molecular dynamics; Tully surface hopping; photochemistry and conical intersections (Jahn--Teller, Renner--Teller).

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Derive the BO approximation and state its validity conditions.
  \item Define the adiabatic PES and the derivative coupling $\mathbf{d}_{IJ}$.
  \item Explain conical intersections and their role in photochemistry.
  \item Describe the Born--Huang expansion and diabatic representations.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Dual-track content:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item \textit{Chemical track:} PES as the foundation of all molecular structure and dynamics; conical intersections in vision, photosynthesis, and photostability of DNA; Jahn--Teller distortions in transition metal complexes.
  \item \textit{Mathematical track:} Adiabatic theorem; Berry phase accumulated around a conical intersection; $\mathbf{d}_{IJ}$ as a gauge connection; diabatic vs.\ adiabatic gauge.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``nuclei are slow; electrons adjust instantly --- that's the Born--Oppenheimer idea.''
Beg.\ UG: BO ansatz; PES definition; validity conditions.
Adv.\ UG: formal BO derivation; derivative couplings; conical intersection definition.
MSc: Born--Huang expansion; diabatisation; Tully surface hopping.
PhD: geometric phase around CI; Longuet-Higgins sign change; exact factorisation of electron--nuclear wavefunction.

\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- write BO decoupling ansatz; identify conditions for BO validity; sketch a conical intersection seam.
Set~B --- derive the BO Hamiltonian; show derivative coupling diverges at CI; diabatisation matrix.
Projects: (simple) PES scan for H$_2$: BO vs.\ exact; (complex) conical intersection in H$_3$: geometric phase and Longuet-Higgins theorem.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.1 / L03: Parametric Dependence and the Feynman--Hellmann Theorem}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Parametric dependence of the electronic energy: $E(\lambda)=\langle\psi(\lambda)|\hat{H}(\lambda)|\psi(\lambda)\rangle$; first-order change in energy; (20--45~min) Feynman--Hellmann theorem: $\partial E/\partial\lambda=\langle\psi|\partial\hat{H}/\partial\lambda|\psi\rangle$; derivation from stationarity of energy; (45--65~min) Applications: nuclear forces from $\partial E/\partial R_{A\alpha}=-\langle\hat{F}_{A\alpha}\rangle$ (Hellmann--Feynman force); geometry optimisation algorithms (steepest descent, BFGS, L-BFGS); vibrational frequencies from second derivatives (Hessian); (65--90~min) Beyond first order: second derivatives and the coupled-perturbed HF/KS equations; analytic vs.\ numerical gradients; computational cost; NMR chemical shifts, IR intensities, polarisability as FH applications; connection to molecular response theory.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Derive the Feynman--Hellmann theorem from variational stationarity.
  \item Apply FH to compute nuclear forces and relate to geometry optimisation.
  \item Distinguish analytic gradients from numerical finite differences in cost.
  \item Describe coupled-perturbed equations for second-order properties.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Dual-track content:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item \textit{Computational chemistry track:} Geometry optimisation workflow; transition-state search; IRC; force-field parameterisation from ab initio gradients; NMR shielding from FH.
  \item \textit{Mathematical track:} FH as the quantum mechanical analogue of Darboux's theorem; Wigner's $2n+1$ rule; Dalgarno--Lewis perturbation theory.
\end{itemize}

\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``the force on a nucleus equals the electrostatic force from the electron density and other nuclei.''
Beg.\ UG: FH theorem derivation; HF force on H nucleus; steepest-descent geometry optimisation.
Adv.\ UG: analytic gradient for HF; BFGS; Hessian for frequencies.
MSc: coupled-perturbed HF/KS; analytic second derivatives; NMR shielding.
PhD: Wigner's $2n+1$ rule; Dalgarno--Lewis; response theory for arbitrary-order properties.

\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- FH theorem derivation; nuclear force on H in H$_2$; identify minimum from gradient.
Set~B --- analytic gradient derivation for HF; FH for NMR shielding; cost comparison analytic vs.\ numerical.
Projects: (simple) geometry optimisation of H$_2$O: energy and gradient at each BFGS step; (complex) FH theorem for polarisability: analytic vs.\ finite-difference comparison for HF/cc-pVDZ.
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[highlightbox]
\textbf{Module III.1 Reading:} Helgaker, J\o rgensen \& Olsen, Ch.~1--2; Born \& Oppenheimer (1927) original paper; Yarkony, Rev.\ Mod.\ Phys.\ \textbf{68}, 985 (1996) --- conical intersections.
\end{tcolorbox}

%=============================================================
\subsection{Module III.2 --- Principles of Molecular and Atomic Electronic Structure}
\label{sec:mod-III2}
%=============================================================

\subsubsection*{Module Overview}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Module III.2 Overview}
{\footnotesize
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lp{4.2cm}p{6.8cm}@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Lec.} & \textbf{Title} & \textbf{Key Concepts}\\
\midrule
L01 & The Quantum Many-Body Problem & Complexity; $N$-representability; curse of dimensionality\\
L02 & Hydrogenic Systems & Exact solution; $Z_{\rm eff}$; quantum defect; radial nodes\\
L03 & Polyelectronic Systems & He prototype; electron correlation; Coulomb/Fermi hole\\
L04 & Spin Orbitals \& Slater Screening & $\chi(\mathbf{x})=\phi(\mathbf{r})\sigma(s)$; Slater rules; shielding\\
L05 & Antisymmetry \& Slater Determinants & Pauli exclusion; Slater determinant; Slater--Condon rules\\
L06 & Restricted and Unrestricted Methods & RHF vs.\ UHF; spin contamination; ROHF\\
L07 & Variational Methods & Ritz; Hylleraas--Undheim; cusp condition; R12/F12\\
L08 & Configurations, Aufbau \& Virtuals & Aufbau; orbital energies; excited configurations\\
\midrule
L09 & Configuration Interaction & FCI; CISD; size consistency; Davidson correction\\
L10 & Hartree--Fock \& Correlation Energy & SCF; Roothaan--Hall; Koopman's; $E_{\rm corr}$\\
L11 & Orbital Theories \& Bonding & MO theory; VB theory; Coulson--Fischer; resonance\\
L12 & Natural and Localised Orbitals & NBO; NAO; Foster--Boys; DLPNO connection\\
L13 & Basis Sets I --- Function Types & STO; GTO; contraction; minimal; split-valence\\
L14 & Basis Sets II --- Standard Families & Pople; Dunning cc-pVXZ; Karlsruhe def2; ECP\\
L15 & Molecular Integral Schemes & Two-electron integrals; Obara--Saika; RI approximation\\
L16 & Glimpse into Solid State & PAW; plane-wave basis; Bloch electrons; band vs.\ MO\\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
}

\subsubsection*{Lecture-by-Lecture Syllabi}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Module III.2 Lecture Syllabi}

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.2 / L01: The Quantum Many-Body Problem in Chemistry}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) The electronic Schr\"odinger equation $\hat{H}_e\psi_e=E_e\psi_e$; why it cannot be solved exactly for $N_e>2$; exponential wall: Hilbert space dimension grows as $\binom{K}{N_e}$ for $K$ basis functions; (20--45~min) $N$-representability: which density matrices can arise from a physical $N$-electron wavefunction; necessary conditions on 1-RDM and 2-RDM; the $v$-representability problem in DFT; (45--65~min) Curse of dimensionality: wavefunction depends on $3N_e$ (+ spin) coordinates; grid methods infeasible; why we need orbital-based methods; (65--90~min) Systematic approximation hierarchy: HF $\to$ MP2 $\to$ CCSD(T) $\to$ FCI; cost scaling; accuracy benchmarks for small molecules; accuracy vs.\ cost trade-off as the central theme of quantum chemistry.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Explain the exponential complexity of the $N$-electron problem.
  \item State the $N$-representability conditions for the 1-RDM.
  \item Identify the systematic approximation hierarchy in quantum chemistry.
  \item Quantify the accuracy--cost trade-off for standard methods.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``quantum chemistry is hard because electrons interact and live in high-dimensional space.''
Beg.\ UG: Hilbert space dimension; method hierarchy; scaling table.
Adv.\ UG: $N$-representability conditions; $v$-representability; curse of dimensionality.
MSc: 2-RDM $N$-representability (P,Q,G conditions); Coleman's theorem; SDP.
PhD: quantum complexity of FCI; MA-hardness; quantum computing for quantum chemistry.
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- Hilbert space dimension for H$_2$O/STO-3G; accuracy table for methods on H$_2$.
Set~B --- $N$-representability conditions for 1-RDM; $v$-representability counterexample.
Projects: (simple) dimension and energy hierarchy for H$_2$ from STO-3G to FCI; (complex) SDP lower bound on FCI energy via 2-RDM.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.2 / L02: Hydrogenic Systems}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Hydrogen-like Hamiltonian $\hat{H}=-\tfrac{1}{2}\nabla^2-Z/r$ (atomic units); separation in spherical coordinates; radial and angular parts; (20--45~min) Exact solution: $\psi_{nlm}(r,\theta,\phi)=R_{nl}(r)Y_l^m(\theta,\phi)$; associated Laguerre polynomials for $R_{nl}$; energy $E_n=-Z^2/2n^2$; radial nodes $n-l-1$; angular nodes $l$; (45--65~min) One-electron atomic orbitals: $1s,2s,2p,3s,3p,3d$; shapes; nodal surfaces; radial probability density $4\pi r^2|R_{nl}|^2$; expectation values $\langle r\rangle,\langle r^2\rangle,\langle r^{-1}\rangle$; (65--90~min) Effective nuclear charge $Z_{\rm eff}$ and orbital exponents in multi-electron atoms; quantum defect for alkali atoms; penetration and shielding; connection to Slater orbitals and GTO basis functions.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Write and interpret the hydrogenic wavefunctions $\psi_{nlm}$.
  \item Compute radial probability densities and expectation values.
  \item Explain the concept of effective nuclear charge and quantum defect.
  \item Connect hydrogenic orbitals to Slater-type and Gaussian-type basis functions.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: shapes and nodal structure of atomic orbitals.
Beg.\ UG: radial wavefunctions; probability density; $\langle r\rangle$; orbital energies.
Adv.\ UG: derivation via Frobenius; quantum defect; $Z_{\rm eff}$ and shielding.
MSc: connection to STO exponents; pseudo-potential core replacement.
PhD: relativistic hydrogenic wavefunctions; Dirac equation for $Z_{\rm eff}\alpha\sim1$.
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- $\psi_{nlm}$ for $1s,2p_z$; radial density; $\langle r\rangle_{2p}$; energy ordering.
Set~B --- derive $E_n=-Z^2/2n^2$ from termination; $\langle r^{-1}\rangle$ for $1s$.
Projects: (simple) radial probability density plotter for all $n\leq3$ AOs; (complex) quantum defect for Li, Na, K: fit from experimental term values.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.2 / L03: Polyelectronic Systems and Electron Correlation}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Helium as prototype: $\hat{H}=-\tfrac{1}{2}\nabla_1^2-\tfrac{1}{2}\nabla_2^2-\tfrac{2}{r_1}-\tfrac{2}{r_2}+\tfrac{1}{r_{12}}$; exact solution impossible; perturbation theory ($1/r_{12}$ as perturbation); zeroth-order: product of hydrogenic $1s$; first-order correction $\langle1/r_{12}\rangle=5Z/8$; (20--45~min) Variational treatment: $Z_{\rm eff}$ as variational parameter; optimal $Z_{\rm eff}=Z-5/16$; comparison to exact; (45--65~min) Electron correlation: definition $E_{\rm corr}=E_{\rm exact}-E_{\rm HF}$; static (near-degeneracy) vs.\ dynamic (short-range) correlation; Coulomb hole and Fermi hole; angular correlation (left--right) in H$_2$; (65--90~min) Survey of correlation effects: dissociation energies; ionisation potentials; electron affinities; geometries; dipole moments; van der Waals interactions (London dispersion = pure correlation).

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Apply PT and variational method to the helium atom.
  \item Define and distinguish static and dynamic correlation.
  \item Explain the Coulomb hole and Fermi hole physically.
  \item Identify properties that are particularly sensitive to electron correlation.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: electrons avoid each other --- that's correlation; why chemistry needs it.
Beg.\ UG: He PT and variational; $E_{\rm corr}$ definition; static vs.\ dynamic.
Adv.\ UG: Coulomb and Fermi holes; left--right correlation in H$_2$; dispersion.
MSc: London dispersion from PT; correlation effects on PES; adiabatic connection.
PhD: transcorrelated methods; R12/F12 explicitly correlated wavefunctions; cusp condition.
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- He energy from PT and variational; optimal $Z_{\rm eff}$; $E_{\rm corr}$ for He.
Set~B --- Coulomb hole derivation; left--right correlation in H$_2$ from CI(2,2).
Projects: (simple) He energy: PT vs.\ variational vs.\ HF vs.\ FCI; (complex) H$_2$ correlation energy vs.\ bond length: dynamic to static crossover.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.2 / L04: Spin Orbitals, Slater Screening, and Effective Nuclear Charge}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Spin orbitals: $\chi(\mathbf{x})=\phi(\mathbf{r})\sigma(s)$ where $\sigma\in\{\alpha,\beta\}$; $\mathbf{x}=(\mathbf{r},s)$; orthonormality; (20--45~min) Slater's rules for $Z_{\rm eff}$: group electrons by $(1s), (2s,2p), (3s,3p), (3d), \ldots$; shielding contributions from inner and same-shell electrons; worked examples for B, Cl, Fe; limitation of Slater rules vs.\ computed $Z_{\rm eff}$; (45--65~min) Physical effects captured by $Z_{\rm eff}$: penetration of $s$ orbitals; orbital contraction; Clementi--Raimondi refined values; connection to orbital exponents in STO/GTO; (65--90~min) Periodic trends from $Z_{\rm eff}$: atomic radius, ionisation energy, electron affinity, electronegativity along period and down group; comparative analysis with experimental data.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Define spin orbitals and state their orthonormality relations.
  \item Apply Slater's rules to compute $Z_{\rm eff}$ for any element.
  \item Explain penetration, shielding, and orbital contraction.
  \item Predict periodic trends from $Z_{\rm eff}$.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: periodic trends from effective nuclear charge.
Beg.\ UG: spin orbitals; Slater rules for B, Cl, Fe; periodic trends.
Adv.\ UG: Clementi--Raimondi; connection to STO exponents; limitations of Slater.
MSc: relativistic contraction of $s,p$ orbitals in heavy atoms; pseudo-potentials from $Z_{\rm eff}$.
PhD: exact $Z_{\rm eff}$ from computed densities; Kohn--Sham $Z_{\rm eff}$; relativistic effective core potentials.
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- $Z_{\rm eff}$ for B, Si, Fe by Slater rules; periodic trend in $r_{\rm cov}$.
Set~B --- Clementi--Raimondi vs.\ Slater; orbital contraction in 4th period.
Projects: (simple) periodic table of $Z_{\rm eff}$ heatmap using Slater rules; (complex) $Z_{\rm eff}$ from HF electron density vs.\ Slater rules for 3d transition metals.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.2 / L05: Antisymmetry, Hartree Products, and Slater Determinants}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Indistinguishable electrons; Pauli exclusion; antisymmetry postulate $\hat{P}_{ij}\Psi=-\Psi$; (20--45~min) Hartree product: $\Psi_{\rm HP}=\chi_1(\mathbf{x}_1)\chi_2(\mathbf{x}_2)\cdots\chi_N(\mathbf{x}_N)$ --- not antisymmetric; antisymmetriser $\hat{\mathcal{A}}=\tfrac{1}{\sqrt{N!}}\sum_{\hat{P}}(-1)^p\hat{P}$; Slater determinant $\Phi=\hat{\mathcal{A}}[\chi_1\chi_2\cdots\chi_N]$; (45--65~min) Properties of Slater determinants: Pauli exclusion from determinant vanishing; exchange symmetry; overlap $\langle\Phi|\Phi\rangle=1$ for orthonormal spin orbitals; orbital rotation and the non-uniqueness of SDs; (65--90~min) Matrix elements of one- and two-body operators between SDs: Slater--Condon rules; $\langle\hat{O}_1\rangle$, $\langle\hat{O}_2\rangle$; application to the HF energy expression.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Construct a Slater determinant from a set of spin orbitals.
  \item Prove Pauli exclusion from the determinant structure.
  \item Apply Slater--Condon rules to evaluate matrix elements.
  \item Derive the Hartree--Fock energy from Slater--Condon rules.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``no two electrons can be in the same quantum state'' --- Pauli exclusion from antisymmetry.
Beg.\ UG: Slater determinant construction; Pauli exclusion; Slater--Condon rules.
Adv.\ UG: antisymmetriser; $N!$ terms; HF energy from Slater--Condon.
MSc: generalised Slater--Condon for multi-determinant wavefunctions.
PhD: second-quantisation derivation of Slater--Condon; matrix elements for CC theory.
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- construct $\Phi$ for He, Li; verify $\langle\Phi|\Phi\rangle=1$; Pauli exclusion.
Set~B --- Slater--Condon rules derivation; HF energy $E_{\rm HF}=\sum_i h_{ii}+\tfrac{1}{2}\sum_{ij}(J_{ij}-K_{ij})$.
Projects: (simple) Slater determinant for H$_2$: evaluate all integrals; (complex) Slater--Condon rules for doubly-substituted configuration: matrix element for CISD.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.2 / L06: Restricted and Unrestricted Methods}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Spin structure of HF: closed-shell (RHF) vs.\ open-shell; restricted open-shell (ROHF) and unrestricted (UHF); (20--45~min) RHF: $\phi_i^\alpha=\phi_i^\beta$; single set of spatial orbitals; correct spin eigenfunction; Roothaan--Hall equations $\mathbf{F}\mathbf{C}=\mathbf{S}\mathbf{C}\boldsymbol\varepsilon$ (details in L10); (45--65~min) UHF: separate $\alpha$ and $\beta$ orbital sets; Pople--Nesbet equations; lower variational energy than RHF; spin contamination $\langle\hat{S}^2\rangle_{\rm UHF}=S(S+1)+N_\beta-\sum_{ij}|\langle\phi_i^\alpha|\phi_j^\beta\rangle|^2$; (65--90~min) ROHF: constrained optimisation; pure spin eigenfunction; applications to radicals; half-open-shell systems; comparison of RHF, UHF, ROHF for dissociation of H$_2$; open-shell singlet states; broken-symmetry DFT.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Distinguish RHF, UHF, and ROHF and state their applicability.
  \item Compute the spin contamination of a UHF wavefunction.
  \item Explain why UHF gives lower energy than RHF for open-shell systems.
  \item Describe broken-symmetry DFT for biradicals.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``restricted'' = paired electrons; ``unrestricted'' = $\alpha$ and $\beta$ electrons optimised independently.
Beg.\ UG: RHF vs.\ UHF; spin contamination formula; H$_2$ dissociation.
Adv.\ UG: Pople--Nesbet equations; ROHF constraint; spin projection.
MSc: broken-symmetry DFT; spin contamination correction; ROHF for excited states.
PhD: GHF (generalised HF); spin--orbit coupling; non-collinear DFT.
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- $\langle\hat{S}^2\rangle_{\rm UHF}$ for O atom; energy ordering RHF vs.\ UHF for H$_2$.
Set~B --- Pople--Nesbet equations derivation; broken-symmetry DFT for H$_2$ at $r=3$~\AA.
Projects: (simple) RHF vs.\ UHF dissociation curve for H$_2$; (complex) spin contamination and spin projection for biradical singlet.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.2 / L07: Variational Methods}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Variational principle for ground state: $E[\Psi]=\langle\Psi|\hat{H}|\Psi\rangle/\langle\Psi|\Psi\rangle\geq E_0$; (20--45~min) Ritz method: linear ansatz $\ket{\Phi}=\sum_k c_k\ket{\chi_k}$; secular equation $\mathbf{H}\mathbf{c}=E\mathbf{S}\mathbf{c}$; Hylleraas--Undheim theorem: $N$ variational eigenvalues bound the exact ones from above; (45--65~min) Hylleraas function for He: $\psi=e^{-\alpha(r_1+r_2)}(1+\beta r_{12})$; dependence on inter-electron coordinate; cusp condition $(\partial\psi/\partial r_{12})|_{r_{12}=0}=\tfrac{1}{2}\psi(0)$; (65--90~min) Explicitly correlated methods (R12/F12): Slater geminal $e^{-\gamma r_{12}}$; resolution-of-identity; CABS (complementary auxiliary basis sets); accelerated basis-set convergence.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Apply the Ritz method to set up and solve the secular equation.
  \item State the Hylleraas--Undheim theorem and apply it.
  \item Derive the electron--electron cusp condition.
  \item Describe explicitly correlated R12/F12 methods.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: variational principle as ``upper bound guarantee.''
Beg.\ UG: secular equation; He with $Z_{\rm eff}$; Hylleraas--Undheim.
Adv.\ UG: cusp condition; Hylleraas wavefunction; convergence.
MSc: R12/F12 methods; CABS; explicitly correlated coupled cluster.
PhD: transcorrelated Hamiltonians; FCIQMC-R12; CCSD(T)-F12 benchmark accuracy.
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- secular equation for 2-basis He; Hylleraas--Undheim check; cusp condition.
Set~B --- cusp condition derivation; Hylleraas function for He: compute energy.
Projects: (simple) He energy from Hylleraas wavefunctions: convergence with terms; (complex) electron--electron cusp: R12 correction to HF energy for He.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.2 / L08: Electronic Configurations, Aufbau, and Virtual Orbitals}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Aufbau principle: fill lowest-energy orbitals first; $1s<2s<2p<3s<3p<4s<3d<\ldots$; anomalies (Cr, Cu); Madelung/$(n+l)$ rule; (20--45~min) Orbital energy ordering in polyelectronic atoms: $\varepsilon_i$ from HF; Koopmans' theorem (preview); orbital degeneracy and symmetry; occupations and electron configurations; term symbols (recap from II.3); (45--65~min) Virtual (unoccupied) orbitals: definition; basis-set dependence; canonical virtual orbitals; natural virtual orbitals (NVOs); their role in CI and CC; (65--90~min) Excited configurations: single, double, triple substitutions $\ket{\Phi_i^a},\ket{\Phi_{ij}^{ab}},\ldots$; excitation operators $\hat{a}^\dagger_a\hat{a}_i$; Brillouin's theorem; orthogonality to HF ground state; matrix elements for CI.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Apply the Aufbau principle and explain anomalies for Cr, Cu.
  \item Construct excited Slater determinants using excitation operators.
  \item Explain the role of virtual orbitals in post-HF methods.
  \item State Brillouin's theorem and its implication for CI.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: filling orbitals in order: the Aufbau principle and periodic table.
Beg.\ UG: electron configurations; Aufbau anomalies; excited configurations.
Adv.\ UG: canonical vs.\ natural virtual orbitals; Brillouin's theorem.
MSc: NVOs for local correlation; pair natural orbitals; orbital localisation.
PhD: optimal virtual space for DLPNO; projected AOs; pair correlation theories.
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- electron configurations for B, Fe, Cr; virtual orbital count for H$_2$O/6-31G*.
Set~B --- Brillouin's theorem derivation; canonical vs.\ NVO comparison.
Projects: (simple) aufbau anomalies: energy rationale for Cr vs.\ expected; (complex) NVO localisation for H$_2$O: compare canonical vs.\ Foster--Boys virtual orbitals.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.2 / L09: Configuration Interaction and the Exact Non-Relativistic Limit}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) CI expansion: $\ket{\Psi}=c_0\ket{\Phi_0}+\sum_{ia}c_i^a\ket{\Phi_i^a}+\sum_{ijab}c_{ij}^{ab}\ket{\Phi_{ij}^{ab}}+\cdots$; FCI = exact non-relativistic ground state within a given basis; (20--45~min) FCI properties: variational; size-consistent; basis-set limit = exact; FCI dimension $\binom{K}{N_\alpha}\binom{K}{N_\beta}$; exponential scaling; (45--65~min) Truncated CI: CIS (singles only; no correlation for ground state by Brillouin); CISD; CISDT; size inconsistency of truncated CI; $\langle\Psi_{N}|\hat{H}|\Psi_{N}\rangle \neq 2\langle\Psi_{N/2}|\hat{H}|\Psi_{N/2}\rangle$ for non-interacting monomers; Davidson correction $\Delta E_Q\approx(1-c_0^2)E_{\rm CISD}$; (65--90~min) Selected CI (SCI): CIPSI, ASCI, HCI algorithms; stochastic FCI; FCIQMC; convergence toward FCI; comparison with CCSD(T).

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Write the FCI expansion and state its properties.
  \item Explain size inconsistency of truncated CI and apply the Davidson correction.
  \item Describe selected CI algorithms (CIPSI, HCI).
  \item Compare FCI, CISD, and CCSD(T) in accuracy and scaling.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: FCI as the ``exact answer'' and why it's too expensive.
Beg.\ UG: CI expansion; FCI dimension; size inconsistency.
Adv.\ UG: Davidson correction; CISD scaling; selected CI idea.
MSc: CIPSI; FCIQMC; initiator approximation.
PhD: SCI extrapolation to FCI; stochastic-CASSCF; heat-bath CI.
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- FCI dimension for H$_2$/STO-3G; size inconsistency for He$_2$; Davidson correction.
Set~B --- prove size inconsistency of CISD; CIPSI selection criterion.
Projects: (simple) FCI vs.\ CISD for H$_2$: energy and $c_0^2$ vs.\ bond length; (complex) selected CI for N$_2$: CIPSI convergence toward FCI.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.2 / L10: Hartree--Fock Theory, Koopman's Theorem, and Correlation Energy}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) HF as variational optimisation of a Slater determinant; energy $E_{\rm HF}=\sum_i h_{ii}+\tfrac{1}{2}\sum_{ij}(J_{ij}-K_{ij})$; Coulomb $J_{ij}=\langle ij|ij\rangle$ and exchange $K_{ij}=\langle ij|ji\rangle$; (20--45~min) Fock operator $\hat{F}=\hat{h}+\sum_j(\hat{J}_j-\hat{K}_j)$; HF equations $\hat{F}\phi_i=\varepsilon_i\phi_i$; Roothaan--Hall in AO basis: $\mathbf{F}\mathbf{C}=\mathbf{S}\mathbf{C}\boldsymbol\varepsilon$; density matrix $\mathbf{P}=2\mathbf{C}_{\rm occ}\mathbf{C}_{\rm occ}^\dagger$; DIIS convergence acceleration; (45--65~min) Koopman's theorem: $\text{IP}_i\approx-\varepsilon_i$ (frozen-orbital approximation); $\text{EA}_a\approx-\varepsilon_a$; orbital relaxation and correlation corrections; (65--90~min) Correlation energy $E_{\rm corr}=E_{\rm exact}-E_{\rm HF}$; typical magnitudes ($\sim$1~eV per electron pair); dynamic and static contributions; the $T_1$ and $D_1$ diagnostic for multi-reference character; post-HF methods as corrections to HF.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Derive the HF equations from the variational principle.
  \item Set up and solve the Roothaan--Hall equations in an AO basis.
  \item Apply Koopman's theorem to estimate IPs and EAs.
  \item Define correlation energy and identify multi-reference character from diagnostics.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``HF gives 99\% of the energy but the remaining 1\% determines chemistry.''
Beg.\ UG: Fock operator; DIIS; Koopman's theorem; $E_{\rm corr}$ definition.
Adv.\ UG: Roothaan--Hall derivation; density matrix; Brillouin's theorem.
MSc: $T_1/D_1$ diagnostics; orbital relaxation vs.\ correlation; OMP2.
PhD: Brueckner orbitals; orbital-optimised CC; HF saddle point.
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- HF energy for He; Koopman's IPs; $E_{\rm corr}$ for Ne.
Set~B --- Roothaan--Hall derivation; density matrix idempotency; DIIS error vector.
Projects: (simple) HF SCF for H$_2$O/STO-3G: convergence and Koopman's IPs; (complex) correlation energy per electron pair across noble gas series.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.2 / L11: Orbital Theories and Bonding Models}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Two paradigms: MO theory (delocalised) and Valence Bond theory (localised, resonance); complementary descriptions; (20--45~min) MO theory: LCAO--MO; bonding, antibonding, non-bonding MOs; correlation diagrams; Walsh diagrams; orbital symmetry and frontier MO theory; HOMO--LUMO gap; (45--65~min) VB theory: Heitler--London wavefunction for H$_2$; ionic and covalent resonance structures; Coulson--Fischer wavefunction: intermediate between MO and VB; resonance in benzene; (65--90~min) Modern VB methods: spin-coupled VB; VBSCF; BOVB; GVB; comparison to CASSCF; VB interpretation of chemical bonding.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Construct and interpret MO correlation diagrams.
  \item Write the Heitler--London and Coulson--Fischer wavefunctions for H$_2$.
  \item Explain resonance structures in VB theory.
  \item Compare MO and VB descriptions and identify when each is more appropriate.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: bonding and antibonding orbitals; resonance structures.
Beg.\ UG: MO correlation diagrams; Heitler--London; resonance in benzene.
Adv.\ UG: Coulson--Fischer; GVB; MO--VB connection.
MSc: VBSCF; spin-coupled VB; BOVB.
PhD: modern VB theories; VB interpretation of aromaticity; VB-CI.
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- MO diagram for N$_2$, O$_2$, F$_2$; VB resonance for benzene; Heitler--London for H$_2$.
Set~B --- Coulson--Fischer wavefunction: ionic/covalent mixing; GVB pair functions.
Projects: (simple) MO vs.\ VB energy for H$_2$: ionic content vs.\ $R$; (complex) VBSCF for allyl radical: spin-coupled vs.\ delocalised picture.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.2 / L12: Natural and Localised Orbitals}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Why localised orbitals? Chemical intuition; transferability; local correlation methods; (20--45~min) Natural orbitals (NOs) from 1-RDM: eigenfunctions of $\gamma(\mathbf{r};\mathbf{r}')$; occupation numbers $n_i\in[0,2]$; multi-reference diagnostics from NOONs; (45--65~min) Natural Bond Orbitals (NBOs): Lewis-structure-based orthogonal localisation; core, lone-pair, and bond NBOs; NBO charge analysis; Natural Population Analysis (NPA); Natural Atomic Orbitals (NAOs); (65--90~min) Localisation methods for MOs: Foster--Boys ($\sum_i\langle r^2\rangle_i - \langle r\rangle_i^2$ minimised); Pipek--Mezey (maximise atomic populations); Edmiston--Ruedenberg (maximise self-repulsion); comparison; use in DLPNO-CCSD(T) and pair natural orbital methods.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Compute NOONs and interpret them as a multi-reference diagnostic.
  \item Describe the NBO procedure and NPA charge analysis.
  \item Apply Foster--Boys and Pipek--Mezey localisation.
  \item Connect localised orbitals to local correlation methods.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: localised orbitals as ``lone pairs and bonds'' --- connecting quantum chemistry to Lewis structures.
Beg.\ UG: NOs and NOONs; NBO for water; NPA charges.
Adv.\ UG: Foster--Boys localisation; NOON diagnostic; Pipek--Mezey.
MSc: DLPNO connection; PNOs from 2-RDM; BOYS localisation gradient.
PhD: intrinsic bond orbitals (IBO); AVAS; automatic active space selection from NOONs.
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- NBO for H$_2$O: identify lone pairs; NPA charges; NOON for H$_2$ at 2$R_e$.
Set~B --- Foster--Boys localisation criterion; derivation of gradient; comparison with Pipek--Mezey.
Projects: (simple) NBO/NPA analysis for a series of molecules; (complex) NOON diagnostic: HF vs.\ FCI NOONs for N$_2$ dissociation.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.2 / L13: Basis Sets I --- Types of Functions}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Why basis sets? LCAO expansion; finite basis approximation; basis set error = incompleteness; (20--45~min) Slater-type orbitals (STO): $\chi^{\rm STO}_{nlm}=Nr^{n-1}e^{-\zeta r}Y_l^m$; correct cusp and asymptotic; expensive two-electron integrals (Boys 1950 Gaussian workaround); Gaussian-type orbitals (GTO): $\chi^{\rm GTO}_{lmn}=Nx^ly^mz^ne^{-\alpha r^2}$; product theorem; (45--65~min) Contraction: $\phi_\mu=\sum_k d_{\mu k}\chi_k^{\rm GTO}$; segmented vs.\ general contraction; minimal basis (1 function/occupied AO); split-valence (double/triple zeta); polarisation ($d$ on heavy, $p$ on H); diffuse functions (for anions and Rydbergs); (65--90~min) Quality indicators: basis set superposition error (BSSE); counterpoise correction (Boys--Bernardi); basis set incompleteness error (BSIE); CBS extrapolation; approximate completeness via RI/density fitting.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Define STO and GTO and explain why GTOs are used in practice.
  \item Describe contraction schemes and the meaning of split-valence, polarised, and diffuse.
  \item Define BSSE and apply the counterpoise correction.
  \item Explain BSIE and CBS extrapolation.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: basis functions as the ``building blocks'' for molecular orbitals.
Beg.\ UG: STO vs.\ GTO; contraction; minimal and split-valence; BSSE.
Adv.\ UG: BSSE counterpoise; BSIE vs.\ correlation error; RI approximation.
MSc: general contraction; CBS extrapolation formulae; resolution-of-identity.
PhD: basis set design principles; even-tempered series; optimisation of exponents for FCI.
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- GTO product theorem; contraction for 6-31G*; BSSE for He$_2$ at 3~\AA.
Set~B --- STO-nG contraction: fit STO with $n$ Gaussians; counterpoise correction derivation.
Projects: (simple) BSSE for H$_2$O dimer vs.\ basis set; (complex) CBS extrapolation for He correlation energy: Dunning cc-pVDZ through cc-pV5Z.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.2 / L14: Basis Sets II --- Standard Basis Families}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Overview of the major families: Pople, Dunning correlation-consistent, Karlsruhe def2, ANO, Sapporo; design philosophy of each; (20--45~min) Pople basis sets: 3-21G, 6-31G*, 6-311++G**; notation; polarisation and diffuse; historical prevalence; (45--65~min) Dunning cc-pVXZ ($X=D,T,Q,5,6$): hierarchical; designed for CBS extrapolation; aug-cc-pVXZ (with diffuse); cc-pCVXZ (core--valence); cc-pwCVXZ (weighted); (65--90~min) Karlsruhe def2-SVP, def2-TZVP, def2-QZVP: efficient segmented contraction; ECP for $Z\geq37$; Ahlrichs ECPs; Dunning ECPs (cc-pVXZ-PP); comparison on a benchmark set; practical choice guide.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Decode basis set notation (Pople, Dunning, def2).
  \item Select an appropriate basis set for a given property and accuracy target.
  \item Explain effective core potentials and when to use them.
  \item Apply CBS extrapolation using the Dunning cc-pVXZ hierarchy.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: practical guide to basis set selection.
Beg.\ UG: decode 6-31G*, cc-pVDZ, def2-TZVP; select for geometry vs.\ energy.
Adv.\ UG: CBS extrapolation; ECP choice; core--valence cc-pCVXZ.
MSc: ANO basis sets; CABS for F12; basis set optimisation.
PhD: basis set extrapolation theory; explicitly correlated basis-set convergence; periodic basis sets.
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- decode basis set notation; select basis for H$_2$O geometry vs.\ interaction energy.
Set~B --- CBS extrapolation for Ne: Helgaker formula; core--valence effect on Cu ionisation.
Projects: (simple) basis set convergence for H$_2$O: geometry and energy from STO-3G to aug-cc-pV5Z; (complex) ECP vs.\ all-electron for Au: relativistic effects on bond length.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.2 / L15: Molecular Integral Schemes}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) The two-electron integral bottleneck: $(\mu\nu|\lambda\sigma)=\int\int\phi_\mu(\mathbf{r}_1)\phi_\nu(\mathbf{r}_1)\tfrac{1}{r_{12}}\phi_\lambda(\mathbf{r}_2)\phi_\sigma(\mathbf{r}_2)d\mathbf{r}_1d\mathbf{r}_2$; formally $\mathcal{O}(K^4)$; (20--45~min) Obara--Saika recurrence relations: generate higher angular momentum integrals from $s$-type; vertical and horizontal recurrence; computational savings; (45--65~min) Resolution-of-identity (RI/density fitting) approximation: $(\mu\nu|\lambda\sigma)\approx\sum_{PQ}(\mu\nu|P)(P|Q)^{-1}(Q|\lambda\sigma)$; auxiliary basis $\{P\}$; reduces to $\mathcal{O}(K^3)$; Coulomb and exchange RI; (65--90~min) Modern integral algorithms: linear-scaling methods (J-engine, LinK); screening (Schwarz); GPU implementations; integral-direct algorithms; resolution of identity for MP2 and CC; RIJCOSX for large molecules.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Write the two-electron repulsion integral and identify its computational complexity.
  \item Describe the Obara--Saika recurrence and its efficiency gain.
  \item Explain the RI approximation and its error and cost.
  \item Describe Schwarz screening and linear-scaling integral algorithms.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: molecular integrals as the computational cost of quantum chemistry.
Beg.\ UG: two-electron integral definition; $\mathcal{O}(K^4)$ scaling; RI approximation.
Adv.\ UG: Obara--Saika recurrence; Schwarz screening; RI error analysis.
MSc: RIJCOSX; GPU implementation; linear-scaling density fitting.
PhD: Boys function; McMurchie--Davidson; Gill's PRISM; adaptive integral algorithms.
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- count two-electron integrals for H$_2$O/STO-3G; RI approximation error estimate.
Set~B --- Obara--Saika for $s$-$p$ integrals; Schwarz screening criterion derivation.
Projects: (simple) RI error vs.\ auxiliary basis size for HF/def2-TZVP; (complex) timing benchmark: conventional vs.\ RI-MP2 for linear alkane chain.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.2 / L16: Glimpse into the Solid State}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Periodic systems: Bloch's theorem $\psi_{n\mathbf{k}}(\mathbf{r})=u_{n\mathbf{k}}(\mathbf{r})e^{i\mathbf{k}\cdot\mathbf{r}}$; crystal momentum; band structure vs.\ MO picture; (20--45~min) Plane-wave basis: $\phi_\mathbf{G}(\mathbf{r})=e^{i(\mathbf{k}+\mathbf{G})\cdot\mathbf{r}}/\sqrt{\Omega}$; kinetic energy cutoff $E_{\rm cut}$; completeness and convergence; (45--65~min) Projector augmented-wave (PAW) method: all-electron quality with plane-wave efficiency; PAW transformation; frozen-core PAW; comparison with pseudopotentials (norm-conserving, ultrasoft); (65--90~min) GTO basis sets for solids (Crystal, CP2K): comparison with plane waves; advantages and disadvantages; k-point sampling; Gamma-point approximation; periodic MP2 and CC with GTOs; $\Gamma$-point CCSD(T) for solids; outlook.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item State Bloch's theorem and explain crystal momentum and band structure.
  \item Describe plane-wave basis sets and the role of the energy cutoff.
  \item Explain the PAW method and compare with pseudopotentials.
  \item Compare GTO and plane-wave approaches for periodic quantum chemistry.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: from molecules to crystals --- how symmetry simplifies the problem.
Beg.\ UG: Bloch's theorem; plane-wave basis; band structure concept.
Adv.\ UG: PAW method; GTO vs.\ PW; k-point sampling.
MSc: periodic MP2; CCSD(T) for solids; GTO-based periodic codes.
PhD: diagrammatic MBPT for periodic systems; stochastic CCSD(T) for solids; quantum Monte Carlo for bulk.
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- Bloch states for 1D chain; plane-wave cutoff for Si; band gap vs.\ k-point density.
Set~B --- PAW transformation derivation; GTO vs.\ PW cost comparison for periodic HF.
Projects: (simple) tight-binding band structure for graphene; (complex) periodic HF/GTO vs.\ DFT/PW for LiH crystal: lattice constant and band gap.
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[highlightbox]
\textbf{Module III.2 Reading:} Helgaker, J\o rgensen \& Olsen, \textit{Molecular Electronic-Structure Theory} (Wiley) --- primary reference; Szabo \& Ostlund, \textit{Modern Quantum Chemistry} (Dover); Jensen, \textit{Introduction to Computational Chemistry}; Cramer, \textit{Essentials of Computational Chemistry}.
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsection{Module III.3 --- Density Functional Theory and Beyond}
\label{sec:mod-III3}
%=============================================================

\subsubsection*{Module Overview}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Module III.3 Overview}

{\footnotesize

\subsubsection*{Lecture-by-Lecture Syllabi}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Module III.3 Lecture Syllabi}

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.3 / L01: Hohenberg--Kohn Theorems}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Motivation: the electron density $\rho(\mathbf{r})$ is a 3D function vs.\ the $3N_e$-dimensional wavefunction; if $\rho$ determines everything, enormous simplification; (20--45~min) HK Theorem 1: for any system of $N$ electrons under an external potential $v_{\rm ext}$, the ground-state density $\rho_0(\mathbf{r})$ uniquely determines $v_{\rm ext}(\mathbf{r})$ (up to a constant); proof by reductio ad absurdum; (45--65~min) HK Theorem 2: the exact ground-state energy is the minimum of $E_v[\rho]=F_{\rm HK}[\rho]+\int v_{\rm ext}\rho\,d\mathbf{r}$ over all $v$-representable densities; universal functional $F_{\rm HK}[\rho]=T[\rho]+V_{ee}[\rho]$; (65--90~min) Limitations: $v$-representability (not all $\rho$ arise from a ground state of some $v_{\rm ext}$); $N$-representability of densities; the Levy--Lieb constrained-search reformulation avoids $v$-representability; excited states (Gross--Oliveira--Kohn); ensemble DFT.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Prove the first HK theorem by contradiction.
  \item State the second HK theorem and identify the universal functional.
  \item Explain the $v$-representability problem.
  \item Describe the Levy--Lieb constrained-search and its advantage.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``the electron density contains all information about a molecule.''
Beg.\ UG: HK1 proof sketch; HK2 variational principle; $F_{\rm HK}[\rho]$.
Adv.\ UG: $v$-representability; Levy--Lieb; ensemble DFT.
MSc: Lieb's convex conjugate; subdifferential; functional derivatives in DFT.
PhD: Moreau--Yosida regularisation; N-representability of $\rho$; adiabatic connection.
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- prove HK1 by contradiction; identify $F_{\rm HK}$ for He; variational principle check.
Set~B --- Levy--Lieb constrained search derivation; $v$-representability counterexample.
Projects: (simple) HK1 visualisation: two different $v_{\rm ext}$ cannot give same $\rho_0$; (complex) Levy--Lieb: evaluate $F_{\rm HK}[\rho]$ for He by constrained optimisation.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.3 / L02: Thomas--Fermi--Weizs\"acker Theory}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Orbital-free DFT: express total energy entirely as a functional of $\rho(\mathbf{r})$; Thomas--Fermi kinetic energy $T_{\rm TF}[\rho]=C_F\int\rho^{5/3}d\mathbf{r}$ from homogeneous electron gas; (20--45~min) Thomas--Fermi total energy $E_{\rm TF}[\rho]=T_{\rm TF}+\int v_{\rm ext}\rho\,d\mathbf{r}+J[\rho]+E_{\rm xc}^{\rm LDA}[\rho]$; Euler--Lagrange equation; Thomas--Fermi equation $\mu=C_F\rho^{2/3}+v_{\rm ext}+v_H+v_{\rm xc}$; (45--65~min) Weizs\"acker correction $T_W[\rho]=\tfrac{1}{8}\int|\nabla\rho|^2/\rho\,d\mathbf{r}$; gradient expansion (GEA); performance: wrong shell structure, no binding for atoms, no molecular binding; (65--90~min) Modern orbital-free DFT: Wang--Teter; Carter kinetic energy functionals; application to large-scale simulations of metals; keDF machine learning; limitations for covalent systems.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Derive the TF kinetic energy from the homogeneous electron gas.
  \item Set up and solve the TF Euler--Lagrange equation.
  \item State the Weizs\"acker correction and explain its physical origin.
  \item Describe the limitations of TF theory and modern orbital-free DFT.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``Thomas--Fermi is the simplest density functional theory.''
Beg.\ UG: TF kinetic energy; TF equation; Weizs\"acker; known failures.
Adv.\ UG: gradient expansion; $T_W$ derivation; comparison with KS.
MSc: Wang--Teter functional; orbital-free MD for metals.
PhD: conjoint gradient expansion; non-local kinetic energy functionals; ML-keDF.
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- TF equation for H atom; Weizs\"acker correction; identify TF failures.
Set~B --- derive $T_{\rm TF}$ from HEG; gradient expansion to second order.
Projects: (simple) TF density for He: compare to exact; (complex) orbital-free DFT for Al: Wang--Teter vs.\ KS.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.3 / L03: Kohn--Sham DFT}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Kohn--Sham idea: introduce a non-interacting reference system with the same density as the interacting system; KS kinetic energy $T_s[\rho]=\sum_i\langle\phi_i|-\tfrac{1}{2}\nabla^2|\phi_i\rangle$; (20--45~min) KS equations: $[-\tfrac{1}{2}\nabla^2+v_{\rm eff}(\mathbf{r})]\phi_i(\mathbf{r})=\varepsilon_i\phi_i(\mathbf{r})$ with $v_{\rm eff}=v_{\rm ext}+v_H+v_{\rm xc}$; XC potential $v_{\rm xc}=\delta E_{\rm xc}/\delta\rho$; self-consistent field loop; (45--65~min) Adiabatic connection formula: $E_{\rm xc}=\int_0^1 d\lambda\langle\Psi^\lambda|\hat{V}_{ee}-\hat{J}|\Psi^\lambda\rangle$; XC hole; exact conditions on $E_{\rm xc}$: negativity of XC hole, sum rule $\int\rho_{\rm xc}d\mathbf{r}=-1$; (65--90~min) KS DFT in practice: basis set expansion of KS orbitals; Coulomb and XC integrals; DIIS; convergence; computational scaling $\mathcal{O}(K^3)$ for hybrid; $\mathcal{O}(K)$ linear-scaling DFT; comparison with HF.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Derive the KS equations from the HK variational principle.
  \item Define the XC energy and potential and their exact properties.
  \item Describe the KS SCF algorithm and its scaling.
  \item Explain the adiabatic connection and the XC hole.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``KS DFT maps the interacting problem onto non-interacting electrons in an effective potential.''
Beg.\ UG: KS equations; effective potential; SCF loop; LDA.
Adv.\ UG: adiabatic connection; XC hole; exact conditions.
MSc: XC sum rule; self-interaction error; linear-response TDDFT.
PhD: ensemble KS DFT; optimised effective potential (OEP); exact exchange.
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- KS equations for He with LDA; identify $v_{\rm xc}$; SCF convergence check.
Set~B --- derive KS equations from $E[\rho]$; adiabatic connection formula.
Projects: (simple) KS SCF for H$_2$O with LDA: density and KS eigenvalues; (complex) adiabatic connection integrand for He: $\lambda$-dependence of $E_{\rm xc}^\lambda$.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.3 / L04: Overview of XC Functionals --- Jacob's Ladder}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Perdew's Jacob's ladder: LDA, GGA, meta-GGA, hybrid GGA, double hybrid --- each rung adds one more ingredient; (20--45~min) LDA: $E_{\rm xc}^{\rm LDA}=\int\epsilon_{\rm xc}^{\rm HEG}(\rho)\rho\,d\mathbf{r}$; Dirac exchange; Vosko--Wilk--Nusair correlation; PW92; accuracy and systematic overbinding; GGA: $E_{\rm xc}^{\rm GGA}[\rho,|\nabla\rho|]$; PBE (parameter-free); B88 exchange; LYP correlation; B3LYP (empirical hybrid); (45--65~min) meta-GGA: kinetic energy density $\tau=\sum_i|\nabla\phi_i|^2/2$; TPSS; SCAN; MN15; range-separated hybrids: $v_{ee}=\tfrac{1-\text{erf}(\omega r)}{r}+\tfrac{\text{erf}(\omega r)}{r}$; CAM-B3LYP; HSE06; (65--90~min) Double hybrids: $E_{\rm xc}^{\rm DH}=a_x E_x^{\rm HF}+(1-a_x)E_x^{\rm GGA}+a_c E_c^{\rm GGA}+b_c E_c^{\rm MP2}$; B2-PLYP; $\mathcal{O}(N^5)$ scaling; accuracy compared to CCSD(T); dispersion corrections: D3, D3BJ, MBD, VV10; practical guidance for choosing functionals.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Describe each rung of Jacob's ladder and its new ingredient.
  \item State the key properties and failures of LDA, PBE, and B3LYP.
  \item Explain range-separated hybrids and when to use them.
  \item Choose an appropriate functional for a given property and accuracy target.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: Jacob's ladder as a guide to increasingly accurate DFT.
Beg.\ UG: LDA, PBE, B3LYP; when to use each; dispersion corrections.
Adv.\ UG: meta-GGA; range-separated hybrids; B2-PLYP double hybrid.
MSc: SCAN; MBD dispersion; GMTKN55 benchmark comparison.
PhD: self-interaction correction; OEP exact exchange; DFT+U; ACFDT-RPA.
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- identify rung for SCAN, CAM-B3LYP, B2-PLYP; choose functional for H-bond energy.
Set~B --- PBE exchange enhancement factor derivation; B2-PLYP energy expression.
Projects: (simple) Jacob's ladder benchmark for atomisation energies: LDA/PBE/B3LYP/B2-PLYP vs.\ CCSD(T); (complex) dispersion corrections for rare-gas dimers: D3 vs.\ MBD vs.\ VV10.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.3 / L05: Useful DFT Quantities --- Fukui Functions and Reactivity Indices}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Conceptual DFT: chemical potential $\mu=(\partial E/\partial N)_v=-\chi$ (negative of electronegativity); chemical hardness $\eta=\tfrac{1}{2}(\partial^2 E/\partial N^2)_v$; (20--45~min) Fukui functions: $f^+(\mathbf{r})=\rho_{N+1}(\mathbf{r})-\rho_N(\mathbf{r})$ (nucleophilic attack site); $f^-(\mathbf{r})=\rho_N(\mathbf{r})-\rho_{N-1}(\mathbf{r})$ (electrophilic attack); $f^0=\tfrac{1}{2}(f^++f^-)$ (radical); finite-difference approximation; Fukui from frontier orbitals; (45--65~min) Yang--Parr local softness $s^\pm(\mathbf{r})=Sf^\pm(\mathbf{r})$; electrophilicity index $\omega=\mu^2/2\eta$; hardness--softness complementarity; HSAB principle; (65--90~min) Dual descriptor $\Delta f(\mathbf{r})=f^+-f^-$; identifies nucleophilic ($\Delta f<0$) and electrophilic ($\Delta f>0$) sites simultaneously; constrained DFT (CDFT) for charge-transfer states; non-covalent interaction (NCI) plots; reduced density gradient; applications in organic and organometallic reactivity.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Define chemical potential, hardness, and electronegativity in DFT.
  \item Compute Fukui functions $f^\pm$ from frontier orbital densities.
  \item Apply the HSAB principle using hardness and Fukui functions.
  \item Interpret the dual descriptor and NCI plots for reactivity analysis.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``Fukui functions point to where a molecule is most reactive.''
Beg.\ UG: $f^\pm$ from frontier orbitals; HOMO/LUMO as reactivity sites; HSAB.
Adv.\ UG: Fukui from density difference; dual descriptor; electrophilicity.
MSc: CDFT for CT states; NCI analysis; chemical softness and polarisability.
PhD: DFT $N$-derivative discontinuity; derivative of chemical potential; ensemble DFT for Fukui.
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- compute $f^\pm$ from HOMO/LUMO for formaldehyde; hardness for hard/soft acids.
Set~B --- dual descriptor for acrolein: identify nucleophilic and electrophilic sites.
Projects: (simple) Fukui function map for a series of carbonyl compounds; (complex) CDFT for charge transfer in push-pull chromophore: ground vs.\ CT state densities.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.3 / L06: Tight-Binding and Effective Hamiltonians}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) LCAO tight-binding Hamiltonian: $H_{ij}=\langle\phi_i|\hat{H}|\phi_j\rangle$; hopping $t_{ij}$ and on-site $\varepsilon_i$; connection to DFT Hamiltonian matrix elements; (20--45~min) Slater--Koster two-centre approximation: parametrise $H_{ij}$ by bond type ($ss\sigma$, $sp\sigma$, $pp\sigma$, $pp\pi$, $\ldots$) and distance; tables of Slater--Koster integrals; applications: Si band structure, graphene Dirac cone; (45--65~min) Su--Schrieffer--Heeger (SSH) model: 1D chain with alternating hoppings $t,t'$; topological insulator; bulk-boundary correspondence; chiral symmetry; edge states; (65--90~min) DFTB (density functional tight-binding): repulsive pair potential from DFT; self-consistent charge (SCC-DFTB); applications to bio- and nano-systems; GFN-xTB for non-covalent interactions; parametrisation strategies.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Set up a tight-binding Hamiltonian using Slater--Koster parameters.
  \item Compute the band structure for a 1D chain and graphene.
  \item Describe the SSH model and identify its topological edge states.
  \item Explain DFTB and its relation to DFT.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: tight-binding as a simple model for electrons in solids.
Beg.\ UG: 1D chain; hopping; band structure; graphene Dirac cone.
Adv.\ UG: Slater--Koster; SSH model; topological edge states.
MSc: SCC-DFTB; GFN-xTB; applications to bio-systems.
PhD: DFTB parametrisation; non-orthogonal TB; Berry phase in TB models.
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- 1D TB chain: band structure and DOS; Dirac cone for graphene.
Set~B --- SSH model: bulk-boundary correspondence; edge state energies.
Projects: (simple) TB band structure for graphene and hBN: compare Dirac cones; (complex) SSH model: topological phase transition as $t'/t$ varies.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.3 / L07: H\"uckel and M\"obius Aromaticity}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Simple H\"uckel MO theory: $\alpha$ and $\beta$ parameters; secular determinant; MO energies and coefficients for ethylene, allyl, butadiene; (20--45~min) Benzene and aromaticity: $4n+2$ H\"uckel rule; delocalisation energy; resonance energy; anti-aromaticity ($4n$); NICS (nucleus-independent chemical shift) as probe; (45--65~min) M\"obius topology: $4n$ electrons aromatic on M\"obius ring; $4n+2$ anti-aromatic; Heilbronner's prediction (1964); twisted annulene experiments; (65--90~min) Woodward--Hoffmann rules: orbital symmetry conservation; pericyclic reactions; thermal and photochemical; Frontier Molecular Orbital (FMO) theory; HOMO--LUMO interactions; electrocyclic reactions; cycloadditions; sigmatropic rearrangements.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Apply H\"uckel theory to compute MO energies for $\pi$ systems.
  \item State H\"uckel's $4n+2$ rule and explain aromaticity/anti-aromaticity.
  \item Describe M\"obius aromaticity and contrast with H\"uckel.
  \item Apply Woodward--Hoffmann rules to predict pericyclic reaction outcomes.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: aromaticity from H\"uckel rule; why benzene is stable.
Beg.\ UG: H\"uckel for ethylene--benzene; aromatic stabilisation energy; W--H rules.
Adv.\ UG: NICS; M\"obius topology; FMO theory for cycloadditions.
MSc: beyond H\"uckel: extended H\"uckel; aromatic transition states.
PhD: magnetic aromaticity indices; ACID plots; spherical aromaticity (fullerenes).
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- H\"uckel MO energies for benzene; resonance energy; W--H rule for [4+2].
Set~B --- M\"obius aromatic [8]annulene: H\"uckel vs.\ M\"obius electron count.
Projects: (simple) H\"uckel MO solver for arbitrary acyclic and cyclic $\pi$ systems; (complex) Woodward--Hoffmann correlation diagram for thermal vs.\ photochemical ring closure.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.3 / L08: Crystal Field Theory}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Transition metal complexes: $d$ orbitals in the field of ligands; point-charge model; electrostatic perturbation of $d$-orbital energies; (20--45~min) Octahedral field: $O_h$ point group; $d$ orbitals split into $t_{2g}$ ($d_{xy},d_{xz},d_{yz}$) and $e_g$ ($d_{z^2},d_{x^2-y^2}$); crystal field splitting $\Delta_o=10Dq$; energy: $t_{2g}=-4Dq$, $e_g=+6Dq$; (45--65~min) High-spin vs.\ low-spin: pairing energy $P$ vs.\ $\Delta_o$; configuration d$^4$--d$^7$ have two possibilities; spectrochemical series $I^-<Br^-<Cl^-<F^-<OH^-<H_2O<NH_3<en<CO<CN^-$; CFSE (crystal field stabilisation energy); (65--90~min) Tetrahedral field: $\Delta_t=\tfrac{4}{9}\Delta_o$; square-planar field: strong field; Jahn--Teller effect: distortion for $e_g^1$, $e_g^3$ ($d^9$, Cu$^{2+}$); elongation vs.\ compression; applications: colour of complexes, magnetic moments.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Derive the $d$-orbital splitting in octahedral and tetrahedral fields.
  \item Determine high-spin vs.\ low-spin configurations from $\Delta_o$ and $P$.
  \item Apply the spectrochemical series.
  \item Explain the Jahn--Teller effect and identify susceptible configurations.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: why transition metal complexes are coloured; high-spin vs.\ low-spin.
Beg.\ UG: octahedral splitting; $t_{2g}/e_g$; CFSE; spin states.
Adv.\ UG: tetrahedral; square planar; Jahn--Teller; spectrochemical series.
MSc: $10Dq$ from group theory; selection rules for $d$--$d$ transitions; Orgel diagrams.
PhD: CFT from first principles (DFT+U); multiplet theory; dynamical Jahn--Teller.
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- $d$ orbital splitting for Fe$^{3+}$ in octahedral field; CFSE for high-spin d$^6$; $\Delta_t$ from $\Delta_o$.
Set~B --- Jahn--Teller distortion for Cu$^{2+}$; derive $t_{2g}$ and $e_g$ energies from point-charge model.
Projects: (simple) colour of octahedral Ti$^{3+}$ complex from $\Delta_o$; (complex) Jahn--Teller distortion in CuF$_2$: Q-mode potential energy surface.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.3 / L09: Ligand Field Theory}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) LFT vs.\ CFT: LFT treats covalency; MO description of metal--ligand bonding; $\sigma$ and $\pi$ donor/acceptor ligands; (20--45~min) Angular overlap model (AOM): $e_\sigma,e_\pi$ parameters; energy from angular overlap geometry factors $F_{lm}(\theta,\phi)$; comparison with Slater--Koster; applications for arbitrary geometries; (45--65~min) Tanabe--Sugano diagrams: energy levels for d$^n$ configurations in octahedral field; Racah parameters $A,B,C$ (electron repulsion); spin-orbit coupling; term symbols for free ion and complex; (65--90~min) Nephelauxetic effect: reduction of Racah $B$ parameter in complex vs.\ free ion; $\beta=B_{\rm complex}/B_{\rm free}$; covalency measure; connection to charge transfer; magnetic moments and spin-orbit coupling in heavy metal complexes; $g$-tensor from EPR.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Apply the angular overlap model to compute $d$-orbital energies.
  \item Read and interpret Tanabe--Sugano diagrams.
  \item Define the nephelauxetic effect and its relation to covalency.
  \item Compute magnetic moments and $g$-tensors from LFT.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: LFT as the bridge between crystal field and full MO theory.
Beg.\ UG: AOM; Tanabe--Sugano for Cr$^{3+}$; nephelauxetic ratio.
Adv.\ UG: $e_\sigma,e_\pi$ for common ligands; Racah parameters; spin-orbit.
MSc: $g$-tensor from EPR; zero-field splitting; spin Hamiltonian.
PhD: ab initio LFT (AILFT); multireference CASSCF for spin--orbit; exchange coupling in dinuclear complexes.
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- Tanabe--Sugano for d$^3$ in octahedral: identify ground state and lowest transitions.
Set~B --- AOM energies for a trigonal complex; nephelauxetic $\beta$ from UV-vis data.
Projects: (simple) Tanabe--Sugano diagram for Cr$^{3+}$: spin-allowed transitions vs.\ $\Delta/B$; (complex) AILFT from CASSCF: extract $e_\sigma,e_\pi$ for [Fe(CN)$_6$]$^{3-}$.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.3 / L10: Full CI Quantum Monte Carlo (FCIQMC)}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Motivation: FCI is exact but exponentially expensive; FCIQMC (Booth \& Alavi, 2009) stochastically samples the FCI space without storing all amplitudes; (20--45~min) FCIQMC algorithm: represent $\ket{\Psi}=\sum_i c_i\ket{D_i}$ by signed walkers on Slater determinants; imaginary-time propagation $\partial_\tau c_i=-\hat{H}_{ij}c_j$; three steps per iteration: (1) spawn: walker at $D_i$ creates offspring at $D_j$ with probability $\propto|H_{ij}|$; (2) death: remove walker with probability $\propto E_S-H_{ii}$; (3) annihilation: opposite-sign walkers on same $D_i$ cancel; (45--65~min) Sign problem: positive and negative walkers must be sampled; without intervention the walk decays to a superposition; initiator approximation ($i$-FCIQMC): only ``initiator'' determinants (with $|c_i|>n_a$) can spawn to unvisited determinants; controlled sign error; (65--90~min) Semistochastic FCIQMC: deterministic subspace for the most important determinants; convergence improvement; FCIQMC benchmarks: carbon dimer (Booth 2013), chromium dimer, iron--sulfur clusters; accuracy vs.\ CCSD(T) and DMC; GPU acceleration.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Describe the FCIQMC algorithm: spawn, death, and annihilation steps.
  \item Explain the sign problem and the initiator approximation.
  \item Describe semistochastic FCIQMC and its convergence improvement.
  \item Place FCIQMC in the accuracy hierarchy vs.\ CCSD(T) and DMC.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: ``FCIQMC is a random walk that converges to the exact ground state.''
Beg.\ UG: imaginary-time propagation; walker concept; annihilation.
Adv.\ UG: sign problem; initiator approximation; error analysis.
MSc: semistochastic FCIQMC; benchmark applications; GPU acceleration.
PhD: FCIQMC for excited states; tailored-CC from FCIQMC; FCIQMC-R12.
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- FCIQMC steps for H$_2$: spawn/death probabilities; initiator threshold.
Set~B --- initiator approximation error scaling; semistochastic subspace selection criterion.
Projects: (simple) FCIQMC for H$_4$ square: energy vs.\ walker number; (complex) i-FCIQMC for N$_2$ at stretched geometry: convergence with initiator threshold.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.3 / L11: Diffusion Quantum Monte Carlo for Molecules}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Recap (from II.1 L06): DMC as imaginary-time projection; $-\partial_\tau\Psi=(\hat{H}-E_T)\Psi$; walker diffusion and branching; (20--45~min) Trial wavefunctions for molecular DMC: Slater--Jastrow $\Psi_T=\mathcal{A}[\Phi]\exp(J)$; Jastrow factor: electron--electron, electron--nuclear, three-body; cusp conditions; optimisation via VMC; fixed-node approximation: constrain walkers to nodal surface of $\Psi_T$; (45--65~min) Quality of nodes: HF nodes vs.\ CASSCF nodes for multi-reference systems; nodal bias; sign problem and fixed-node error as the main source of DMC error; (65--90~min) Pseudopotentials in DMC: non-locality problem; T-moves; Casula's locality approximation; backflow transformation; DMC for molecular energetics: benchmarks for atomisation energies, reaction barriers; comparison with CCSD(T) and FCIQMC; GPU implementation (CASINO, QMCPack, TurboRVB).

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Construct a Slater--Jastrow trial wavefunction and optimise its parameters.
  \item Explain the fixed-node approximation and identify its main sources of error.
  \item Describe T-moves for non-local pseudopotentials.
  \item Assess DMC accuracy for molecular energetics vs.\ other methods.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: DMC as ``the most accurate method for large molecules.''
Beg.\ UG: Slater--Jastrow; cusp conditions; fixed-node approximation.
Adv.\ UG: node quality from HF vs.\ CASSCF; T-moves derivation; pseudopotentials.
MSc: backflow transformation; DMC benchmarks; GPU workflow.
PhD: exact nodes from FCI; multi-determinant Jastrow; neural-network trial functions.
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- Jastrow factor construction; cusp condition for H$_2$; fixed-node energy bound.
Set~B --- T-moves derivation; fixed-node error analysis for N$_2$ at $r=2R_e$.
Projects: (simple) DMC for H$_2$: fixed-node energy vs.\ HF and CASSCF nodes; (complex) node quality study: HF vs.\ CASSCF(6,6) nodes for O$_3$ dissociation.
\end{tcolorbox}

\medskip

\begin{tcolorbox}[chembox, title={Module~III.3 / L12: Synthesis and Outlook}]
\textbf{90-min pacing:} (0--20~min) Complete method hierarchy for molecular electronic structure: HF $\to$ DFT $\to$ MP2 $\to$ CCSD $\to$ CCSD(T) $\to$ CASSCF $\to$ NEVPT2 $\to$ MRCI $\to$ FCIQMC $\to$ DMC; accuracy and cost at each level; (20--40~min) Open challenges: (1) strong correlation in transition metal and $f$-element chemistry; (2) excited states: TDDFT, EOM-CC, MR methods, quantum computing; (3) relativistic effects: scalar and spin--orbit; four-component DFT; X2C; (20--40~min continued) (4) periodic systems: DFT+U, hybrid DFT, periodic CCSD(T), stochastic CCSD(T), FCIQMC for solids; (5) large molecules and biological systems: DLPNO-CCSD(T), DFTB, ML potentials; (65--80~min) Future directions: machine learning for electronic structure (SchNet, PaiNN, DeepMind AlphaFold-like potentials); neural-network wavefunctions (DeepWF, FermiNet, PauliNet); quantum computing (VQE, QITE, QPE for fault-tolerant); (80--90~min) Synthesis: how all the methods taught in Series III fit together; choosing the right method; the promise of exact quantum simulation.

\medskip\textbf{Core learning outcomes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.4em,topsep=2pt,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Place all quantum chemistry methods in a unified accuracy--cost hierarchy.
  \item Identify the open challenges and describe current frontiers.
  \item Describe neural-network wavefunctions and their advantages.
  \item Outline the quantum computing approach to quantum chemistry.
\end{itemize}
\medskip\textbf{Tier differentiation:}
HS: from H$_2$ to drug design --- quantum chemistry shapes the modern world.
Beg.\ UG: method hierarchy; practical choice guide; exciting frontiers.
Adv.\ UG: open challenges in detail; ML potentials; VQE concept.
MSc: neural-network wavefunctions; periodic CCSD(T); relativistic DFT.
PhD: quantum complexity; resource estimation for QPE; FermiNet for correlated systems.
\medskip\textbf{Assessment:}
Set~A --- method selection for: (i) organocatalysis barrier, (ii) Mn$_4$O$_4$ cluster, (iii) singlet oxygen, (iv) protein binding energy.
Set~B --- VQE ansatz for H$_2$: UCCSD circuit; FermiNet architecture for helium.
Projects: (simple) decision-tree: method selection for 10 representative chemical problems; (complex) FermiNet energy for He and Li: variational quality vs.\ classical wavefunction ansatz.
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[highlightbox]
\textbf{Module III.3 Reading:} Koch \& Holthausen, \textit{A Chemist's Guide to DFT} (Wiley); Parr \& Yang, \textit{Density-Functional Theory of Atoms and Molecules} (Oxford); Booth, Thom \& Alavi, J.\ Chem.\ Phys.\ \textbf{131}, 054106 (2009) --- FCIQMC; Foulkes \textit{et al.}, Rev.\ Mod.\ Phys.\ \textbf{73}, 33 (2001) --- QMC review.
\end{tcolorbox}

%=============================================================
\section*{Appendix B --- Suggested Textbooks}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{Appendix B --- Suggested Textbooks}
%=============================================================

\medskip\noindent{\large\bfseries\color{midblue}Quantum Mechanics --- Foundations}\par\smallskip
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.5em]
  \item Dirac, P.A.M.\ --- \textit{The Principles of Quantum Mechanics}, 4th ed.\ (Oxford)
  \item Sakurai, J.J.\ \& Napolitano, J.\ --- \textit{Modern Quantum Mechanics}, 3rd ed.
  \item Weinberg, S.\ --- \textit{Lectures on Quantum Mechanics}, 2nd ed.
  \item Galindo, A.\ \& Pascual, P.\ --- \textit{Quantum Mechanics} (2 vols., Springer)
\end{itemize}

\medskip\noindent{\large\bfseries\color{midblue}Many-Body and Advanced Topics}\par\smallskip
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.5em]
  \item Fetter, A.L.\ \& Walecka, J.D.\ --- \textit{Quantum Theory of Many-Particle Systems}
  \item Bruus, H.\ \& Flensberg, K.\ --- \textit{Introduction to Many-Body Quantum Theory in Condensed Matter Physics}
  \item Stefanucci, G.\ \& van Leeuwen, R.\ --- \textit{Nonequilibrium Many-Body Theory of Quantum Systems} (Cambridge)
  \item Negele, J.W.\ \& Orland, H.\ --- \textit{Quantum Many-Particle Systems}
\end{itemize}

\medskip\noindent{\large\bfseries\color{midblue}Quantum Chemistry and Electronic Structure}\par\smallskip
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.5em]
  \item Szabo, A.\ \& Ostlund, N.S.\ --- \textit{Modern Quantum Chemistry}
  \item Helgaker, T., Jorgensen, P.\ \& Olsen, J.\ --- \textit{Molecular Electronic-Structure Theory} (Wiley)
  \item Jensen, F.\ --- \textit{Introduction to Computational Chemistry}, 3rd ed.
  \item Koch, W.\ \& Holthausen, M.C.\ --- \textit{A Chemist's Guide to Density Functional Theory}
  \item Martin, R.M., Reining, L.\ \& Ceperley, D.\ --- \textit{Interacting Electrons} (Cambridge)
\end{itemize}
